Talbiyah Required for Ihram: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
States ruling that talbiyah is essential for ihram, with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement of talbiyah for ihram and explain the thamarah al-khilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on this issue.

Core Idea
In ihram, intention alone is insufficient; Hanafi school mandates vocal talbiyah for validity.

This lesson addresses a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: is uttering the talbiyah necessary for entering the state of ihram, or is mere intention enough? The Hanafi position, rooted in the Prophet's ﷺ practice, requires talbiyah; the Shafi'i school considers intention sufficient. Understanding this dispute clarifies the practical consequences for anyone assuming ihram.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school requires the utterance of talbiyah for ihram to be valid. Mere intention is insufficient.
2
Identify the opposing school's view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that intention alone is sufficient for ihram. Talbiyah is recommended, not required.
3
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a person who intends ihram but does not recite talbiyah has a valid ihram according to Shafi'i but invalid according to Hanafi.
This affects the validity of subsequent Hajj or Umrah acts.
4
Note the additional ruling
The passage also prohibits a muhrim from pointing towards game or guiding others to it, as this facilitates hunting which is forbidden during ihram.
This is separate from the talbiyah requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإحرام بغير تلبیۃ صرف نیت احرام کے لئے کافی نہیں، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر نیت کافی ہے۔ محرم شکاری طرف اشارہ اور راہنمائی بھی نہ کرے۔
Chapter of Ihram: Without talbiyah, mere intention is not sufficient for ihram. Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint: intention is sufficient. A muhrim should not point towards game nor guide [others] to it.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the conditions of entering ihram. It states that uttering the talbiyah (لبيك اللهم...) is necessary; mere intention (niyyah) without vocalizing the talbiyah does not constitute ihram according to Abu Hanifa and his students. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that intention alone suffices, as he considers niyyah to be the essence of worship. The Hanafi position is based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ who always combined intention with talbiyah. Additionally, the passage notes that the muhrim must not point towards game or guide others to it, as this would facilitate hunting during ihram, which is prohibited.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited to enter ihram.
نیت (niyyah): Intention; in ihram, it is the resolve to perform Hajj or Umrah.
احرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, involving specific prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for ihram in addition to niyyah?
A) Ghusl
B) Talbiyah
C) Wearing two sheets
D) Tawaf

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, utterance of talbiyah is an essential condition for the validity of ihram; mere intention is insufficient.

Prohibitions of Ihram: Sewn Garments, Perfume, and Head Covering
Lists prohibited acts for a muhrim regarding dress and perfume

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibited actions for a man in ihram regarding clothing, perfume, and covering the head and face, and identify the Hanafi ruling on colored cloth.

Core Idea
In ihram, a man must abandon all sewn garments, coverings of head/face, and perfume — these are forbidden acts that require a penalty.

The state of ihram is marked by a set of prohibitions that distinguish the pilgrim's conduct from ordinary life. This lesson focuses specifically on the rulings related to clothing and perfume for men, as outlined in the Hanafi school. Understanding these prohibitions is essential for performing Hajj or Umrah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify prohibited garments
Note the specific sewn garments mentioned: qurtah (shirt), pajamah (trousers), imamah (turban), and mawzah (socks). These are all forbidden for a man in ihram.
Only unsewn white wraps (izar and rida) are permitted.
2
Understand head and face covering
The term 'cherah' (face) and 'sar' (head) indicate that both must remain uncovered for men. Covering them deliberately incurs a penalty (dam).
Women may cover their face with a cloth that does not touch the skin, but not with a sewn veil.
3
Recognize perfume and hair cutting prohibition
Applying perfume to the body or clothing, and cutting hair or nails are also prohibited. These acts break the state of ihram and require compensation.
These apply to both men and women.
4
Consider colored cloth ruling
The passage mentions 'ranga hua kapda' (colored cloth). The Hanafi view is that wearing colored unsewn cloth is permissible as long as it is not perfumed, though white is preferred.
Colored sewn garments remain prohibited.
5
Note Shafi'i viewpoint
The mention of Imam Shafi'i signals an ikhtilaf: Shafi'i permits wearing sewn garments if necessary with a fidyah, while Hanafi forbids them absolutely.
This is a legitimate difference; the Hanafi position is stricter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حالت احرام میں کرتہ، پانجامہ، عمامہ، موزے پہننے ممنوع ہیں۔ چیرہ اور سر نہ ڈھانپے۔ امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر۔ محرم کے لئے خوشبو لگانا اور بال کا شنا ممنوع ہے۔ رنگا ہوا کپڑا پہنے کا حکم۔
During ihram, wearing shirt, trousers, turban, and socks is prohibited. Do not cover the face and head. Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint. For a muhrim, applying perfume and cutting hair is prohibited. Ruling on wearing colored cloth.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage outlines key prohibitions for a person in the state of ihram, focusing on men. Sewn garments (like shirts and trousers) are not allowed; instead two unsewn white sheets (izar and rida) are worn. Covering the head and face is prohibited for men. The mention of Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint indicates that there might be differences—for example, Shafi'i permits wearing sewn garments if necessary with a fidyah compensation. Additionally, applying perfume and cutting hair or nails are prohibited (these are acts that break ihram). Colored cloth may be permissible as long as it is not perfumed, but the preferred practice is to wear white unsewn garments.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
إحرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, marked by specific prohibitions.
فدية (fidyah): Compensation (usually slaughter of an animal) for violating certain ihram prohibitions, typically required by Shafi'i school.
دم (dam): Penalty of sacrificing a sheep for each prohibited act committed in ihram, according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is prohibited for a man in ihram?
A) Wearing a turban
B) Wearing sandals
C) Drinking water
D) Sleeping

Key Takeaway
A man in ihram must avoid all sewn garments, covering his head and face, applying perfume, and cutting hair; these are prohibited acts requiring a penalty.

Rulings on Combining Hajj and Umrah (Qiran and Beyond)
Rulings on combining Hajj and Umrah in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for various sequences of Hajj and Umrah ihrams and identify when a dam (sacrifice) is wajib.

Core Idea
When Umrah ihram precedes Hajj ihram, the Hajj is abandoned; when Hajj ihram precedes, both are obligatory with a dam.

This passage presents a series of scenarios involving combining Hajj and Umrah in a single journey. The rulings depend on the order of ihrams and what actions have been completed. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correct practice and avoiding unnecessary penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of ihrams
Determine which act (Hajj or Umrah) was entered first, and whether any actions of the first were performed before the second ihram.
The order matters: Umrah first vs. Hajj first yield different rulings.
2
Apply the rule for Umrah-first scenarios
If Umrah ihram was first and no Umrah actions are done, the Hajj is abandoned. Even if four circuits of tawaf were done, the same ruling applies.
The text explicitly says 'leave Hajj without dispute'.
3
Apply the rule for Hajj-first scenarios
If Hajj ihram was first and then Umrah ihram, both are obligatory and a single dam is due for combining, unless the Hajj was already completed (shaved) before the second Hajj ihram.
There is a difference of Imams regarding the shaving scenario.
4
Check for exceptions and penalties
A resident of Makkah (Makki) who performs both is covered. If Umrah is abandoned after ihram, a dam is wajib and one Umrah must be made up. If Hajj is missed, the later ihram is maintained and the other is abandoned.
The text also covers Umrah during Tashriq days and the Afaqi scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حج اور عمرہ لازم ہے
جب عمرہ کا احرام باندھا پھر حج کا احرام باندھا اور عمرہ کے افعال سے کچھ نہیں کیا اور اگر عمرہ کے طواف کے چار چکر کاٹے پھر حج کا احرام باندھ بلا خلاف حج کو چھوڑ دے اگر مکی نے دونوں کو کر لیا دونوں سے کفایت کر جائے گا
جس نے حج کا احرام باندھا پھر یوم النحر کو دوسرے حج کا احرام باندھا اگر پہلے میں حلق کیا دوسرا لا زم ہوگا اور اس پر کچھ لا زم نہیں اور اگر پہلے میں حلق نہیں کیا دوسرا لا زم ہے اس پر دم ہے قصر کیا ہو یا نہیں ، اختلاف ائمہ
جو عمرہ سے فارغ ہوا سوائے قصر کے پھر دوسرے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اس پر دم واجب ہے آفاقی نے حج کا احرام باندھا پھر عمرہ کا احرام باندھا تو دونوں لازم ہوں گے
اگر حج کا طواف کیا پھر عمرہ کا احرام باندھا پھر ان دونوں کو کر گذرا دونوں لازم ہیں اس پر ایک دم ہے جمع کرنے کی وجہ سے حج کے احترام کی وجہ سے عمرہ کا احترام چھوڑ دے جس نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا یوم النحر میں یا ایام تشریق میں اس پر عمرہ لازم ہے
عمرہ چھوڑ دیا تو اس پر عمرہ چھوڑنے کی قربانی اور اس کی جگہ ایک عمرہ واجب ہے حج فوت ہو گیا پھر عمرہ یا حج کا احرام باندھا تو دوسرے کو ترک کر دے حج فوت ہونے کے بعد دوسرے حج کا احرام باندھا تو احرام میں دونج جمع کرنے والا ہوگا
Hajj and Umrah are obligatory. When one dons ihram for Umrah then dons ihram for Hajj and does not perform any actions of Umrah, and if one performed four circuits of tawaf for Umrah then dons ihram for Hajj, he should leave Hajj without dispute. If a resident of Makkah performs both, both will suffice. One who dons ihram for Hajj then on the Day of Nahr dons ihram for another Hajj: if he shaved in the first, the second becomes obligatory and nothing is upon him; if he did not shave, the second is obligatory and a dam is upon him whether he trimmed or not – difference of Imams. One who completed Umrah except trimming then dons ihram for another Umrah, a dam is wajib upon him. An Afaqi dons ihram for Hajj then dons ihram for Umrah, then both are obligatory. If one performed tawaf for Hajj then dons ihram for Umrah then performs both, both are obligatory and one dam is upon him due to combining; due to the honor of Hajj he abandons the honor of Umrah. One who dons ihram for Umrah on the Day of Nahr or the Days of Tashriq, Umrah is obligatory upon him. If he abandons Umrah, then upon him is a sacrifice for abandoning Umrah and in its place one Umrah is wajib. If Hajj is missed then dons ihram for Umrah or Hajj, he should abandon the other. After missing Hajj, he dons ihram for another Hajj, then he will be one who combines two in ihram.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings on combining Hajj and Umrah in ihram. The Hanafi school holds that if one dons ihram for Umrah and then for Hajj before performing any Umrah actions, the Hajj overrides and the Umrah is abandoned without penalty. However, if one has performed four circuits of Umrah tawaf, then the Hajj is abandoned (contradictory? Possibly means one must continue Umrah). The text also discusses a Makki (resident of Makkah) performing both – they suffice. For someone who dons ihram for Hajj and then another on the Day of Nahr, if he has already shaved (i.e., completed the first), the second is obligatory but no penalty; otherwise, a dam is required. This is an intra-madhhab difference (اختلاف ائمہ). Other scenarios involve combining two Umrahs, an Afaqi combining Hajj and Umrah, and the prohibition of Umrah during certain days. The overall principle is that combining acts can incur a dam, and missed obligations must be compensated.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal required as expiation for certain violations or omissions during Hajj/Umrah.
قارن (qarin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah together in a single ihram (qiran).
آفاقی (afaqi): A person who comes from outside the Miqat (the boundary for entering the state of ihram).
مکی (makki): A resident of Makkah (or within the Miqat boundaries).
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely, an act of completing Hajj/Umrah.
قصر (qasr): Trimming the hair, an alternative to shaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if an Afaqi (person from outside Miqat) dons ihram for Hajj first, then later dons ihram for Umrah, what is the ruling?
A) The Hajj is abandoned
B) The Umrah is abandoned
C) Both are obligatory and one dam is due
D) Both are obligatory but no dam is due

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rulings on combining Hajj and Umrah depend on the order of ihrams and the extent of actions completed; in most cases, combining incurs a wajib dam, but when Umrah precedes Hajj without any Umrah actions, the Hajj is abandoned without penalty.

Rulings on Ihsaar – Exiting Ihram by Sending a Sacrifice
Rulings on the prevented pilgrim and the requirement to send a sacrifice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the muhsar's exit from ihram and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A prevented pilgrim may exit ihram by sending a sacrifice to the Haram – the disagreement is over the location of slaughter.

This passage from Bab al-Ihsaar addresses a critical scenario: what happens when someone in ihram is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to enemy or illness. The Hanafi school permits exiting ihram by sending a sacrificial animal to be slaughtered in the Haram. This ruling differs from Imam al-Shafi'i's view, leading to practical consequences in how and where the sacrifice is performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of ihsar
Recognize that a muhsar is a muhrim prevented from completing Hajj/Umrah due to enemy, illness, or similar. The prevention occurs before wuquf at Arafah.
If the pilgrim has already done wuquf, he is not considered muhsar.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi school rules that the muhsar may become halal (exit ihram) by sending a sacrificial animal (dam) to be slaughtered in the Haram. Sending the dam is wajib.
A qarin must send two dams.
3
Note the Shafi'i opposition
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the sacrifice must be slaughtered at the place where one was prevented, not in the Haram.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi can send money or an animal from afar, while a Shafi'i must sacrifice locally (or at the place of prevention).
5
Apply to a scenario
If a qarin is prevented, he must send two dams. If the prevention lifts, he must proceed if possible; otherwise, he may become halal with the already sent dam.
Refer to the various sub-scenarios in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإحصار
محرم دشمن یا مرض کی وجہ سے مصر ہو جائے اور جانے سے رک جائے تو اس کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
محصر کے لئے حلال ہونے کی صورت
قارن دودم بھیجے
دم احصار کو حرم میں ہی ذبح کرنا لازم ہے اور یوم النحر سے پہلے ذبح کرنا بھی جائز ہے
محصر بانچ جب ہلال ہو جائے تو اس پر حج اور عمر و لا زم ہے محصر بالعمرہ پر عمرہ کی قضا ہے، عمرہ میں احسار تحقیق ہوتا ہے یا نہیں
قارن پر حج اور دوعمرے ہیں
اگر قارن نے بدن کو بھیجا اور ان سے وعدہ لیا کہ اس کو معین دن ذبیح کریں پھر احصار زائل ہو گیا اب اگر ہدی اور حج کو نہ پاسکتا ہو تو توجہ لازم نہیں ہے اگر حج اور بدی پالے تو اسپر توجہ لازم ہے اگر بدی کو پالے جو چاہے اس کے ساتھ کرے
دس کو پا سکے نہ کہ حج کو تو حلال ہو جائے
حج کو پالے نہ کہ ہدی کو اس کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے جس نے وقوف عرفہ کر لیا پھر مصر ہوا محصر شمار نہ ہوگا
Chapter of Prevention. A Muhrim who is prevented due to enemy or illness and is stopped from going, it is permissible for him to become halal (exit ihram). [With] Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint. The manner of becoming halal for a muhsar. A Qarin sends two dams. It is necessary to slaughter the dam of ihsar in the Haram, and it is permissible to slaughter before the Day of Nahr. A muhsar, when he becomes halal, then Hajj and Umrah are obligatory upon him. A muhsar bi'l-umrah has to make up the Umrah. Does ihsar actually occur in Umrah? Upon a Qarin are Hajj and two Umrahs. If a Qarin sent sacrificial animals and made a promise with them to slaughter them on a specific day, then the prevention is removed, then if he cannot reach the hady and Hajj, then proceeding is not necessary. If he can reach Hajj and hady, then proceeding is necessary. If he can reach the hady but not Hajj, he may do whatever he wishes with it. If he can reach the ten [days?] but not Hajj, then he becomes halal. If he can reach Hajj but not the hady, it is permissible for him to become halal. One who performed wuquf at Arafah then was prevented, he is not counted as a muhsar.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This is the chapter on Ihsaar (prevention). The Hanafi position is that a muhrim who is prevented from continuing Hajj or Umrah due to an enemy or illness may exit ihram by sending a sacrificial animal (dam) to be slaughtered in the Haram. Imam Shafi'i holds a different view (possibly requiring sacrifice at the place of prevention). The text details various scenarios: a Qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) must send two dams; the dam must be slaughtered in the Haram and may be before the Day of Nahr. Once the muhsar exits ihram, he is obligated to make up the Hajj and Umrah later. There is a question whether ihsar (prevention) applies to Umrah – the Hanafi answer is yes. Additional scenarios involve a Qarin who sent animals but then the prevention is lifted; the ruling depends on whether he can still reach the sacrifice and the Hajj. If he can reach the sacrifice but not Hajj, he may do as he wishes with the animal. If he performed wuquf at Arafah before being prevented, he is not considered a muhsar (i.e., his Hajj is valid).

Key Terms
محصر (muhsar): A person in ihram who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to enemy, illness, or other valid hindrance.
احصار (ihsar): The state of being prevented from completing Hajj/Umrah after entering ihram.
قارن (qarin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram (qiran).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, where must the dam of ihsar be slaughtered?
A) At the place where one was prevented
B) In the Haram (Mecca)
C) At the nearest mosque
D) Anywhere in the Arabian Peninsula

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows the prevented pilgrim to exit ihram by sending a sacrifice to the Haram, with a later obligation to make up the missed pilgrimage.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner

Missing the Standing at Arafah: Fawaat in Hajj
Ruling on one who misses the standing at Arafah and thus Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on missing wuquf of Arafah and explain the consequence for the pilgrim's Hajj and Umrah.

Core Idea
Missing wuquf of Arafah invalidates Hajj; Umrah is never missed and can be done any time.

This passage from the Hidayah introduces the chapter on Fawaat—when a pilgrim misses the essential standing at Arafah. The key distinction is that Hajj becomes faa'it (missed), but Umrah does not. Understanding this ruling clarifies the difference in legal treatment between Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The pilgrim dons ihram for Hajj but misses wuquf of Arafah until dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Nahr).
Wuquf is the essential standing at Arafah on the 9th; its time ends at dawn of the 10th.
2
State the ruling for Hajj
The Hajj is considered faa'it (missed). The pilgrim must exit ihram by performing Umrah and will need to make up the Hajj in a future year.
Missing wuquf invalidates the Hajj because wuquf is a rukn.
3
State the ruling for Umrah
Umrah is not subject to fawat; it can be performed any day of the year except five prohibited days (Day of Arafah and the three days of Tashriq).
Hanafi school: Umrah is sunnah mu'akkadah, not obligatory like Hajj.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds Umrah to be wajib at least once in a lifetime, while the Hanafi school considers it sunnah mu'akkadah.
This difference affects the consequences for one who misses Hajj and the importance of performing Umrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الفوات
جس نے حج کا احرام باندھا اور وقوف عرفہ فوت ہو گیا حتی کہ یوم النحر کی صبح طلوع ہو گئی اس کا حج فوت ہو گیا عمرہ فوت نہیں ہوتا، عمرہ پورے سال جائز ہے سوائے پانچ ایام کے عمرہ کی شرعی حیثیت ، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
Chapter of Missing. One who dons ihram for Hajj and misses wuquf of Arafah until the morning of the Day of Nahr rises, his Hajj is missed. Umrah is not missed; Umrah is permissible throughout the year except five days. The legal status of Umrah, Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This is the chapter on Fawaat (missing the Hajj). The key ruling: if a person enters ihram for Hajj but fails to perform wuquf at Arafah before dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the Hajj is considered missed (faa'it). He must then exit ihram and perform Umrah instead, and later make up the Hajj. Umrah, in contrast, is not subject to a specific time and can be performed any day of the year except five days (the Day of Arafah and the three days of Tashriq according to some views). The text also notes a difference with Imam Shafi'i regarding the legal status of Umrah – Shafi'i considers Umrah as obligatory at least once in a lifetime, while Hanafi considers it a highly recommended sunnah.

Key Terms
فوت (fawat): The state of having missed the time for Hajj (wuquf of Arafah).
وقوف عرفہ (wuquf Arafah): The essential standing at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; missing it invalidates the Hajj.
عمرہ (Umrah): The lesser pilgrimage, consisting of ihram, tawaf, sa'yi, and halq/taqsir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What event causes Hajj to be considered 'faa'it' (missed) according to this passage?
A) Not completing tawaf al-ifadah
B) Missing wuquf at Arafah until dawn of 10th Dhul Hijjah
C) Not stoning the Jamarat
D) Leaving Mina before sunset

Key Takeaway
Missing wuquf of Arafah before dawn of 10th Dhul Hijjah invalidates the Hajj; Umrah is never subject to fawat.

Hajj on Behalf of Others: General Rule and Two Clients
Rulings on Hajj niyabah: general permissibility and the two-client case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a single talbiyah is recited on behalf of two principals and identify the consequences for the agent.

Core Idea
A single talbiyah on behalf of two counts only for the agent himself, who then guarantees the expenses.

The chapter on performing Hajj for others begins with a general principle: one may transfer the reward of an act to another. The first specific case involves an agent hired by two clients who recites a single talbiyah. This lesson examines that ruling, which protects the integrity of the intention (niyyah) in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its permissibility
Recognize the general rule: a person can intend the reward of his action for another. This applies to Hajj on behalf of someone else (niyabah).
Hanafi school permits niyabah only for Hajj, not for prayers or fasting.
2
Analyze the two-client scenario
Two people each instruct the agent to perform Hajj for them. The agent recites one talbiyah for both. Determine the legal effect.
3
Apply the ruling: Hajj is for the agent
The single talbiyah cannot represent two distinct intentions. Therefore, the Hajj is valid for the agent himself, not for the clients.
The agent’s own Hajj is fulfilled.
4
Examine the expense guarantee
If the agent spent the clients' money, he must guarantee the expenses (i.e., repay them). If he spent his own, no guarantee is needed.
The guarantee applies only when spending from the clients' wealth.
5
Consider unspecified intention
If the agent enters ihram with an unspecified intention (not naming any client), he is considered to be opposing the clients. The Hajj is still valid for him.
This highlights the importance of a clear intention (ta'yin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الحج عن الغير
انسان اپنے عمل کا ثواب کسی دوسرے کے لئے کرنا چاہے تو کر سکتا ہے
شخص کو دو شخصوں نے حکم کیا کہ وہ ہر ایک کی طرف سے حج ادا کرے اس نے دونوں کی طرف سے ایک حج کا تلبیہ کہا تو یہ حج اس ایک حاجی نائب کی طرف سے ہوگا اور یہ نفقہ کا ضامن ہوگا
نفقہ کا ضامن ہو گا بشرطیکہ دونوں موکلوں کے مال سے خرچ کیا ہو
احرام بہم باندھا کہ ایک غیر معین کی طرف سے نیت کی اور اس مہم نیت سے افعال حج ادا کر لئے تو یہ موکلوں کی مخالفت کرنے والا ہے
اگر غیر نے امر کیا کہ اس کی طرف سے قرآن کیا جائے تو دم قرآن وکیل پر واجب ہے
کسی عاجز نے حکم دیا کہ اس کی طرف سے حج ادا کیا جائے اور دوسرے نے کہا کہ اس کی طرف سے عمرہ کیا جائے دونوں نے قران کی اجازت دی تو دم قیر ان وکیل پر ہوگا
دم احصار امر پر ہے اگر میت کی طرف سے حج کر رہا تھا پھر مصر ہو گیا تو دم میت کے مال میں ہے
جماع کا دم حاجی پر ہے
جس نے حج کی وصیت کی ورثہ نے ایک آدمی کو حج کے لئے بھیجاوہ راستے میں فوت ہو گیا یا اس کا نفقہ چوری ہو گیا اور اس نے نصف کو خرچ کر دیا اب نائب ثانی کو سفر حج کا خرچ کس مال سے دیا جائے اور سفر کہاں سے شروع کرے۔ اختلاف ائمہ
جس نے اپنے والدین کی طرف سے حج کا تلبیہ کہا اسے جائز ہے کہ وہ حج کو کسی ایک کی طرف سے کر دے
Chapter of Hajj on Behalf of Others. A person can intend the reward of his action for another. A person was instructed by two persons to perform Hajj on behalf of each. He recited talbiyah for one Hajj on behalf of both. This Hajj will be on behalf of the one agent (nayib) and he will be the guarantor of the expenses. He will be guarantor of expenses provided he spent from the wealth of both clients. He donned ihram with the intention for an unspecified person and performed the actions of Hajj with this unspecified intention, then he is opposing the clients. If another person commanded that qiran be performed on his behalf, then the dam of qiran is wajib upon the agent. A weak person commanded that Hajj be performed on his behalf, and another said Umrah be performed on his behalf, and both allowed qiran, then the dam of qiran is upon the agent. The dam of ihsar is upon the one who commanded; if he was performing Hajj on behalf of a deceased and then was prevented, the dam is from the wealth of the deceased. The dam of intercourse is upon the pilgrim. One who made a will for Hajj, the heirs sent a man for Hajj, he died on the way or his expenses were stolen and he spent half, now where should the second agent's travel expenses be given from and from where should he begin the journey? Difference of Imams. One who recited talbiyah for Hajj on behalf of his parents, it is permissible for him to perform the Hajj on behalf of one of them.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This chapter deals with performing Hajj (or Umrah) on behalf of another person (niyabah). The Hanafi ruling: one may intend the reward of one's own voluntary actions for another, but for obligatory acts like Hajj, permission is needed if the person is alive and capable. The text presents several specific cases: if two people appoint an agent to perform Hajj for each, and the agent recites one talbiyah for both, the Hajj counts for the agent himself (not the clients) and he must guarantee the expenses. If he spends from the clients' wealth, he guarantees the expenses. If he makes an unspecified intention, he opposes the clients. If someone is hired to perform qiran (combined Hajj/Umrah), the dam for qiran is on the agent. If two clients each ask for different types (Hajj and Umrah) but both permit qiran, the agent's qiran dam is on him. If the agent is performing on behalf of a deceased and is prevented (ihsar), the dam is from the deceased's estate. If the pilgrim commits sexual intercourse, the dam is on him personally. For a Hajj bequest: if the first agent dies or loses the money, the second agent's expenses and starting point are disputed among Imams. Finally, if one recites talbiyah for both parents, he may choose to apply the Hajj to one of them.

Key Terms
نائب (na'ib): An agent appointed to perform Hajj or Umrah on behalf of another.
دم (dam): Sacrificial animal due for violations; in this context, for qiran or ihsar.
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The formula 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited upon entering ihram, establishing the intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An agent is hired by two people to perform Hajj for each. He recites one talbiyah for both. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The Hajj is valid for both clients equally.
B) The Hajj is valid for the agent himself, and he must guarantee expenses if he spent the clients' money.
C) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
D) The Hajj counts for the first client mentioned.

Key Takeaway
The talbiyah determines the beneficiary; a single talbiyah cannot cover two principals.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Liability for Dams When Performing Hajj on Behalf of Others
Rulings on dam liability for qiran, ihsar, and intercourse in Hajj niyabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify who bears the dam for qiran, ihsar, and intercourse when performing Hajj on behalf of another.

Core Idea
The agent bears the dam for qiran unless the principal is deceased; the dam for intercourse always falls on the pilgrim.

Performing Hajj on behalf of another can involve additional obligations, such as sacrificing a dam (animal) for certain actions. This lesson covers three common scenarios: qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah), ihsar (being prevented from completing Hajj), and sexual intercourse while in ihram. Each has different rules regarding who must pay the dam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of dam
Recognize that the passage discusses three distinct causes: qiran, ihsar, and intercourse. Each has its own ruling.
2
Analyze qiran dam
If the principal commands the agent to perform qiran (combined Hajj and Umrah), the dam for qiran is wajib upon the agent (vakil).
This is because the agent choose the type of ihram.
3
Examine ihsar dam
If the agent is prevented (ihsar) from completing Hajj, the dam is upon the one who commanded (amir) – i.e., the principal. But if the agent is performing on behalf of a deceased person, the dam is taken from the deceased's estate.
Differentiate between living and deceased principal.
4
Examine intercourse dam
If the pilgrim (whether agent or principal) commits sexual intercourse during ihram, the dam is upon the pilgrim personally, regardless of agency.
This is a personal sin and cannot be transferred.

Source Text

Issues in Hajj Bequest and Performing for Parents
Rulings on Hajj bequest and performing for parents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the rules for a second agent in a Hajj bequest and the option to apply a talbiyah to one parent when recited for both.

Core Idea
If the first agent dies, the second agent's expenses come from the original bequest; a talbiyah for both parents may be applied to one.

This lesson covers two further sub-topics: the proper procedure when a bequest (wasiyyah) for Hajj is executed but the hired agent dies or loses the money, and the permissibility of dedicating a talbiyah to one parent when the agent had originally recited it for both. These rulings highlight the importance of precise planning in Hajj bequests.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the bequest scenario
A person makes a will (wasiyyah) for Hajj to be performed on his behalf. The heirs send an agent who either dies on the way or loses the funds. A second agent must be sent.
2
Determine source of expenses for second agent
The passage asks: from which wealth should the second agent's travel expenses be given, and where should he start his journey? This is a point of ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams.
The text does not give a single answer; it notes the difference.
3
Examine the parent case
If an agent recites talbiyah for Hajj on behalf of both parents, it is permissible for him to perform the Hajj on behalf of one of them (whichever he chooses).
This is a relaxation (rukhsah) because the intention can be clarified before the actual Hajj.

Source Text

Rules for Hady (Sacrificial Animals)
Rules for sacrificial animals during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid hady animal and apply the rule that one goat suffices for only one offense.

Core Idea
One goat covers one jinayah in hady; two offenses require two animals.

This lesson covers the essential fiqh of hady – the sacrificial animal offered during Hajj. We learn which animals are valid, how many are needed for offenses, and from which types of hady it is permissible to eat. Understanding these rules is crucial for a valid Hajj and for avoiding additional expiations.

Guided Path
1
Identify valid animals
First, note that the animals valid for hady are the same as for udhiyah (Eid sacrifice). This includes sheep, goats, cows, and camels meeting age requirements.
The exact conditions (like age, health) are covered elsewhere but are identical for both.
2
Understand coverage of offenses
A single goat (or sheep) suffices as expiation for one jinayah (offense committed during ihram). However, it does NOT cover two offenses - you would need two animals or one larger animal? The text specifies goat does not suffice for two.
The exact rule: for multiple offenses, the number of animals must equal the number of offenses.
3
Distinguish types of hady
Recognize that 'badal tatawwu'' refers to voluntary compensatory sacrifice, 'tamattu'' and 'qiran' are specific Hajj types. The ruling on eating the meat differs: it is permissible (ja'iz) to eat from the first three, but mustahab (recommended) to eat from general hady.
General hady includes wajib offerings; the recommendation to eat is for non-obligatory ones? The text implies mustahab for all hady.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہدی کا ادنی درجہ ہدی کی اقسام
باب الهدي
ہدایا میں وہی جانور درست ہیں جو ضحایا میں درست ہیں بکری ہر جنایت سے کافی ہے مگر دو جنایتوں میں کافی نہیں بدی تطوع تمتع اور قرآن سے کھانا جائز ہے ہدایا سے کھانا مستحب ہے
The lowest level of Hady, types of Hady. Chapter of Hady. In hadaya, the same animals are valid as in dahaya. A goat suffices for every offense except two offenses it does not suffice. It is permissible to eat from badal tatawwu', tamattu', and qiran; it is mustahab to eat from hadaya.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This is the chapter on Hady (sacrificial animals offered in the Haram during Hajj). The Hanafi ruling: the animals valid for Hady are the same as those for Udhiyah (sacrifice on Eid al-Adha) – sheep, goats, cows, and camels, with minimum age requirements. A goat (or sheep) is sufficient as expiation for a single offense (e.g., violating an ihram prohibition or compensating for a missed wajib). However, if someone has committed two offenses, one goat does not cover both; he must provide two animals or a larger animal. The text also distinguishes between different types of Hady: badal (compensatory), tatawwu' (voluntary), tamattu' (offered by one performing tamattu'), and qiran (for qiran). It is permissible to eat from the meat of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran sacrifices, but it is mustahab (recommended) to eat from the Hady (generally).

Key Terms
ہدی (hady): A sacrificial animal offered in the Haram (Mecca) as part of Hajj or as expiation.
ضحایا (dahaya): Plural of udhiyah; animals sacrificed on Eid al-Adha.
جنایت (jinayah): An offense or violation during ihram that requires expiation (dam).

Hajj on Behalf of Two Persons with One Talbiyah: Ruling and Liability
Ruling on performing one hajj for two principals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a deputy performs one hajj for two principals and identify the financial liability.

Core Idea
One talbiyah for two principals: valid for one, deputy liable for expenses from both.

This passage addresses a scenario where a deputy (na'ib) is appointed by two persons to perform Hajj on their behalf. If the deputy recites talbiyah with intention for both principals in a single Hajj, the Hajj is valid for only one of them. Additionally, if the deputy spent from the wealth of both principals, he becomes a guarantor (damin) for those expenses. This ruling underscores the principle that a single act cannot be intended for two separate individuals simultaneously, and misallocation of funds incurs liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two principals appoint a single deputy to perform Hajj on behalf of each. The deputy intends to perform one Hajj for both.
2
Note the deputy's action
The deputy recites talbiyah (the proclamation of ihram) for both principals together for one Hajj.
Talbiyah signifies the intention and type of pilgrimage.
3
Apply the ruling on validity
The Hajj is valid for only one principal. It cannot count for both simultaneously.
The text states: 'this Hajj will be on behalf of one pilgrim.'
4
Determine the financial consequence
The deputy becomes a guarantor (damin) for the expenses if he spent from the money of both principals.
Liability arises because the deputy used funds from both without proper allocation.
5
Understand the principle
The ruling is based on the principle that a single act of worship cannot be performed for two separate individuals at once. The deputy must have intended a specific principal.
This prevents sharing of reward or responsibility in a single physical act.

Source Text

Chapter of Hajj on Behalf of Others: A person can dedicate the reward of his action to someone else if he wishes. A person ordered by two persons that he perform Hajj on behalf of each; he recited talbiyah for both for one Hajj, then this Hajj will be on behalf of one pilgrim, and he will be guarantor for the expenses. He will be guarantor for expenses provided that he spent from the wealth of both principals.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This is a ruling regarding a deputy (na'ib) appointed by two persons to perform hajj on their behalf. If the deputy recites talbiyah with the intention of both, the hajj is valid for only one of them (the one he intended first or the one designated? The text says 'one pilgrim' meaning it counts for one principal). The deputy is responsible for the expenses (nafaqa) and must ensure he spends from the money of both principals. This ruling is based on the principle that a single act cannot be performed for two different persons simultaneously. The deputy must intend a specific principal at the time of talbiyah.

Key Terms
نائب (na'ib): A deputy appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another person who is unable to perform it themselves.
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The proclamation 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk' recited upon entering ihram, which signifies intention.
ضامن (damin): Guarantor; liable to pay damages from his own wealth if he acts improperly.

Timing for Slaughtering Hadi: Restricted Categories
Ruling on timing of slaughter for different hadi types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which three categories of hadi must be slaughtered on Yawm al-Nahr and explain the Hanafi-Shafi'i difference on timing.

Core Idea
Three categories of hadi are restricted to Yawm al-Nahr; all others may be slaughtered any time.

This lesson focuses on a precise Hanafi ruling about when different types of sacrificial animals (hadi) must be slaughtered during Hajj. The passage distinguishes between restricted and unrestricted categories, and also hints at a well-known difference with the Shafi'i school. Understanding this classification helps ensure that the hadi fulfills its wajib requirement correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the restricted categories
List the three types of hadi that must be slaughtered on Yawm al-Nahr: hadi tatawwu' (voluntary), hadi tamattu', and hadi qiran.
These are the only ones with a fixed timing according to Hanafi fiqh.
2
Distinguish unrestricted hadi
Note that all other types of hadi, such as those for penalty (jinanat) or due to vows (nazr), may be slaughtered at any time.
The text says 'the remaining hadi' are free in timing.
3
Recognize the madhhab difference
The passage mentions 'Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint'. In the Shafi'i school, even the restricted categories may be slaughtered on any of the days of tashriq (11th-13th), not only Yawm al-Nahr.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
4
Note the consequence of missing the time
According to the Hanafi school, if one intentionally delays the slaughter of a restricted hadi beyond Yawm al-Nahr, the act is still valid but a penalty (dam) becomes wajib. This is derived from general Hanafi rules, though not explicit in the text.
This step supplements the text with standard Hanafi principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہدی تطوع تمتع اور قرآن کو یوم النحر میں ہی ذبح کیا جائے باقی ہدایا کو جس وقت میں چاہے ذبح کرے امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
The hadi of voluntary (tatawwu'), tamattu', and qiran should only be slaughtered on the Day of Sacrifice. The remaining hadi may be slaughtered whenever one wishes. The viewpoint of Imam Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage clarifies the timing of slaughter for different categories of hadi (sacrificial animals in Hajj). According to the Hanafi school, hadi that is voluntary (nafl), or due to tamattu' or qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah) must be slaughtered specifically on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). Other types of hadi, such as those for penalty (jinanat) or vows (nazr), can be slaughtered any time. The mention of Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint suggests a difference: Shafi'i allows slaughter of all hadi on any day of the Hajj days (10th-13th) according to his school.

Key Terms
ہدی تطوع (hadi tatawwu'): A voluntary sacrificial animal offered during Hajj without being obligatory.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first, then Hajj in the same year with a break in between, requiring a hadi.
قرآن (qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah with one ihram, also requiring a hadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the hadi of tatawwu', tamattu', and qiran are restricted to slaughter on Yawm al-Nahr; other hadi are unrestricted in timing, and the Shafi'i school extends the period to the days of tashriq.

Definition and Obligation of Hajj
Defines hajj lexically and technically, discusses when it became obligatory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and technical definitions of hajj and identify the Qur'anic evidence for its obligation, explaining why it is fard 'ayn once in a lifetime.

Core Idea
Hajj is the intention to visit the Ka'bah with specific rites in specific months; it is fard 'ayn once in a lifetime.

This lesson opens the Book of Hajj with a precise definition. The author, al-Marghinani, begins by clarifying the pronunciation of the word 'hajj' and then provides both the linguistic and technical meanings. Understanding this definition is crucial because it distinguishes hajj from other acts of worship and establishes the framework for its rulings, including its obligation as a fard 'ayn upon every capable Muslim once in a lifetime.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two pronunciations
Note that 'hajj' can be read with fatha (ḥajj) or kasra (ḥijj). Each pronunciation is supported by a Qur'anic verse: fatha in 2:197, kasra in 3:197. This establishes both the correct recitation and the source of obligation.
The verse with kasr (3:97) is the primary proof for the obligation of hajj.
2
Analyze the linguistic definition
Linguistically, hajj means 'intending something great' (qasd shay' muʿaẓẓam). Focus on the root meaning: qasd = intention/direction, muʿaẓẓam = something revered. This distinguishes hajj from ordinary travel.
The greatness refers to the Ka'bah and the sacred rites.
3
Dissect the technical definition
Technically, hajj is defined as 'intending a specific place with specific actions in a specific time.' Break this into three components: specific place (the Ka'bah and its precincts), specific actions (the rites like ihram, tawaf, sa'y, wuquf), and specific time (the months of Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, and first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah).
This technical definition excludes 'umrah, which has no fixed time.
4
Connect the definition to obligation
The verse cited with kasr (3:97) states: 'And for Allah upon the people is the hajj of the House.' The phrase 'upon the people' indicates obligation (fard). The Hanafi school treats this as a definitive command (amr) establishing fard, not just wajib.
The verse also includes conditions of capability: 'whoever is able to find a way.'
5
Determine the Hanafi ruling
According to the Hanafi school, hajj is fard 'ayn (individual obligation) once in a lifetime for every free, adult, sane Muslim who is physically and financially capable. Additional hajj is nafl (supererogatory).
This consensus ruling is based on definitive evidence (qat'i).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْحَجِّ. لَفْظُ حَجٍّ بِفَتْحِ الْحَاءِ وَبِكَسْرِ الْحَاءِ. فَتْحُ الْحَاءِ: {الْحَجُّ أَشْهُرٌ مَّعْلُومَاتٌ} [البقرة: 197]، وَبِكَسْرِ الْحَاءِ: {وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ} [آل عمران: 97]. الْحَجُّ لُغَةً: قَصْدُ شَيْءٍ مُعَظَّمٍ. وَشَرْعًا: قَصْدُ مَكَانٍ مَخْصُوصٍ بِفِعْلٍ مَخْصُوصٍ فِي زَمَانٍ مَخْصُوصٍ.
Book of Hajj. The word 'hajj' with fatha on the ha and with kasr on the ha. With fatha: 'Hajj is [in] well-known months' [2:197]. With kasr: 'And for Allah upon the people is hajj of the House' [3:97]. Hajj linguistically: intending something magnified. Legally: intending a specific place with specific actions in a specific time.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Hajj with a definition. It notes that the word 'hajj' can be pronounced with fatha (hajj) or kasra (hijj) on the initial letter, citing Quranic verses for each. Linguistically, hajj means to intend or head towards something great or revered. In Islamic law (shar‘an), it is defined as the intention to visit the sacred House (Ka‘bah) in Mecca during the appointed months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi‘dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah) and to perform the prescribed rituals (such as ihram, tawaf, sa‘y, standing at Arafat, etc.). The definition emphasizes that hajj combines a specific place (the Ka‘bah and its precincts), specific actions (the rites), and a specific time (the Hajj season). This distinguishes it from 'umrah, which can be performed year-round. The passage then discusses when hajj became obligatory for the Muslim ummah. While the text here only gives the definition, the surrounding Urdu commentary mentions differing opinions: some say it was made obligatory in 9 AH, others in 5 or 6 AH, and that the Prophet performed only one Hajj (Hajjat al-Wada‘) after hijrah. There is also a discussion whether hajj was obligatory for previous nations; the stronger view (supported by Hafiz Ibn Hajar) is that it was, as all prophets performed it, but others argue it was merely recommended for them and obligatory only for the Ummah of Muhammad (SAW).

Key Terms
حج (ḥajj): Linguistically: intending something great; legally: visiting the Ka'bah with specific rites in specific time.
فريضة (farīḍah): An obligatory act established by definitive evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Visiting the Ka'bah at any time
B) Intending a specific place with specific actions in a specific time
C) Traveling to Mecca for any purpose
D) Performing tawaf only

Key Takeaway
Hajj is fard 'ayn once; its definition as visiting the Ka'bah with specific rites in specific months distinguishes it from other pilgrimages and establishes its obligation.

Definition and Obligation of Hajj
Introduces the book of Hajj with definition, evidence, conditions, and terminological clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and technical definition of Hajj, cite the primary evidence for its obligation, list the conditions of obligation, and explain why al-Quduri's use of 'wajib' does not reduce the fard status.

Core Idea
Hajj is a definitive fard once in a lifetime upon those with ability; 'wajib' in the matn means established and binding, not the technical lower category.

This lesson opens the chapter on Hajj in Al-Hidayah. You will learn why the chapter is placed after fasting, the linguistic and technical definition of Hajj, the historical background of its obligation, the primary proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma, and the conditions that must be met for Hajj to be obligatory. A key clarification is made about the word 'wajib' in al-Quduri’s text—it does not imply a lesser obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its definition
Determine the linguistic and technical definition of Hajj as presented in the text. Note the two pronunciations.
Linguistically: intending something great. Technically: intending the Kaaba with specific actions at a specific time.
2
Locate the primary proof of obligation
Find the Quranic verse and explain how the preposition 'ala indicates obligation (ijab). Also note the supporting hadiths and consensus.
Quran 3:97: 'wa lillahi 'ala an-nasi hijju al-bayti...' The word 'ala is key.
3
List the conditions of obligation
Extract all conditions for Hajj being obligatory: freedom, adulthood, sanity, health, ability (zad wa rahila) surplus over housing, necessities, and family maintenance, and a safe route.
Ability (istita'ah) includes both provisions and a mount, with surplus conditions.
4
Analyze the terminological nuance
Understand why al-Quduri used 'wajib' even though Hajj is fard. The commentator explains that here 'wajib' means thubut (established) and luzum (binding), not the technical category distinct from fard.
This clarification prevents misunderstanding about the level of obligation.
5
Confirm the ruling: once in a lifetime
Note that Hajj is obligatory only once, based on the hadith 'bal marrah' and that the cause (the House) is singular, so the obligation does not repeat.
Extra Hajj beyond the first is nafl (voluntary).

تشریح حج چونکہ مرکب ہوتا ہے عبادت بدنیہ اور عبادت مالیہ سے اس لئے اس کو روزہ سے جو فقط عبادت بدنیہ ہے مؤخر کیا گیا کیونکہ مرکب مفرد سے مؤخر ہوتا ہے دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ روزہ ہر سال مکرر ہوتا ہے اور حج مکر نہیں ہوتا بلکہ عمر میں فقط ایک بار فرض ہے اس لئے روزہ کی طرف احتیاج زیادہ ہوگی بہ نسبت حج کے اور جس چیز کی طرف احتیاج زیادہ ہوتی ہے وہ تقدیم کے زیادہ لائق ہے اس لئے روزہ کو حج پر مقدم کر کے حج کو بعد میں بیان کیا گیا ہے۔
لفظ حج بِفَتْحِ الْحَاءِ اور بِكَسْرِ الْحاء دونوں طرح استعمال ہوتا ہے فتح الحاء جیسے اَلْحَجُّ اشْهُرٌ مَّعْلُومَاتٌ فَمَنْ فَر ... الآية (بقرة: ۱۹۷) ہے اور بکسر الحاء جیسے وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ .... الآية (ال عمران : ۹۷) ہے حج کے لغوی معنیٰ کسی معظم اور بڑی چیز کی طرف ارادہ کرنے کے ہیں اور شریعت کی اصطلاح میں مخصوص مکان کا مخصوص فعل کے ساتھ مخصوص زمانہ میں ارادہ کرنا ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ حج کب فرض ہوا تو اس بارے میں بذل المجہود میں متعدد اقوال مذکور ہیں (۱)۹ھ ، (۲) ۵ھ، (۳)۶ھ ، (۴) ہجرت سے پہلے ملاعلی قاری نے شرح نقایہ میں لکھا ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فریضہ حج واھ میں ادا کیا ہے جس کو حجتہ الوداع کے نام سے یاد کیا جاتا ہے اور حضرت ابو بکر صدیق نے وھ میں حج کیا ہے اور حج اسی سال فرض ہوا تھاور ۸ھ میں فتح مکہ کے موقع پر لوگوں کو عتاب بن اسید نے حج کرایا تھا حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فتح مکہ کے بعد امیر مکہ انہی کو مقرر فرمایا تھا۔ اس بارے میں بڑا اختلاف ہے کہ ہجرت سے پہلے آپ صلی اللہ علیہ سلم نے کتنے حج کئے ہیں۔ چنانچہ ابن الا بیٹر نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہجرت سے پہلے آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہر سال حج کیا کرتے تھے جابر بن عبداللہ کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فقط تین حج کئے ہیں دو ہجرت سے پہلے اور ایک اھ میں حجتہ الوداع اور ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ رسول خدا صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ہجرت سے پہلے تین حج کئے ہیں ابن الجوزی کہتے ہیں کہ رسول خدا ہے نے بہت سے حج کئے ہیں جن کی تعداد ہمیں معلوم نہیں رہا۔ یہ کہ حج پہلی امتوں پر فرض تھا یا نہیں تو اس میں دو قول ہیں۔ (۱ پہلی امتوں پر بھی حج فرض تھا حافظ ابن حجر نے اس کو ترجیح دی ہے۔
وجوب حج امت محمدیہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے پہلی امتوں پر حج فرض نہ تھا۔ حافظ نے استدلال کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے مَسامِنُ نَنِي إِلَّا حَجَّ الْبَيْتِ یعنی کوئی نبی ایسا نہیں گذرا جس نے بیت اللہ کا حج نہ کیا ہو اور یہ بات بھی کہی جاتی ہے کہ حضرت آدم علیہ السلام نے ہندوستان سے پیدل چل کر چالیس حج کئے ہیں جبریل علیہ السلام نے آدم سے کہا تھا کہ آپ سے سات ہزار سال پہلے ملائکہ بیت اللہ کا طواف کرتے چلے آرہے ہیں۔ قول ثانی کے قائل حضرات نے جواب دیتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ سابقہ دلائل سے صرف اتنی بات ثابت ہوتی ہے کہ انبیاء سابقین کے زمانہ میں حج مشروع رہا ہے اور مشروع ہونے سے واجب اور فرض ہونا لازم نہیں آتا اور یہ بھی ممکن ہے کہ حج انبیاء سابقین پر تو واجب رہا ہو مگر ان کی امتوں پر واجب نہ رہا ہو پس اس صورت میں حج انبیاء کی خصوصیات میں سے ہوگا اور امت محمدیہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی خصوصیات میں سے ہوگا۔
حج کی فرضیت کتاب سنت اور اجماع متینوں سے ثابت ہے بہر حال کتاب اللہ تو باری تعالیٰ کا قول وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلا (ال عمران : ۹۷) ہے علی الناس میں کلمہ علی ایجاب کے لئے ہے اور سنت
( حديث بُنِي الْإِسْلامُ عَلَى الْخَمس ... الحديث
(۲) حَجُوْا فَإِنَّ الْحَجَّ يَغْسِلُ الذُّنُوبَ كَمَا يَغْسِلُ الْمَاءُ الدَّرَن - یعنی حج کرو اس لئے کہ حج گناہوں کو اس طرح دھوڈالتا ہے جس طرح پانی میل کچیل کو ۔ (٣) مَنْ مَّاتَ وَلَمْ يَحُجَّ فَلْيَمُتُ إِنْ شَاءَ يَهُودِيًّا أَوْ نَصْرَانِيًا جوشخص استطاعت کے باوجود بغیر حج کئے مرگیا تو وہ یہودی ہوکر مرے یا نصرانی ہو کر مرے۔ اور اجماع تو ظاہر ہے کہ عہد رسالت سے لے کر آج تک تمام مسلمانوں کا فرضیت حج پر اتفاق چلا آ رہا ہے۔ جمیل احمد ۔
حج کی شرعی حیثیت ، شرائط وجوب حج
الحَج وَاجِبٌ عَلَى الْأحْرَارِ الْبَالِغِيْنَ الْعُقَلاءِ الأَصْحَاءِ إِذَا قَدَرُوا عَلَى الزَّادِ وَالرَّاحِلَةِ فَاضِلا عن المسكن و ما لَا يُدَّمِنَهُ وَعَنْ نَفَقَةِ عَيَّالِهِ إِلى حِيْنَ عَوْدِهِ وَ كَانَ الطَّرِيقُ امِنًا وَصَفَهُ بالوجوب وَهُوَ فَريضَةٌ مُحْكَمَةٌ ثَبَتَ فَرْضِيَّتُها بالكتاب وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ وَلِلهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُ الْبَيْتِ الآية
ترجمہ حج واجب ہے ایسے آدمیوں پر جو آزاد ہوں بالغ ہوں عاقل ہوں تندرست ہوں جبکہ وہ زاد اور راحلہ پر قادر ہوں بشرطیکہ وہ مسکن اور ضرورت کی چیزوں اور تا واپسی عیال کے نفقہ سے فاضل ہو اور راستہ پر امن ہو ۔ مصنف کتاب نے حج کو وجوب کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے حالانکہ حج فریضہ محکمہ ہے جس کی فرضیت کتاب اللہ سے ثابت ہے اور وہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِیلا ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ حج اس پر واجب ہوگا جو آزاد ہو بالغ ہو عاقل ہوا تندرست ہو بشرطیکہ زاد و راحلہ : لہ پر قادر ہو اور یہ زاد و راحلہ رہنے کے مکان ضروریات خانہ اور واپسی تک اہل وعیال کے نفقہ سے فاضل ہو اور راستہ پر امن ہو ۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ قدوری نے حج کے لئے لفظ وجوب استعمال کیا ہے حالانکہ حج فرض قطعی ہے اس کی فرضیت کتاب الله يعني وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِج البيت الآية سے ثابت ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قدوری کی عبارت میں وجوب سے اصطلاحی وجوب مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ وجوب بمعنی ثبوت اور لزوم مراد ہے یعنی حج ثابت اور لازم ہے آزاد عاقل بالغ تندرست پر پس اس صورت میں یہ لفظ فرض کو بھی شامل ہوگا۔ حج زندگی میں ایک مرتبہ فرض ہے
ولا يجب فى الْعُمْرِ الأمَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً لِأنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قِيلَ لَهُ الْحَجُ فِى كُلّ عَامِ أَمْ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً فَقَالَ لَابَلُ مَرَّةً فَمَازَادَ فَهُوَ تَطوُّع ولأنَّ سَبَبَهُ الْبَيْتُ وَأَنَّهُ لَا يَتَعَدَّدُ فَلا يَتَكَرَّ رُالْوُجُوبُ
The Book of Hajj. Translation: This book is about Hajj. Explanation: Since Hajj is composed of bodily worship and financial worship, it is delayed after fasting which is only bodily worship, because the composite is delayed after the simple. Second reason: Fasting is repeated every year while Hajj is not repeated; rather it is obligatory only once in a lifetime, so the need for fasting is greater than for Hajj, and the thing needed more is more deserving of precedence. Therefore fasting was placed before Hajj and Hajj was mentioned later. The word 'hajj' is used with both fatha and kasra on the ha: with fatha as in 'al-hajju ashhurun ma'loomatun...' (al-Baqarah 197) and with kasra as in 'wa lillahi 'ala an-nasi hijju al-bayt...' (Aal-e-Imran 97). Linguistically, hajj means intending something great and important; in Shari'ah terminology, it means intending a specific place with specific actions at a specific time. As for when Hajj became obligatory, multiple opinions are mentioned in Bazi al-Majhood: (1) 9 AH, (2) 5 AH, (3) 6 AH, (4) before Hijra. Mulla 'Ali al-Qari wrote in Sharh al-Niqayah that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) performed the obligation of Hajj in 10 AH known as Hajjat al-Wada', and Abu Bakr al-Siddiq performed Hajj in that year, and Hajj became obligatory that year. In 8 AH at the time of the conquest of Makkah, 'Attab ibn Usayd led the people in Hajj; the Prophet (SAW) had appointed him as governor of Makkah after the conquest. There is great disagreement about how many Hajjs the Prophet (SAW) performed before Hijra. Ibn al-Baytar said he performed Hajj every year before Hijra; Jabir ibn 'Abdillah said he performed only three Hajjs, two before Hijra and one in 10 AH (Hajjat al-Wada'); Ibn 'Abbas said three before Hijra; Ibn al-Jawzi said he performed many Hajjs whose number is unknown to us. Regarding whether Hajj was obligatory on previous nations: there are two opinions. (1) Hajj was obligatory on previous nations as well; Hafiz Ibn Hajar preferred this. (2) The obligation of Hajj is specific to the Ummah of Muhammad (SAW); it was not obligatory on previous nations. Hafiz argued using the hadith 'ma min nabiyyin illa hajja al-bayt' (there is no prophet except that he performed Hajj of the House), and it is also said that Adam (AS) performed forty Hajjs on foot from India; Jibril (AS) told Adam that angels had been circumambulating the Kaaba seven thousand years before him. Those who hold the second opinion respond that the previous proofs only establish that Hajj was legislated (mashru') in the time of previous prophets, and legislation does not necessarily entail obligation (wujub or fardiyyah). It is also possible that Hajj was obligatory on the prophets themselves but not on their nations, so in that case it would be among the special characteristics of the prophets and of the Ummah of Muhammad (SAW). The obligatory nature of Hajj is established by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus. As for the Book of Allah, it is His saying: 'wa lillahi 'ala an-nasi hijju al-bayti mani istata'a ilayhi sabila' (Aal-e-Imran 97); the word 'ala indicates obligation. And the Sunnah includes the hadith 'buniya al-islamu 'ala al-khams...', and (2) 'hujju fa inna al-hajja yaghsilu al-dhunuba kama yaghsilu al-ma'u al-darana' (perform Hajj for it washes away sins as water washes away dirt), and (3) 'man mata wa lam yahujja falyamut in sha'a yahudiyyan aw nasraniyyan' (whoever dies without performing Hajj [despite ability] may die as a Jew or Christian). Consensus is clear: from the time of the Prophet to today, all Muslims have agreed upon the obligation of Hajj. Jamal Ahmad. The legal status of Hajj and the conditions of its obligation. 'Al-Hajj is wajib upon free, adult, sane, healthy persons when they are able to afford provisions and a mount, surplus to housing and what one cannot do without, and to the maintenance of his family until his return, and the road is safe.' The author [al-Quduri] described it with wujub, while it is a confirmed fard whose fardiyyah is established by the Book, namely His saying 'wa lillahi 'ala an-nasi hijju al-bayt' etc. Translation: Hajj is wajib upon people who are free, adult, sane, healthy, when they are able to afford provisions and a mount, provided that this is surplus to housing and necessary items and the maintenance of family until return, and the road is safe. The author of the book used the word wujub for Hajj although Hajj is a confirmed fard whose fardiyyah is established by the Book of Allah, and that is the saying of Allah 'wa lillahi 'ala an-nasi hijju al-bayti mani istata'a ilayhi sabila.' Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says that Hajj will be wajib upon one who is free, adult, sane, healthy, provided he is able to afford provisions and mount, and these provisions and mount are surplus to the dwelling, household necessities, and the maintenance of dependents until return, and the road is safe. Sahib al-Hidayah says that al-Quduri used the word wujub for Hajj although Hajj is a definitive fard, its fardiyyah established by the Book of Allah, i.e., 'wa lillahi 'ala an-nasi hijju al-bayt' etc. The answer to this is that the word wujub in al-Quduri's text does not mean the technical wujub (which is distinct from fard), but rather wujub in the sense of thubut (established) and luzum (binding), i.e., Hajj is established and binding upon a free, sane, adult, healthy person. In that case, this word includes fard as well. Hajj is fard once in a lifetime. 'And it is not wajib in a lifetime except once' because the Prophet (SAW) was asked: 'Is Hajj every year or once?' He said: 'Rather once, and whatever is extra is voluntary.' Also because its cause is the House, and it is not multiple, so the obligation does not recur.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Hajj from Sharh al-Hidayah 'Ashraf al-Hidayah'. The author first explains why the chapter on Hajj is placed after Sawm: Hajj is a composite worship (both physical and financial), and the composite follows the simple; also fasting is repeated annually while Hajj is only once in a lifetime, so the need for fasting is greater. Then he defines the word 'hajj' linguistically (intending something great) and technically (intending the Kaaba with specific actions in specific months). A historical discussion follows about when Hajj became obligatory: multiple opinions from 5 AH to 9 AH to before Hijra, with references to the Prophet's own Hajj practices. The passage then addresses whether Hajj was obligatory on previous nations—two opinions: one that it was (with the saying 'ma min nabiyyin illa hajja al-bayt'), the other that it was only legislated but not obligatory, and that the wujub is specific to this Ummah. After that, the text establishes the fardiyyah of Hajj through three proofs: the Quranic verse (Aal-e-Imran 97) where the preposition 'ala indicates obligation; the Sunnah (three hadiths: the pillars of Islam, the hadith about washing sins, and the threat of dying as a Jew or Christian for neglecting Hajj despite ability); and Ijma' (consensus of the Ummah). Then the passage translates and explains the matn of al-Quduri regarding the conditions of obligation (shurut al-wujub): freedom, adulthood, sanity, health, ability (zad wa rahila) that is surplus beyond housing, indispensable items, and family maintenance until return, and a safe route. There is a technical note: al-Quduri uses the word 'wajib' while Hajj is actually 'fard' (definitive obligation). The commentator resolves this by saying that here 'wajib' means 'thabit' (established) and 'lazim' (binding), not the technical category distinct from fard; thus it includes fard. Finally, the passage states that Hajj is obligatory only once in a lifetime, citing the hadith where the Prophet (SAW) said 'bal marrah' (rather once), and the reasoning that the cause (the House) is singular, so the obligation does not repeat.

Key Terms
حج (hajj): Linguistically: intending something great. Technically: intending the Kaaba with specific actions at a specific time (the months of Hajj).
استطاعة (istita'ah): Ability: possession of provisions (zad) and a mount (rahila) beyond one's dwelling, indispensable items, and family expenses until return.
وجوب (wujub): In the text, it means thubut (establishment) and luzum (binding), not the technical category between fard and sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is the chapter on Hajj placed after the chapter on Sawm?
A) Because Hajj is more important than Sawm
B) Because Hajj is a composite of physical and financial worship, and the composite follows the simple; also fasting is repeated annually while Hajj is once in a lifetime
C) Because the Prophet performed Hajj after Ramadan
D) Because the Quran mentions Hajj after fasting

Key Takeaway
Hajj is a definitive fard once in a lifetime for those who meet the conditions of ability, and the term 'wajib' in the matn is used in its linguistic sense of established and binding, not the technical category.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
The Obligation of Hajj: Proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma
Establishes the obligation of Hajj with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic and hadith proofs for the obligation of Hajj and explain why it is a definitive fard (fard muhkamah).

Core Idea
Hajj is a definitive obligation proven by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.

The obligation of Hajj is one of the five pillars of Islam. In this lesson, we examine the primary evidence that establishes Hajj as a fard upon every eligible Muslim once in a lifetime. The Quranic verse (Al-Imran 3:97) with the preposition 'ala clearly indicates obligation, and the Sunnah provides additional emphasis and warnings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
Recognize that the passage states Hajj is a 'fard muhkamah' (confirmed obligation). Note the use of 'fard' as the highest level of obligation, exceeding 'wajib'.
The author emphasizes that Hajj is not merely wajib but a definitive fard.
2
Locate the Quranic evidence
Find the verse cited: wa lillahi 'ala an-nasi hijju al-bayt... (Al-Imran 3:97). Understand that 'ala indicates obligation (ilzam) in Arabic.
The word 'ala is crucial for deriving wujub.
3
Examine the Sunnah evidence
The passage mentions three hadiths: the five pillars hadith, the hadith that Hajj washes sins, and the severe warning hadith (dying as Jew/Christian if not performed despite ability). Recognize that these are cited as supporting evidence.
These hadiths strengthen the obligation.
4
Consider Ijma (consensus)
The author notes that the entire Ummah has agreed upon the obligation of Hajj from the Prophet's time until today. This provides additional certainty.
Ijma makes the ruling qati (definitive).
5
Derive the conclusion
Combine the evidence: the Quranic verse with its clear indication, the prophetic hadiths, and the consensus. Conclude that Hajj is a definitive fard (fard muhkamah) upon every eligible Muslim once in a lifetime.
The obligation is beyond any doubt.

کتاب الحج
حج کی فرضیت کتاب سنت اور اجماع متینوں سے ثابت ہے بہر حال کتاب اللہ تو باری تعالیٰ کا قول وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلا (ال عمران : ۹۷) ہے علی الناس میں کلمہ علی ایجاب کے لئے ہے اور سنت ( حديث بُنِي الْإِسْلامُ عَلَى الْخَمس ... الحديث) (۲) حَجُوْا فَإِنَّ الْحَجَّ يَغْسِلُ الذُّنُوبَ كَمَا يَغْسِلُ الْمَاءُ الدَّرَن - یعنی حج کرو اس لئے کہ حج گناہوں کو اس طرح دھوڈالتا ہے جس طرح پانی میل کچیل کو ۔ (٣) مَنْ مَّاتَ وَلَمْ يَحُجَّ فَلْيَمُتُ إِنْ شَاءَ يَهُودِيًّا أَوْ نَصْرَانِيًا جوشخص استطاعت کے باوجود ) بغیر حج کئے مرگیا تو وہ یہودی ہوکر مرے یا نصرانی ہو کر مرے۔ اور اجماع تو ظاہر ہے کہ عہد رسالت سے لے کر آج تک تمام مسلمانوں کا فرضیت حج پر اتفاق چلا آ رہا ہے۔
حج کی شرعی حیثیت ، شرائط وجوب حج
الحَج وَاجِبٌ عَلَى الْأحْرَارِ الْبَالِغِيْنَ الْعُقَلاءِ الأَصْحَاءِ إِذَا قَدَرُوا عَلَى الزَّادِ وَالرَّاحِلَةِ فَاضِلا عن المسكن و ما لَا يُدَّمِنَهُ وَعَنْ نَفَقَةِ عَيَّالِهِ إِلى حِيْنَ عَوْدِهِ وَ كَانَ الطَّرِيقُ امِنًا وَصَفَهُ بالوجوب وَهُوَ فَريضَةٌ مُحْكَمَةٌ ثَبَتَ فَرْضِيَّتُها بالكتاب وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ وَلِلهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُ الْبَيْتِ الآية
ترجمہ حج واجب ہے ایسے آدمیوں پر جو آزاد ہوں بالغ ہوں عاقل ہوں تندرست ہوں جبکہ وہ زاد اور راحلہ پر قادر ہوں بشرطیکہ وہ مسکن اور ضرورت کی چیزوں اور تا واپسی عیال کے نفقہ سے فاضل ہو اور راستہ پر امن ہو ۔ مصنف کتاب نے حج کو وجوب کے ساتھ بیان کیا ہے حالانکہ حج فریضہ محکمہ ہے جس کی فرضیت کتاب اللہ سے ثابت ہے اور وہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِیلا ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ حج اس پر واجب ہوگا جو آزاد ہو بالغ ہو عاقل ہوا تندرست ہو بشرطیکہ زاد و راحلہ : لہ پر قادر ہو اور یہ زاد و راحلہ رہنے کے مکان ضروریات خانہ اور واپسی تک اہل وعیال کے نفقہ سے فاضل ہو اور راستہ پر امن ہو ۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ قدوری نے حج کے لئے لفظ وجوب استعمال کیا ہے حالانکہ حج فرض قطعی ہے اس کی فرضیت کتاب الله يعني وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِج البيت الآية سے ثابت ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قدوری کی عبارت میں وجوب سے اصطلاحی وجوب مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ وجوب بمعنی ثبوت اور لزوم مراد ہے یعنی حج ثابت اور لازم ہے آزاد عاقل بالغ تندرست پر پس اس صورت میں یہ لفظ فرض کو بھی شامل ہوگا۔
Hajj's obligation is established by the Book, Sunnah, and consensus of the Ummah. In any case, the Book of Allah is His saying: 'And for Allah is the pilgrimage to the House for those who are able to find a way to it' (Al-Imran:97). The word 'ala in 'ala al-nas indicates obligation. And the Sunnah (hadith: 'Islam is built upon five...'), (2) 'Perform Hajj, for Hajj washes away sins as water washes dirt.' (3) 'Whoever dies without performing Hajj, let him die as a Jew or a Christian.' And consensus is apparent: from the time of the Prophet until today, all Muslims have agreed upon the obligation of Hajj.
The legal status of Hajj, conditions of its obligation: Hajj is obligatory upon free, adult, sane, healthy individuals when they can afford provision and mount, beyond the dwelling and what is indispensable and beyond the maintenance of his household until his return, and the road is safe. The author described it with wujub, whereas it is a confirmed obligation (fard muhkamah) whose obligation is established by the Book, i.e., His saying: 'And for Allah is the pilgrimage to the House...'
Translation: Hajj is obligatory upon those who are free, adult, sane, healthy, when they can afford provision and mount, provided that it is surplus to their dwelling, necessities, and maintenance of dependents until return, and the road is safe. The author of the book stated Hajj with wujub, whereas Hajj is a confirmed fard whose obligation is established by the Book of Allah, i.e., His saying: 'And for Allah is the pilgrimage to the House...'
Explanation: Sahib Quduri says: Hajj will be obligatory upon one who is free, adult, sane, healthy, provided he can afford provision and mount, and these provision and mount are surplus to the dwelling, household necessities, and maintenance of family until return, and the road is safe. Sahib Hidayah says: Quduri used the word wujub for Hajj, whereas Hajj is a definitive fard, its obligation proven by the Book of Allah, i.e., 'And for Allah is the pilgrimage to the House...' The answer is that in Quduri's expression, wujub does not mean the technical wujub, but rather wujub in the sense of thubut (establishment) and luzum (bindingness). That is, Hajj is established and binding upon the free, sane, adult, healthy. In this case, the word includes fard as well.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing the obligation of Hajj and its conditions. The author begins by citing the primary proofs: the Quranic verse (Al-Imran:97) where the preposition 'ala indicates obligation; a hadith from the five pillars; another hadith encouraging Hajj; and a severe warning hadith. Consensus (ijma) of the Ummah from the Prophet's era onward is also invoked. Then the classic matn from al-Quduri is presented, listing the conditions for Hajj obligation: free, adult, sane, healthy, ability (provision and mount), surplus beyond basic needs (dwelling, essentials, dependents' maintenance), and a safe route. The commentator (al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah) notes that al-Quduri used 'wajib' but Hajj is actually fard (a higher level of obligation). The explanation resolves this: al-Quduri's 'wajib' here means 'established and binding' (thabit and lazim), not the technical term that differs from fard. Thus the ruling is clear: Hajj is a definitive fard upon those who meet the conditions. The commentary follows the Hanafi school, affirming that the obligation is proven by definitive evidence (Quran, mutawatir Sunnah, Ijma).

Key Terms
فريضة محكمة (farīḍah muḥkamah): A confirmed, decisive obligation established by definitive evidence (Quran or mutawatir Hadith).
زاد (zād): Provision; food and supplies necessary for the journey to and from Hajj.
راحلة (rāḥilah): A mount or means of transportation suitable for the journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Quranic evidence for the obligation of Hajj?
A) Surah Al-Baqarah 2:196
B) Surah Al-Imran 3:97
C) Surah Al-Hajj 22:27
D) Surah Al-Fatihah 1:1

Key Takeaway
Hajj is a definitive obligation (fard muhkamah) proven by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma, binding upon every eligible Muslim once in a lifetime.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Conditions for the Obligation of Hajj and the Meaning of 'Wajib' in the Matn
Details the conditions for Hajj obligation and resolves the wujub/fard terminology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the conditions that trigger the obligation of Hajj and explain why al-Quduri's use of 'wajib' does not downgrade the ruling from fard.

Core Idea
Hajj is binding upon free, adult, sane, healthy Muslims who have ability (zad and rahila) above essential needs, with a safe route.

The matn from al-Quduri lists precise conditions for when Hajj becomes obligatory. These include personal capacity (free, adult, sane, healthy) and financial ability (provision, mount, surplus beyond basic needs, and safety of the road). The commentator in al-Hidayah addresses an apparent discrepancy: although the matn uses the word 'wajib', Hajj is actually a definitive fard. The explanation is that 'wajib' here carries its linguistic meaning of 'established and binding' (thabit and lazim), not the technical Hanafi category. This resolves the terminological issue and affirms that the obligation is at the highest level.

Guided Path
1
List the personal conditions
Identify the conditions related to the individual: free (not a slave), adult (baligh), sane (a qil), healthy (sahih). These are prerequisites for the obligation.
A slave, minor, insane, or seriously ill person is not obligated to perform Hajj.
2
List the financial conditions
Note the conditions of ability: having provision (zad) and a mount (rahila) that are surplus to one's dwelling, essential needs, and the maintenance of dependents until return. Also, the route must be safe.
These ensure that the obligation does not cause hardship.
3
Identify the terminological issue
Observe that the matn uses the word 'wajib' for Hajj, while the author of al-Hidayah states it is actually a 'fard muhkamah'. Understand that this is not a contradiction.
The apparent contradiction is resolved by understanding the intended meaning of 'wajib'.
4
Understand the resolution
The commentator explains that 'wajib' here means 'thabit' (established) and 'lazim' (binding). In this sense, it includes fard. This is a common usage in early Hanafi texts.
Thus the ruling remains fard; there is no downgrade.
5
Apply the ruling
Conclude that a person who meets all these conditions (free, adult, sane, healthy, with surplus ability and safe route) must perform Hajj as a fard obligation. The term 'wajib' in the matn should not be misunderstood.
This resolves potential confusion for students of fiqh.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner

Hajj Obligatory Once in a Lifetime – The Proofs
Ruling that Hajj is obligatory only once, with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Hajj is fard once in a lifetime and explain the two proofs (hadith and qiyas al-sabab) that support it.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory once because its cause (the Kaaba) is singular and the Prophet rejected annual obligation.

The Hanafi school firmly establishes that Hajj is a once-in-a-lifetime obligation. This lesson unpacks the two proofs relied upon: the explicit hadith in Sahih Muslim and a rational argument based on the uniqueness of the cause (sabab). Understanding these proofs prevents the misconception that Hajj becomes due every year.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The text begins with 'Wa la yajibu fi al-‘umri illa marratan wahidah' – Hajj is not obligatory in one's lifetime except once. Note that additional Hajj is tatawwu' (voluntary).
The ruling applies to the entire lifetime, not per year.
2
Analyze the first proof: the hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked if Hajj is every year. He remained silent, then said if he had said yes it would have become obligatory yearly, and they would not be able to do it. This shows the obligation is not annual.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim, authentically transmitted.
3
Analyze the second proof: qiyas based on cause
The cause (sabab) of Hajj's obligation is the House (Baytullah). Since the House is one and unique, cause is not repeated; therefore the effect (obligation) is not repeated.
This is a logical argument (qiyas) linking uniqueness of cause to non-repetition of ruling.
4
Confirm the mufta bihi and cross-madhhab agreement
All schools agree Hajj is fard once. The Hanafi position is clear and relied upon (mufta bihi).
Intra-school difference is on immediacy (fawr) vs. delay, not on once-only.

Source Text
