ولا يجب فى الْعُمْرِ الأمَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً لِأنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قِيلَ لَهُ الْحَجُ فِى كُلّ عَامِ أَمْ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً فَقَالَ لَابَلُ مَرَّةً فَمَازَادَ فَهُوَ تَطوُّع ولأنَّ سَبَبَهُ الْبَيْتُ وَأَنَّهُ لَا يَتَعَدَّدُ فَلا يَتَكَرَّ رُالْوُجُوبُ
ترجمہ اور حج عمر میں نہیں واجب ہوتا مگر ایک مرتبہ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم سے پوچھا گیا تھا کہ حج ہر سال ہے یا ایک مرتبہ ہے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ نہیں بلکہ ایک مرتبہ پس جو زیادہ کرے افضل ہے اور اس لئے کہ اس کا سبب بہت ہے اور بہت متعدد نہیں ہوتا لہذا او جوب بھی متعدد اور مکرر نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح حج زندگی میں فقط ایک مرتبہ فرض ہے ہر سال فرض نہیں ہے۔ اور اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ صحیح مسلم میں ہے عن آيش هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ الله تَعَالَى عَنْهُ خَطَبَنَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ قَدْ فَرَضَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْحَجَّ فَحَجُوا فَقَالَ رَجُلٌ أَكُلُّ عَامٍ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ فَسَكَتَ حَتَّى قَالَهَا ثَلَانَا فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَوْ قُلتُ نَعَمْ لَوَ جَبَتْ وَلَمَا اسْتَطَعْتُمْ ثُمَّ قَالَ ذَرُونِي مَا تَرَكْتُمْ فَإِنَّمَا هَلَكَ مَنْ كَانَ قَبْلَكُمْ بِكَثْرَةِ سُؤَالِهِمْ وَاخْتِلَافِهِمْ عَلَى هِمْ فَإِذَا أَمَرْتُكُمْ بِشَيْءٍ فَاتُوامَهُ مَاسْتَطَعْتُم وَإِذَا نَهَيْتُكُمْ عَنْ شَيْءٍ فَدُعُوهُ ابو ہریرہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم کو رسول خدا صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے خطبہ دیا تو فرمایا کہ اے لوگو! تم پر حج فرض ہے سوتم حج کرو۔ ایک شخص نے کہا کہ اللہ کے رسول کیا ہر سال ؟ آپ خاموش رہے حتی کہ اس نے یہ بات تین بار کہی پس حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اگر میں ہاں کہہ دیتا تو حج ہر سال واجب ہو جاتا اور ہرگز تم اس کی طاقت نہ رکھتے پھر آپ نے فرمایا کہ مجھ کو چھوڑ دو ان چیزوں سے متعلق سوال کرنے سے جن کو میں نے تمہارے سامنے بیان کرنے سے چھوڑ دیا اس لئے کہ تم سے بہت پہلے لوگ کثرت سوال اور اپنے انبیاء پر اختلاف کرنے کی وجہ سے ہلاک ہوئے ہیں پس جب میں تم کو کسی چیز کا حکم دو تو تم اس کو اپنی بساط کے مطابق بجالا ؤ اور جب میں تم کو کسی چیز سے روکوں تو اس کو چھوڑ دو ۔ اس حدیث میں لفظ لَو قُلْتُ نَعَمُ لَوَجَبَتْ وَلَمَا اسْتَطَعْتُم اس پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ حج میں تکرار نہیں ہے۔ یعنی حج زندگی میں ایک ہی بار فرض ہے بار بار فرض نہیں ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ وجوب حج کا سبب بیت اللہ ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ بیت کی طرف حج کو مضاف کرکے حج بیت اللہ کہا جاتا ہے اور اضافت سبیت کی علامت ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ حج کا سبب بیت اللہ ہے اور بیت اللہ متعدد اور مکر نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک ہی ہے اور یہ معلوم ہی ہے کہ سبب اگر مکرر نہ ہو تو مسبب مکرر نہیں ہوتا اس وجہ سے کہا گیا ہے کہ حج زندگی میں ایک ہی فرض ہے۔
And it is not obligatory in one's lifetime except once, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked: 'Is Hajj every year or once?' He said: 'No, once, and whatever is additional is voluntary.' And because its cause is the House (Kaaba), and it is not multiple, so obligation does not repeat.
Translation: And Hajj is not obligatory in one's lifetime except once, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked: 'Is Hajj every year or once?' He said: 'No, once, so whatever is extra is voluntary.' And because its cause is the House, and the House is not multiple, so obligation does not repeat.
Explanation: Hajj is fard only once in a lifetime, not every year. Its proof is the hadith in Sahih Muslim from Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah addressed us saying, 'O people, Allah has made Hajj obligatory upon you, so perform Hajj.' A man asked, 'Every year, O Messenger of Allah?' He remained silent until the man asked three times, then said, 'If I said yes, it would become obligatory, and you would not be able to do it. Then he said, 'Leave me as I have left you; those before you were destroyed by their excessive questioning and their contradicting their prophets. So when I command you with something, do as much as you can, and when I forbid you from something, avoid it.' The phrase 'If I said yes, it would become obligatory, and you would not be able to do it' indicates that Hajj is not repeated. That is, Hajj is fard once in a lifetime, not repeatedly. The second proof is that the cause of obligation is the House (Kaaba). That is why Hajj is attributed to it and called Hajj of the House. Attribution indicates causation. So the cause is the House, and the House is not multiple or repeated; it is one. And it is known that if the cause is not repeated, the effect is not repeated. For this reason, it is said that Hajj is fard once in a lifetime.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, stating that Hajj is obligatory only once in a lifetime. The matn from al-Quduri gives the ruling succinctly: 'Wa la yajibu fi al-'umri illa marratan wahidah.' The proof is twofold. First, the hadith in Sahih Muslim where the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly refrains from making it annual, saying if he had said 'yes' it would have become obligatory every year, which shows that the obligation is only once. Second, a rational proof (qiyas) based on causation: the cause (sabab) of Hajj's obligation is the House (Baytullah). The House is singular and unique, not multiple. Since the cause is not repeated, the effect (obligation) is not repeated. This is a clear example of Hanafi use of qiyas in establishing rulings. The commentary also notes that additional Hajj beyond the first is voluntary (tatawwu') and meritorious, not obligatory. This ruling is agreed upon within the school, but there is a dispute about whether it must be performed immediately or can be delayed (see next lesson).

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): Legal cause; the reason that triggers an obligation. Here, the House (Kaaba) is the cause for Hajj's obligation.
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary, supererogatory act. Additional Hajj beyond the obligatory one is considered nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is Hajj not obligatory every year?
A) Because the Quran does not mention Hajj.
B) Because the cause of obligation (the Kaaba) is one, not multiple, so the obligation is not repeated.
C) Because the Prophet said Hajj is only for the rich.
D) Because it is impossible to perform Hajj every year.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is fard once in a lifetime because its cause (the Kaaba) is singular, and the Prophet explicitly negated annual obligation.

Hajj: Immediate or Delayed Obligation?
Intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on timing of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether Hajj is obligatory immediately (fawr) or can be delayed (taraakhi), identify the evidence for each, and derive the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime—but must it be done immediately or can it be delayed? The answer depends on how you analogize it to prayer.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: once the conditions for Hajj are met, does it become mandatory at once (fawr) or may it be delayed (taraakhi)? Imam Abu Yusuf argues for immediacy, while Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i allow delay. The disagreement hinges on whether Hajj is like prayer (where the entire period is the time) or a unique annual obligation. Understanding this dispute sharpens your skills in legal analogy (qiyas) and the evaluation of conflicting proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
Determine the exact issue: when all conditions for Hajj are present (adulthood, sanity, ability, etc.), is the obligation to perform Hajj due immediately (fawr) or can it be delayed (taraakhi)?
The dispute is about the timing of performance, not whether Hajj is obligatory.
2
State the two positions within the Hanafi school
Abu Yusuf holds fawr (immediate), supported by a narration from Abu Hanifa. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds taraakhi (delayed), aligning with al-Shafi'i.
Note that both are Hanafi views; the school does not have a single unanimous position.
3
Examine the proof for fawr (Abu Yusuf's view)
Hajj is tied to a specific time (the months of Hajj). Death within a year is not rare, so caution demands immediate performance. Hastening is better (afdal).
The argument uses risk of death and the limited annual window for Hajj.
4
Examine the proof for taraakhi (Muhammad's view)
Hajj is a lifelong duty (wazifat al-umr). Therefore, one's entire lifetime is like the time for prayer: you can perform it at any point within that period. Delay is permissible as long as one intends to do it eventually.
This is an analogy (qiyas) between Hajj and prayer, focusing on the nature of the duty.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If a person delays without excuse and dies, according to Abu Yusuf they are sinful; according to Muhammad, they are not sinful as long as they intended to perform it eventually.
This difference affects moral accountability and recommendation for action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ هُوَ وَاحِبُ عَلَى الْفَوْرِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ وَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ مَا يَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَالشَّافِعِى عَلَى التَّرَاحِى لأنَّهُ وَظِيفَةُ الْعُمُرِ فَكَانَ الْعُمُرِ فِيهِ كَالوَقْتِ فِى الصَّلوةِ وَجْهُ الْأَوَّلِ أَنَّه يَخُصُّ بَوَقْتٍ خَاصِ وَالْمَوْتُ فِي سَنَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ غَيْرَنَا دِرٍ فَيَتَضَيقُ اِحْتِيَاطًا وَلِهَذَا كَانَ التَّعْجِيلِ أفْضَلَ بِخِلَافِ وَقَتِ الصَّلَوةِ لِأَنَّ الْمَوْتَ فِي مِثْلِهِ نَادِرُ
ترجمہ پھر ابو یوسف کے نزدیک حج علی الفور واجب ہے اور ابوحنیفہ سے ایسی بات مروی ہے جو اس پر دلالت کرتی ہے اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک علی التراخی واجب ہے کیونکہ حج تو ء کا وظیفہ ہے پس عمر حج میں ایسی ہے جیسے نماز میں وقت ہے اور اول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ حج وقت مخصوص کے ساتھ خاص ہے اور ایک سال کے عرصہ میں مرجانا نا در نہیں ہے تو احتیاطاتنگی کی گئی اور اسی وجہ سے جلدی ادا کرنا افضل ہے برخلاف نماز کے وقت کے اس لئے کہ اتنے وقت میں مرجانا نا در ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہی کہ جب کسی شخص کے اندر حج فرض ہونے کی تمام شرطیں جمع ہو گئیں تو حج اسی سال علی الفور واجب ہوگا یا علی التراخی واجب ہوگا تو حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اسی سال علی الفور واجب ہے حتی کہ اگر بلا عذر مؤخر کر دیا تو گنہگار ہوگا یہی امام احمد کا قول
Then it is obligatory immediately according to Abu Yusuf, and from Abu Hanifa what indicates it, and according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i it is obligatory at leisure (taraakhi), because it is a lifelong duty, so one's lifetime in it is like the time in prayer. The face of the first (view) is that it is specific to a particular time, and death within one year is not rare, so it becomes restricted out of precaution, and for this reason hastening is better, contrary to the time of prayer because death within such a time is rare.
Translation: Then it is obligatory immediately according to Abu Yusuf, and from Abu Hanifa what indicates it, and according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i it is obligatory at leisure, because it is a lifelong duty, so one's lifetime in it is like the time in prayer. The face of the first is that it is specific to a particular time, and death within one year is not rare, so it is narrowed out of precaution, and for this reason hastening is better, contrary to the time of prayer because death within such a time is rare.
Explanation: The issue is that when all conditions for Hajj being obligatory are met, is it obligatory immediately (within the same year) or at leisure (can be delayed)? Imam Abu Yusuf holds it is immediate, so if one delays without excuse, they sin. This is also the view of Imam Ahmad. Abu Hanifa has a transmission that indicates immediacy. Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i hold it can be delayed, by analogy with prayer: just as the time for prayer is the entire prayer period, one's entire lifetime is the time for Hajj. The proof for Abu Yusuf's view is that Hajj is linked to a specific time (the months of Hajj) and death within a year is not rare, so to be cautious one should hasten; thus hastening is better. In contrast, the time for prayer is broad, and death during that short period is rare.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (with al-Shafi'i also mentioned) regarding whether Hajj, once obligatory, must be performed immediately (fawr) or can be delayed (taraakhi). Abu Yusuf holds fawr, and a narration from Abu Hanifa supports that. Muhammad al-Shaybani and al-Shafi'i hold taraakhi by analogy with prayer: just as the time for prayer extends over the entire prayer period, the lifetime is the time for Hajj. Abu Yusuf's argument: Hajj is specific to a particular time (the months and days of Hajj; if one misses it, they must wait another year), and death within a year is not unlikely, so caution demands prompt performance. Thus, hastening is better (afdal). The commentary notes that this is the view of Imam Ahmad (Hanbali) as well. The Hanafi mufta bihi position is a point of later discussion; many later scholars preferred fawr for precaution, but the school accepts both views. The passage demonstrates the use of qiyas (analogy) and talil (legal reasoning) in deriving the ruling.

Key Terms
على الفور (ʿalā al-fawr): Immediately; the obligation must be fulfilled at the earliest opportunity, without delay.
على التراخي (ʿalā al-tarākhī): With leisure; the obligation can be delayed as long as one intends to fulfill it within one's lifetime.
وظيفة العمر (waẓīfat al-ʿumr): A lifelong duty; something required once in a lifetime, not annually.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the primary basis for Imam Muhammad's view that Hajj is obligatory at leisure (taraakhi)?
A) Death in a year is common.
B) The Quran commands ease.
C) Hajj is a lifelong duty, so the entire lifetime is like the time for prayer.
D) The Prophet said to delay Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two valid views on the timing of Hajj: immediate (fawr) preferred for caution, and delayed (taraakhi) allowed with intention, but the operative fatwa leans toward immediacy.

Hajj: Obligatory Immediately or Permissible to Delay? The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fawr vs tardkhi in Hajj obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf, Abu Hanifa, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the timing of Hajj obligation, and explain the mufta bihi position with its proof.

Core Idea
Hajj is wajib immediately (fawran) upon conditions being met; delaying without excuse is sinful.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines a key intra-madhhab dispute: once all conditions for Hajj are present, must it be performed that very year or can it be delayed? Three Hanafi imams differ, with Abu Yusuf and a narration from Abu Hanifa favouring immediacy, while Muhammad al-Shaybani permits delay but with a condition. Understanding this dispute clarifies the binding nature of Hajj in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
The obligation of Hajj: is it fawran (immediate) or tardkhi (with delay)?
2
State the positions of each imam
Abu Hanifa: reportedly fawran; Abu Yusuf: fawran; Muhammad: tardkhi but sinful if dies without performing; al-Shafi'i: tardkhi with no sin even at death.
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Yusuf's proof: Hajj is tied to specific months and death in a year is not rare. Muhammad's proof: Hajj is a lifelong duty, analogous to prayer within its time.
4
Examine the nuance between Muhammad and al-Shafi'i
Both allow delay, but Muhammad attaches a condition: if one dies without performing, he is sinful; al-Shafi'i does not.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and tarjih
The Hanafi school gives weight to Abu Yusuf's view: Hajj is wajib immediately. This is the preferred position for fatwa.

ثُمَّ هُوَ وَاجِبُ عَلَى الْفَوْرِ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ وَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ مَا يَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَالشَّافِعِى عَلَى التَّرَاخِى لأنَّهُ وَظِيفَةُ الْعُمُرِ فَكَانَ الْعُمُرِ فِيهِ كَالوَقْتِ فِى الصَّلوةِ وَجْهُ الْأَوَّلِ أَنَّه يَخُصُّ بَوَقْتٍ خَاصِ وَالْمَوْتُ فِي سَنَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ غَيْرُ نَادِرٍ فَيَتَضَيقُ اِحْتِيَاطًا وَلِهَذَا كَانَ التَّعْجِيلِ أفْضَلَ بِخِلَافِ وَقَتِ الصَّلَوةِ لِأَنَّ الْمَوْتَ فِي مِثْلِهِ نَادِرُ

ترجمہ پھر ابو یوسف کے نزدیک حج علی الفور واجب ہے اور ابوحنیفہ سے ایسی بات مروی ہے جو اس پر دلالت کرتی ہے اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک علی التراخی واجب ہے کیونکہ حج تو ء کا وظیفہ ہے پس عمر حج میں ایسی ہے جیسے نماز میں وقت ہے اور اول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ حج وقت مخصوص کے ساتھ خاص ہے اور ایک سال کے عرصہ میں مرجانا نا در نہیں ہے تو احتیاطاتنگی کی گئی اور اسی وجہ سے جلدی ادا کرنا افضل ہے برخلاف نماز کے وقت کے اس لئے کہ اتنے وقت میں مرجانا نا در ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہی کہ جب کسی شخص کے اندر حج فرض ہونے کی تمام شرطیں جمع ہو گئیں تو حج اسی سال علی الفور واجب ہوگا یا علی التراخی واجب ہوگا تو حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اسی سال علی الفور واجب ہے حتی کہ اگر بلا عذر مؤخر کر دیا تو گنہگار ہوگا یہی امام احمد کا قول ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام کرتی ہیں اور حضرت امام اعظم سے بھی ایسی بات مروی ہے جو علی الفور وجوب پر دلالت کرتی ہے چنانچہ مروی ہے کہ ایک بار حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے دریافت کیا گیا کہ اگر کسی کے پاس مال ہو تو وہ حج کرے یا نکاح کرے حضرت امام صاحب نے فرمایا کہ حج کرے۔ اس سے بھی ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک حج علی الفور واجب ہے اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک علی التراخی واجب ہے چنانچہ اگر پہلے سال حج نہ کیا بلکہ اس کو مؤخر کر دیا تو ان کے نزدیک گنہگار نہ ہوگا اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے قول میں بھی فرق ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ امام محمد کے نزدیک تاخیر کی اجازت اس شرط کے ساتھ ہے کہ موت کی وجہ سے حج فوت نہ ہو جائے چنانچہ اگر حج کو مؤخر کیا اور بغیر حج کے مر گیا تو گنہ گار ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک تاخیر کی وجہ سے گنہگار نہ ہوگا اگر چہ وہ مر گیا ہو۔ بہر حال ان دونوں حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فریضہ حج کا وقت پوری زندگی ہے بیک حج کے سلسلہ میں پوری زندگی ایسی ہے جیسا کہ نماز کے لئے نماز کا وقت پس جس طرح نماز آخر وقت میں ادا کرنا جائز ہے اس طرح حج بھی آخر عمر میں ادا کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ حج ایک خاص وقت یعنی اشہر حج ( شوال، ذوالقعدہ، ذوالحجہ ) کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے اور جو چیز کسی خاص وقت کے ساتھ مخصوص ہوا گر وہ اپنے وقت سے فوت ہوگئی تو وہ اس کو اس وقت معینہ میں ادا کرے گا۔ اب حج کا وقت فوت ہونے کے بعد دوبارہ ایک سال میں عود کرے گا اور سال بھر کی مدت بہت طویل ہے اس مدت میں موت وحیات دونوں برابر ہیں یعنی اس مدت میں موت کا آنا کوئی نادر نہیں ہے بلکہ موت آ سکتی ہے اس لئے احتیاط اس میں ہے کہ حج کا وقت تنگ کر دیا جائے اور یہ کہا جائے کہ جس سال شرائط حج جمع ہو گئیں اس سال حج فرض ہے لیکن یہ خیال رہے کہ اگر اس سال حج نہ کر سکا تو جب بھی کرے گا وہ ادا ہو گا، قضاء نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ تنگی وقت کا مدارا احتیاط پر ہے نہ کہ تحقیق پر۔ امام ابو یوسف نے اپنی دلیل کو مضبوط کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ حج ادا کرنے میں با اتفاق جلدی کرنا افضل ہے برخلاف نماز کے وقت کے اتنی دیر میں موت کا آنا نا در ہے اس لئے نماز کو اس کے وقت میں مؤخر کرنا خلاف احتیاط کام نہ ہوگا۔
Then it (hajj) is obligatory immediately according to Abu Yusuf, and from Abu Hanifa there is what indicates it. According to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, it is obligatory with delay (tardkhi) because it is a lifelong duty, so the lifespan in it is like the time for prayer. The evidence for the first is that it is specific to a particular time, and death in one year is not rare, so it is narrowed as a precaution, and thus acceleration is better, unlike the time of prayer because death in its like is rare. Translation: Then, according to Abu Yusuf, Hajj is obligatory immediately, and from Abu Hanifa a narration indicates that. According to Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i, it is obligatory with delay because Hajj is a lifelong duty, so the lifespan for Hajj is like the time for prayer. The evidence for the first (immediate) is that Hajj is specific to a particular time, and death within a year is not rare, so it is narrowed as a precaution, and therefore acceleration is better, unlike the time of prayer because death in its period is rare. Explanation: The issue is that when all conditions for Hajj being obligatory are met, is it obligatory immediately that year or can it be delayed? Imam Abu Yusuf says it is obligatory immediately that year; if delayed without excuse, one becomes sinful. This is also the view of Imam Ahmad. And it is also the view of Imam Karkhi. And from Imam Abu Hanifa a narration indicates immediate obligation, as he said when asked whether to perform Hajj or marry: 'Perform Hajj.' Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i say it is obligatory with delay; if not performed the first year, no sin. However, there is a difference between Muhammad and Shafi'i: Muhammad permits delay on condition that Hajj is not lost by death; if one delays and dies without Hajj, he is sinful. Shafi'i says no sin even if death occurs. Their proof: the time for Hajj is one's entire life, so performing at the end of life is permissible, just as prayer at the end of its time is permissible. Abu Yusuf's proof: Hajj is specific to a particular time (the months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, Dhu al-Hijjah). If that time passes, it returns after a year. Since death in a year is not rare, precaution demands narrowing the time to the first year. However, if one cannot perform that year, later performance is ada (not qada) because the narrowing is based on precaution, not actual fixed time. Abu Yusuf also says that there is consensus that acceleration is better, unlike the time of prayer where delaying to the end is not against precaution because death is rare in that short period.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (and also includes al-Shafi'i) on whether Hajj must be performed immediately upon the conditions being met or can be delayed. Abu Yusuf holds that it is wajib immediately (fawran), such that if one delays without excuse, they are sinful. There is a narration from Abu Hanifa also indicating fawran, as he advised to perform Hajj over marriage when asked. Muhammad and al-Shafi'i hold it is wajib with delay (tardkhi), meaning it can be performed at any time during one's life, and one is not sinful for delaying. However, Muhammad adds a condition: if one delays and then dies without performing Hajj, they are sinful, whereas Shafi'i says even if they die, no sin. Their proof: Hajj is a lifelong duty, like the time for prayer, so delay is permissible. Abu Yusuf's proof: Hajj is specific to the Hajj months, and since death is not rare within a year, precaution demands immediate action. Nevertheless, even according to Abu Yusuf, if one misses the year, performing it later counts as ada (not qada). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that Hajj is wajib immediately (fawran) according to the majority of later scholars.

Key Terms
علی الفور (ala al-fawr): Immediately, without delay.
علی التراخی (ala al-tarakhi): With delay, permissible to postpone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which imam holds that delaying Hajj is permissible without sin even if one dies before performing it?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Al-Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that Hajj is wajib immediately upon conditions being met; delaying without excuse incurs sin, though the later performance counts as ada.

Why Freedom and Puberty are Conditions for Hajj Obligation
Evidence for requiring freedom and puberty for Hajj obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith evidence for why freedom and puberty are conditions for Hajj obligation and explain the legal implication for a slave or child's Hajj.

Core Idea
A slave's or child's Hajj does not count for the obligatory Hajj; freedom and puberty are prerequisites for obligation.

This lesson examines the proof from hadith that establishes freedom and puberty as conditions for Hajj obligation. You will see why a slave's repeated Hajj before freedom does not fulfill the Islamic duty, and similarly for a child. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining when Hajj becomes wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is Hajj. The ruling established is that Hajj is obligatory only upon a free, adult Muslim. Slavery and minority are obstacles to this obligation.
The ruling is not about the validity of the act, but about its requirement.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is a hadith: 'Any slave who performs ten Hajjs and then is freed, upon him is the Hajj of Islam; and any child who performs Hajj and then reaches puberty, upon him is the Hajj of Islam.'
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator) but accepted by all Hanafis.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly states that even after many Hajjs, the obligation remains upon freedom or puberty. This shows that the previous Hajj did not fulfill the fard. Hence, slavery and childhood are conditions that prevent the obligation from being discharged.
The hadith uses the words 'عليه حجة الإسلام' – upon him is the Hajj of Islam – indicating the obligatory Hajj.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no disagreement among Hanafi jurists on this ruling. All three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree that freedom and puberty are conditions for obligation.
The ruling is muttafaq alayh within the school.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The position is squarely based on the hadith, supported by the general principle that acts of worship are not required of minors and slaves. Sound intellect and physical ability are also mentioned as conditions.
No tarjih needed as there is no conflict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرط حریت و بلوغ کی دلیل

إنَّمَا شُرِطَ الْحُرِّيَةُ وَالْبُلُوعُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَيُّمَا عَبْدٍ حَجَّ عَشْرَ حِجَجٍ ثُمَّ أُعْتِقَ فَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةُ الْإِسْلَامِ وَأَيُّمَا صَبِيٍّ حَجَّ ثُمَّ بَلَغَ فَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةُ الإِسْلَامِ وَلِأَنَّهُ عِبَادَةُ وَالْعِبَادَاتُ بِأَسَرِهَا مَوْضُوعَةً عَنِ الصَّبْيَانِ وَالْعَقْلُ شَرْطٌ لِصِحَةِ التَّكْلِيفِ وَكَذَا صِحَةُ الْجَوَارِحِ لِأَنَّ الْعَجْزَ دُونَهَا لَازِم

ترجمہ اور آزادی اور بلوغ کی شرط اس لئے لگائی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر کسی غلام نے دس حج کئے پھر آزاد ہو گیا تو اس پر اسلام کا حج فرض ہے اور جس بچہ نے حج کئے پھر بالغ ہو گیا تو اس پر اسلام کا حج فرض ہے اور اس لئے کہ حج ایک عبادت ہے اور تمام عبادات بچوں سے اٹھالی گئیں ہیں اور عقل صحت تکلیف کی شرط ہے اور یوں ہی جوارح کا تندرست ہونا کیونکہ بغیر صحت جوارح کے عاجز ہونا لازم ہے۔

تشریح امام قدوری نے پہلی شرط آزاد ہونے کی لگائی ہے اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ايَّمَا عَبْدٍ حَجَّ عَشْرَ حِجَجٍ ثُمَّ أَعْتَقَ فَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةُ الإِسْلَامِ یعنی غلام اگر دس حج کرلے اور پھر آزاد ہو تو اس پر فریضہ حج لازم ہوگا یعنی آزاد ہونے سے پہلے جو حج کئے ہیں الخ
The reason for stipulating freedom and puberty: because of his (SAW) statement: 'Any slave who performs ten Hajjs and then is freed, upon him is the Hajj of Islam; and any child who performs Hajj and then reaches puberty, upon him is the Hajj of Islam.' And because it is an act of worship, and all acts of worship are lifted from children. Intellect is a condition for the validity of taklif, and similarly soundness of limbs, because inability without them is necessary. Translation: And the condition of freedom and puberty is stipulated because the Prophet (SAW) said: 'Any slave who performs ten Hajjs and then is freed, upon him is the Hajj of Islam; and any child who performs Hajj and then reaches puberty, upon him is the Hajj of Islam.' And because Hajj is an act of worship, and all acts of worship are removed from children. Intellect is a condition for the validity of legal obligation, and similarly soundness of limbs, because inability is necessary without them. Commentary: Imam al-Quduri stipulated the first condition of freedom. Its proof is this hadith: 'Any slave who performs ten Hajjs and then is freed, upon him is the Hajj of Islam.' That is, if a slave performs ten Hajjs and then is freed, the obligatory Hajj becomes required, meaning the Hajj he performed before freedom does not count.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage provides the proof for the conditions of freedom (hurriyya) and puberty (bulugh) for the obligation of Hajj. The primary evidence is a hadith: a slave's Hajj does not fulfill the Islamic obligation; if freed, he must perform Hajj again. Similarly, a child's Hajj before puberty does not count for the obligatory Hajj. The commentator adds a general principle: acts of worship are not required of children. Additionally, sound intellect and physical ability are conditions. This is a standard Hanafi position: the Hajj of a slave or child is valid as nafl (supererogatory) but does not discharge the fard obligation.

Key Terms
حریت (hurriyyah): Freedom; not being a slave.
بلوغ (bulugh): Puberty; reaching the age of legal responsibility.
عقل (aql): Intellect, sanity; a condition for legal responsibility (taklif).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith in this passage indicate about a slave's Hajj?
A) It fulfills the obligation completely.
B) It is invalid and must be repeated even if freed.
C) It does not fulfill the obligation; the slave must perform Hajj again after being freed.
D) A slave is not required to perform Hajj at all.

Key Takeaway
Freedom and puberty are essential conditions for the obligation of Hajj; a slave or child's Hajj is valid as nafl but does not fulfill the Islamic duty.

Immediate vs. Delayed Obligation of Hajj
Inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute on fawran vs tarakhi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing of Hajj obligation (fawran) and explain the proof of Abu Yusuf versus the opposing view of Muhammad and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Hanafi: Hajj must be performed the first year possible; delay risks death and sin.

This passage examines a key ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school and between madhhabs: is Hajj obligatory immediately (fawran) when conditions are met, or can it be delayed (tarakhi) until later? The ruling has practical implications: if someone delays and dies, are they sinful? We will explore the proofs of each position, focusing on the talil (ratio legis) and the precautionary principle that shapes the Hanafi mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine the exact point of disagreement: is the obligation of Hajj to be fulfilled immediately (fawran) upon meeting conditions, or may it be delayed (tarakhi) within one’s lifetime?
The obligation itself is fard; the dispute is about timing.
2
State the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold fawran. The text narrates an incident where Abu Hanifa prioritized Hajj over marriage, indicating immediacy. Abu Yusuf argues that Hajj is tied to specific months, and the long interval between two Hajj seasons makes death a real possibility, so precaution requires immediacy.
3
State the opposing view
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i hold tarakhi. Their proof: the entire lifetime is the time for Hajj, analogous to the time for prayer. Just as one may pray at the end of the prayer time, one may perform Hajj at any point in life.
Imam Muhammad adds a condition: delay is allowed only if death does not cause the Hajj to be missed.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the qiyas
The Hanafis respond that the analogy to prayer is flawed because death within a short prayer time is rare, but within a full year it is not rare. Thus, delaying Hajj carries a risk of missing the obligation entirely, which is impermissible.
This distinction is based on precaution (ihtiyat), not on a strict textual proof.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If one delays and dies: according to Muhammad, he is sinful if he could have performed it; according to Shafi'i, he is not sinful. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, he is sinful for delaying without performing.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the fawran position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Source Text

آتا به ارنج [؟] ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام کرتی ہیں اور حضر - امام اعظم سے بھی ایسی بات مروی ہے جو علی الفور و جوب پر دلالت کرتی ہے چنانچہ مروی ہے کہ ایک بار حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے دریافت کیا گیا کہ اگر کسی کے پاس مال ہو تو وہ حج کرے یا نکاح کرے حضرت امام صاحب نے فرمایا کہ چ کرے۔ اس سے بھی ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک حی علی الفور واجب ہے اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک علی التراخی واجب ہے چنا نچہ اگر پہلے سال حج نہ کیا بلکہ اس کو مؤخر کر دیا تو ان کے نزدیک گنہگار نہ ہوگا اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے قول میں بھی فرق ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ امام محل کے نزدیک تاخیر کی اجازت اس شرط کے ساتھ ہے کہ موت کی وجہ سے حج فوت نہ ہو جائے چنانچہ اگر حج کو مؤخر کیا اور بغیر حج کے مر گیا تو گنہ گار ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک تاخیر کی وجہ سے گنہگار نہ ہوگا اگر چہ وہ مر گیا ہو۔ بہر حال ان دونوں حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فریضہ حج کا وقت پوری زندگی ہے بیک حج کے سلسلہ میں پوری زندگی ایسی ہے جیسا کہ نماز کے لئے نماز کا وقت پس جس طرح نماز آخر وقت میں ادا کرنا جائز ہے اس طرح حج بھی آخر عمر میں ادا کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ حج ایک خاص وقت یعنی اشہر حج ( شوال، ذوالقعدہ، ذوالحجہ ) کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے اور جو چیز کسی خاص وقت کے ساتھ مخصوص ہوا گر وہ اپنے وقت سے فوت ہوگئی تو وہ اس کو اس وقت معینہ میں ادا کرے گا۔ اب حج کا وقت فوت ہونے کے بعد دوبارہ ایک سال میں عود کرے گا اور سال بھر کی مدت بہت طویل ہے اس مدت میں موت وحیات دونوں برابر ہیں یعنی اس مدت میں موت کا آنا کوئی نادر نہیں ہے بلکہ موت آ سکتی ہے اس لئے احتیاط اس میں ہے کہ حج کا وقت تنگ کر دیا جائے اور یہ کہا جائے کہ جس سال شرائط حج جمع ہو گئیں اس سال حج فرض ہے لیکن یہ خیال رہے کہ اگر اس سال حج نہ کر سکا تو جب بھی کرے گا وہ ادا ہو گا، قضاء نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ تنگی وقت کا مدارا احتیاط پر ہے نہ کہ تحقیق پر۔ امام ابو یوسف نے اپنی دلیل کو مضبوط کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ حج ادا کرنے میں با اتفاق جلدی کرنا افضل ہے برخلاف نماز کے وقت کے اتنی دیر میں موت کا آنا نا در ہے اس لئے نماز کو اس کے وقت میں مؤخر کرنا خلاف احتیاط کام نہ ہوگا۔
[Unclear text] and Imam [Kurti?] are of this view, and from Imam A'zam a similar narration is reported indicating immediacy. As narrated: once Imam Abu Hanifa was asked if someone has wealth, should he perform Hajj or marriage? Imam said: perform Hajj. This shows that according to Imam, Hajj is obligatory immediately. According to Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i, it is obligatory with delay. So if one does not perform Hajj in the first year but delays, they are not sinful. There is a difference between Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i: according to Imam Muhammad, delay is allowed on condition that death does not cause Hajj to be missed. If one delays and dies without Hajj, he is sinful. According to Imam Shafi'i, delay does not cause sin even if he dies. In any case, the proof of these two is that the time for Hajj is one's entire life; for Hajj, the whole life is like the time for prayer. Just as it is permissible to pray at the end of the time, so is Hajj at the end of life. And the reason for Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is that Hajj is specific to a particular time, i.e., the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, Dhul-Hijjah). Something specific to a time, if that time passes, it will be performed in that specific time. Now after the time passes, it returns in another year. One year is a long period; in that period, life and death are equal, meaning death is not rare. So precaution dictates that the time be tightened and it be said that in the year conditions are met, Hajj is obligatory. But note that if he cannot perform Hajj that year, whenever he does it, it will be ada, not qada, because tightening is based on caution, not reality. Imam Abu Yusuf strengthened his proof by saying that performing Hajj quickly is unanimously better. Unlike the time for prayer, death is rare in that short delay, so delaying prayer in its time is not against caution.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage discusses the dispute on whether Hajj is obligatory immediately (fawran) or with delay (tarakhi). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it is immediate; Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i hold it is with delay. The text narrates an incident where Abu Hanifa prioritized Hajj over marriage, indicating fawran. Muhammad and Shafi'i argue that the entire lifetime is the time for Hajj, analogous to prayer time. Abu Yusuf reasons that Hajj is specific to a fixed time (the hajj months), and if missed, it returns the next year, making delay risky; thus precaution requires immediacy. The passage compares this to prayer, where delay within the time is allowed due to rarity of death. The author explains the nuanced differences: for Muhammad, delay is conditional on not dying without Hajj; for Shafi'i, no sin even at death. This is an inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute, with the Hanafi mufta bihi being fawran.

Key Terms
علی الفور ('ala al-fawr): Immediately, without delay; obligation must be fulfilled as soon as possible.
علی التراخی ('ala al-tarakhi): With delay; obligation can be postponed within one's lifetime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Imam Abu Yusuf on the obligation of Hajj?
A) It is obligatory immediately.
B) It is obligatory with delay.
C) It is not obligatory at all.
D) It depends on the availability of a guide.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school (with the exception of Imam Muhammad) holds that Hajj must be performed immediately upon ability, due to precaution against death.

Conditions of Freedom and Puberty for Hajj: Evidence and Proof
Provides evidence for freedom and puberty as conditions for Hajj obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for Hajj obligation (freedom, puberty, intellect, soundness) and explain the evidence from hadith and rational arguments.

Core Idea
A slave's or child's Hajj does not fulfill the obligation; freedom and puberty are essential conditions for Hajj to be obligatory.

This lesson delves into the proof provided by Imam al-Quduri for the conditions of freedom and puberty in Hajj. The primary evidence is a prophetic hadith, augmented by rational arguments concerning ownership, rights, and capacity. Understanding these proofs solidifies the Hanafi position on who must perform Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Conditions Stated
The passage explicitly requires freedom (hurriyah) and puberty (bulugh) for Hajj obligation. Also mentioned are intellect (aql) and soundness of limbs (sihhat al-jawarih).
2
Examine the Primary Hadith Evidence
The hadith states that a slave who performs ten Hajj then freed must perform Hajj al-Islam; similarly a child who performs ten Hajj then reaches puberty must do the same. This proves that prior Hajj does not count as obligatory.
Both narrations are ahad, but their meaning is clear (qati' al-dalalah).
3
Understand the Rational Arguments for Freedom
Three reasons: (a) slave cannot own provisions and mount (lack of istita'ah), (b) master's right to service is lost, (c) the right of a human (master) precedes the right of Allah when they conflict.
4
Understand the Rational Arguments for Puberty
Two reasons: (a) worship is lifted from children (the pen is lifted), (b) the clear hadith evidence.
5
Note Additional Conditions
Intellect and physical ability are also conditions; without them, obligation is not valid, as the incapable are not obligated.

Source Text

Evidence for condition of freedom and puberty: It is required by his (saw) statement: 'Any slave who performs ten Hajjs and then is freed, upon him is the Hajj of Islam. And any child who performs [ten] Hajjs and then reaches puberty, upon him is the Hajj of Islam.' And because Hajj is an act of worship, and all acts of worship are lifted from children. And intellect is a condition for validity of obligation, as is soundness of limbs, because incapacity without them is necessary. Translation: The condition of freedom and puberty is set because the Prophet (saw) said: 'Any slave who performs ten Hajjs and then is freed, upon him is the Hajj of Islam. And any child who performs ten Hajjs and then reaches puberty, upon him is the Hajj of Islam.' And because Hajj is worship, and all worships are lifted from children. And intellect is a condition for validity of obligation, and similarly soundness of limbs, because without soundness of limbs, incapacity is necessary. Commentary: Imam Quduri set the first condition as freedom. Its evidence is this hadith. If a slave performs ten Hajjs and then is freed, the obligation of Hajj becomes upon him, meaning the Hajj performed before freedom does not fulfill the obligation. The second evidence is that Hajj cannot be attained without wealth, because for obligation, ability regarding provisions and mount is a condition, and a slave is not capable of owning provisions and mount, so he is not qualified for obligation of Hajj. The third evidence is that in the long duration of Hajj, the master's right to service would be lost, while the right of the servant precedes the right of Allah, so for protection of the servant's right, Hajj is not made obligatory upon him. And the condition of puberty is set because the hadith says: 'Any child who performs ten Hajjs and then reaches puberty, upon him is the Hajj of Islam.' Meaning if a child performs ten Hajjs and then becomes adult, the obligation of Hajj is necessary upon him; the Hajj performed before puberty does not drop the obligation. Second evidence: Hajj is worship, and all worships are lifted from children, so Hajj is not obligatory upon children. And intellect is a condition because without intellect, making one obligated is not valid. And soundness of limbs is a condition because without soundness and health, incapacity is necessary, and the incapable is not obligated for any worship, so Hajj is not obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage provides the evidence for why freedom and puberty are conditions for the obligation of Hajj. The primary proof is the hadith: a slave's Hajj before freedom does not count as the obligatory Hajj of Islam, nor does a child's Hajj count after puberty. Additional rational arguments are given: (1) A slave does not own the means of travel (provisions and mount) so he is not capable. (2) The master's right to service would be lost during the long Hajj journey, and the right of the servant (human) takes precedence over the right of Allah. Therefore Hajj is not obligatory on slaves. For minors, worship is generally not required (the pen is lifted). Intellect and physical ability are also necessary; the insane or disabled are not obligated. This lesson is a standard Hanafi presentation of the conditions for Hajj obligation based on textual and rational evidence.

Key Terms
حریت (hurriyah): Freedom; being a free person, not a slave. A condition for Hajj obligation.
بلوغ (bulugh): Puberty; reaching legal maturity. A condition for any obligation in worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Those Hajj count as the obligatory Hajj.
B) He must perform Hajj again after freedom.
C) He is exempt from Hajj for life.
D) He must perform additional Hajj for each year of slavery.

Key Takeaway
Freedom and puberty are essential conditions for Hajj obligation, proven by hadith and rational arguments; a slave or child's Hajj does not fulfill the Islamic obligation.

Hajj Obligation for a Blind Person with a Guide
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Hajj obligation with guide

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on Hajj for a blind person with a guide and identify the basis of the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Ability through another is insufficient for obligation according to Abu Hanifa.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a blind person who possesses provisions and a mount, and also finds a guide to lead him, is obligated to perform Hajj. The disagreement revolves around the concept of istita'ah (ability) and whether it can be fulfilled through the help of another. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi school's approach to obligation and the role of indirect capacity.

Guided Path
1
State the uncontested scenario
Identify the case where all scholars agree: a blind person without a guide is not obligated to perform Hajj. This establishes a baseline.
If the blind person lacks a guide, there is no capacity, so Hajj is not obligatory.
2
Identify the point of disagreement
When a guide is available, Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree. State each position clearly.
Abu Hanifa: not obligatory. Sahibayn: obligatory.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to Jumu'ah prayer, which is not obligatory on the blind even if a guide leads them. The underlying principle is that ability must be personal, not achieved through a helper.
The analogy shows that indirect assistance does not create obligation in other acts of worship.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn consider the guide as a valid means of achieving ability. For them, istita'ah bil-ghayr is sufficient for obligation because the blind person can still perform the actions with help.
They prioritize the possibility of performing the rituals over the source of ability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is whether the blind person is sinful for not performing Hajj and whether it is wajib on him to go or hire someone.
According to Abu Hanifa, no sin; according to Sahibayn, sin if he does not go.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْأَعْمَى إِذَا وَجَدَ مَنْ يَكْفِيهِ مَوْنَةَ سَفَرِهِ وَوَجَدَ زَادًا وَرَا حِلَةً لَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الْحَجُّ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ خِلَاقًا لَهُمَا وَ قَدْ مَرَّ فِي كِتَابِ الصَّلوة
ترجمہ اور نا بینا بجب ایسے شخص کو پائے جو اس کے سفر کی مشقت کو کفایت کرے اور زاد وراحلہ بھی پائے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر حج واجب نہیں ہوگا صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے اور یہ کتاب الصلوۃ میں گزر چکا۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نابینا آدمی اگر زاد و راحلہ پر قادر ہو لیکن قائد جو اس کو افعال حج ادا کرا سکے میسر نہ ہو تو بالا تفاق اس نا بینا پر حج فرض نہ ہوگا اور اگر قائد موجود ہے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی حج واجب نہیں ہے جیسا کہ نابینا پر قائد موجود ہونے کے باوجود جمعہ فرض نہیں ہوتا ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک واجب ہو جائے گا بنیاد اختلاف یہ ہے کہ غیر کی قدرت سے جو استطاعت حاصل ہوتی ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک وہ معتبر نہیں ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک معتبر ہے اب رہی یہ بات کہ نابینا کو اگر قائد میسر نہ ہو اور زاد وراحلہ پر قادر ہو تو کیا دوسرے کسی کو مال دیگر حج کرانا واجب ہے یا واجب نہیں ہے تو اسکا حکم یہ ہے کہ حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک واجب نہیں ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک واجب ہے۔ اس کی تفصیل کتاب الصلوۃ میں گزر چکی ۔
And the blind person, if he finds someone who suffices for the hardship of his travel and finds provisions and mount, Hajj is not obligatory upon him according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And it has passed in the Book of Prayer. Translation: For a blind person, if he finds someone who covers his travel hardship and finds provisions and mount, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Hajj is not obligatory upon him; the two companions disagree, and this has passed in the Book of Prayer. Commentary: The issue is that if a blind person has provisions and mount but no guide, all agree Hajj is not obligatory. If a guide is present, Abu Hanifa says Hajj is not obligatory, like Jumu'ah is not obligatory on a blind person even with a guide. The two companions say it becomes obligatory. The basis of the difference is whether ability attained through another is considered valid. Abu Hanifa says it is not considered; the two companions say it is. Now if a blind person has no guide but has provisions and mount, is it obligatory to hire someone to perform Hajj on his behalf? According to Imam, it is not obligatory; according to the two, it is. This detail has passed in the Book of Prayer.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of Hajj for a blind person. If the blind person cannot find a guide, all agree Hajj is not obligatory. The dispute arises when a guide is available: Abu Hanifa holds that Hajj is not obligatory, analogous to Jumu'ah (Friday prayer) which is not obligatory on the blind even if they are led. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it becomes obligatory because the ability derived from another (the guide) is valid. The fundamental difference is whether istita'ah (ability) can be achieved through the help of another. Abu Hanifa does not consider it sufficient for obligation; the two companions do. The text also notes that if the blind person cannot go himself but has funds, he must hire someone to perform Hajj on his behalf? According to Abu Hanifa, this is not obligatory; according to the two, it is. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute with the mufta bihi likely being the view of the two companions (as per later Hanafi fatwa), but the text does not specify.

Key Terms
قائد (qa'id): A guide who leads the blind person to perform the actions of Hajj.
استطاعت بالغیر (istita'ah bil-ghayr): Ability attained through the help of another person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Whether ability acquired through another is valid for obligation.
C) Whether the blind person has sufficient wealth.
D) Whether Hajj is obligatory on the blind at all.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on Hajj for the blind hinges on whether istita'ah bil-ghayr creates obligation, with the mufta bihi being the Sahibayn's view that it does.

Hajj Obligation for a Paralyzed Person
Intra-Hanafi dispute about a paralyzed person's Hajj obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the position of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad on Hajj for a paralyzed person and apply Abu Hanifa's ruling to a relevant scenario.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa obliges Hajj for the paralyzed who can be carried; Muhammad does not — depends on whether ability through another suffices.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of Hajj for a person who is paralyzed (maq'ad) and cannot walk but can be carried to the sacred sites. The crux is whether being carried constitutes 'ability' (istita'ah) for Hajj. Abu Hanifa analogizes to a person with a mount, while Imam Muhammad analogizes to one who gets lost. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to see how different analogical premises lead to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed issue
Identify the exact point of disagreement: whether Hajj is obligatory on a paralyzed person who can be transported to the rituals.
The common ground: both agree the paralyzed cannot perform the actions actively.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa holds Hajj is obligatory. His evidence: the paralyzed has ability through another (being carried), so he is like one who has a mount (mustati' bi al-rahila). The mount compensates for lack of walking ability.
The key analogy: passive participation suffices for Hajj.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position and dalil
Imam Muhammad holds Hajj is not obligatory. His evidence: the paralyzed cannot perform the actions himself, unlike the blind who can act with guidance. He analogizes the paralyzed to one who loses his way (dal) — unable to reach the destination.
Muhammad emphasizes direct personal action as essential.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a paralyzed person has means to be carried, according to Abu Hanifa he must perform Hajj; according to Muhammad he is not obligated.
This affects whether one must spend wealth on hiring carriers.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The passage does not give a tarjih, but later Hanafi fatwa often follows Abu Hanifa's view. In practice, a paralyzed person with resources must perform Hajj.
Check the fatwa hierarchy for your jurisdiction.

And as for the paralyzed, from Abu Hanifa that it is obligatory because he is capable through another, so he resembles the one capable with a mount. And from Muhammad that it is not obligatory because he is not able to perform by himself, unlike the blind because if he is assisted, he can perform by himself, so he resembles the one who gets lost from the place of Hajj. Translation: As for the paralyzed (maq'ad), from Abu Hanifa: it is obligatory, because he has capability through another, and thus resembles the one who has capability through a mount. From Muhammad: it is not obligatory, because he is not capable of performing by himself, unlike the blind, because if he is given assistance, he can perform by himself, so he resembles the one who gets lost from the place of Hajj.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for a paralyzed person (maq'ad) who cannot walk but can be carried. According to Abu Hanifa, Hajj is obligatory because he has ability through another (being carried), similar to a person who has a mount (riding animal) to perform Hajj. According to Imam Muhammad, it is not obligatory because he cannot perform the actions of Hajj himself (like walking, tawaf, sa'i). The blind person is different: he can perform the actions himself if guided. So the paralyzed person is like someone who gets lost from the place of Hajj (i.e., cannot reach the location). The dispute is again based on whether ability through another counts. Abu Hanifa counts it; Muhammad does not. The text notes that Abu Yusuf's opinion is not mentioned here; the dispute is between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Key Terms
مقعد (maq'ad): A paralyzed person who cannot walk or move without assistance.
مستطیع بالراحلة (mustati' bi al-rahila): One who has ability through a mount (riding animal) to perform Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because he has no guide.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether a paralyzed person must perform Hajj if he can be carried; Abu Hanifa's view that it is obligatory is often relied upon in later fatwa.

Hajj Not Obligatory for Slaves and Children: Proofs
States ruling and provides three proofs for slaves and children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Hajj is not obligatory upon slaves and children, and explain the three proofs (condition of istita'ah, precedence of servant's right, and hadith) that support this ruling.

Core Idea
Slaves and children are not obligated for Hajj because they lack either legal capacity or the ability to own provisions and a mount.

This passage addresses a fundamental question: who is obligated to perform Hajj? The Hanafi school, based on the Quranic condition of istita'ah (ability) and the Sunnah, clarifies that slaves and prepubescent children are not required to perform Hajj. The author provides three distinct proofs that reinforce this ruling and also explains the general conditions for taklif (legal responsibility) such as sanity and health.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage opens with the core ruling: the obligatory Hajj (fard) is not performed by slaves and children. Understand that this means Hajj is not wajib upon them at all.
This is a negative ruling: it states what is not obligatory.
2
Examine proof 1: financial ability
The first proof (called second proof in the text) is that Hajj requires wealth (zad wa rahila). A slave cannot own property, so he lacks istita'ah. Therefore, Hajj is not obligatory.
The condition of istita'ah is derived from the Quran (3:97): '...and for all people, Hajj to the House is a duty upon those who can afford the journey.'
3
Examine proof 2: master's right
The second proof (third in text) is that performing Hajj would deprive the master of the slave's service over a long period. Since the rights of human beings (servant) take precedence over the rights of Allah, Hajj is not made obligatory.
This is a legal maxim: the rights of people are given priority when they conflict with divine obligations that can be deferred.
4
Examine proof 3: hadith on child's Hajj
The third proof is a hadith stating that if a child performs Hajj ten times, upon reaching puberty he must perform the Hajj of Islam. This shows that pre-puberty Hajj does not fulfill the fard obligation.
The hadith is a strong textual evidence (Sunnah ahad, but authoritative in Hanafi usul).
5
General conditions for obligation
The passage also mentions the conditions of sanity and health for Hajj to be obligatory, which are standard for all acts of worship. Without these, taklif is not valid.
This reinforces that only a sane, healthy, free, adult Muslim who has istita'ah is obliged to perform Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فریضہ حج ادا نہ ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حج بغیر مال کے حاصل نہیں ہو سکتا۔ کیونکہ حج فرض ہونے کے لئے زاد و راحلہ پر قدرت شرط ہے اور غلام زاد و راحلہ کے مالک ہونے پر قادر نہیں ہے اس لئے وہ وجوب حج کا اہل نہ ہو گا۔ تیسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حج کی طویل مدت میں مولی کا حق خدمت فوت ہو جائے گا حالانکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے حق پر بندے کا حق مقدم ہوتا ہے پس بندے کے حق کی حفاظت کے پیش نظر بھی اس پ حج فرض نہیں کیا گیا ہے اور با لگ ہونے کی شرط اس لئے لگائی ہے کہ حدیث میں ہے أَيَّمَا صَبِي حَجَّ عَشْرَ حِجَجٍ ثُمَّ بَلَغَ فَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةُ الإسلام ۔ یعنی جس بچہ نے اس حج کئے پھر وہ بالغ ہو گیا تو اس پر فریضہ حج لا زم ہے یعنی بالغ ہونے سے پہلے جو بچ گئے ہیں ان سے فریضہ ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حج ایک عبادت ہے اور بچوں سے تمام ہی عبادتیں اٹھالی گئی ہیں اس لئے حج بھی بچوں پر فرض نہ ہوگا اور عقل کی شرط اس لئے لگائی ہے کہ بغیر عقل کے مکلف کرنا درست نہیں ہوتا اور تندرست ہونے کی شرط اس لئے لگائی ہے کہ بغیر تندرستی اور صحت کے بجز لازم ہے اور عاجز کسی عبادت کا مکلف نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے اس پر حج بھی فرض نہ ہوگا۔
The obligatory Hajj will not be performed. Second proof: Hajj cannot be obtained without wealth, because for Hajj to be obligatory, power over provision and mount is a condition, and a slave is not capable of owning provision and mount, so he is not qualified for the obligation of Hajj. Third proof: In the long duration of Hajj, the master's right of service will be lost, while the right of the servant takes precedence over the right of Allah, so for the protection of the servant's right, Hajj has not been made obligatory upon him. And the condition of reaching puberty is imposed because the hadith states: 'Any child who performs Hajj ten times, then reaches puberty, upon him is the Hajj of Islam.' Meaning: that child performed these Hajjs, then he reached puberty, so the obligatory Hajj is binding upon him; that is, the Hajjs performed before puberty do not remove the obligation. Second proof: Hajj is a worship, and all worships are lifted from children, so Hajj will not be obligatory upon children. And the condition of sanity is imposed because without sanity, making someone responsible is not correct. And the condition of being healthy is imposed because without health, it is not binding, and the incapable person is not responsible for any worship. Therefore, Hajj will not be obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary. It states that Hajj is not obligatory upon slaves and children (pre-puberty). Three proofs are given: (1) Hajj requires wealth (zad wa rahila), and a slave cannot own property; (2) the master's right to service takes precedence over Allah's right; (3) a hadith shows that a child's Hajj does not fulfill the obligation after puberty. Additionally, sanity and health are required for taklif, so children and the insane/incapable are not obligated. This is a standard Hanafi position based on the Quranic condition of istita'ah and the hadith.

Key Terms
زاد و راحلہ (zād wa rāḥilah): Provisions (food, money) and a mount (riding animal) necessary for the journey to Hajj.
غلام (ghulām): A male slave who is owned by a master and has no legal capacity to own property.
صبی (ṣabī): A child who has not yet reached puberty; not legally responsible (mukallaf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because a slave cannot own provision and mount (zad wa rahila)
C) Because a slave is always sick
D) Because a slave has performed Hajj before

Key Takeaway
Hajj is not obligatory for slaves and children before puberty because they lack the conditions of legal capacity and financial ability, as supported by the hadith and legal reasoning.

Hajj for the Paralyzed: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Hajj for the paralyzed with two qiyas arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi positions on Hajj for the paralyzed and evaluate the two qiyas arguments used.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school has conflicting views on Hajj for the paralyzed: ability through another may or may not suffice.

This passage tackles a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of Hajj for a paralyzed person (maq'ad). Two narrations from Abu Hanifa and the position of Imam Muhammad are presented, each using a different qiyas (analogy). Understanding this dispute requires careful analysis of the conditions of istita'ah (ability) and the nature of personal performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the positions
State the two narrations from Abu Hanifa (Zahir al-Riwayah: not obligatory; from Hasan ibn Ziyad: obligatory) and Imam Muhammad's view (not obligatory).
Note the authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah is the primary transmission.
2
Analyze the qiyas for obligation
The narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad analogizes the paralyzed to one who has a mount (rahila): both are mustati' through an external means. Determine the illa: ability through another.
This qiyas treats the proxy as equivalent to a mount.
3
Analyze the qiyas against obligation
Muhammad analogizes the paralyzed to a lost traveler (dall) who cannot perform without guidance. The blind person is different because he can perform if guided. The illa is personal physical inability.
The key distinction: the blind can still move and act; the paralyzed cannot.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the obligatory view, the paralyzed must send a proxy. Under the non-obligatory view, no obligation exists at all, even to delegate.
This practical difference matters for fatwa.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Al-Hidayah mentions the obligatory narration but the Zahir al-Riwayah is considered stronger. In practice, the mufta bihi is usually the non-obligatory view.
Be aware of both positions for completeness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا المَقْعَدُ فَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّه يَجِبُ لِأَنَّهُ مُسْتَطِيعُ بِغَيْرِهِ فَأَشْبَة الْمُسْتَطِيعَ بِالرَّاحِلَةِ وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّهُ لَا يَجِبُ أَنَّهُ لِأَنَّهُ غَيْرُ قَادِرٍ عَلَى الْأَدَاءِ بِنَفْسِهِ بِخِلَافِ الْأَعْمَى لِأَنَّ لَوَهَدَى يُؤَدِّى بِنَفْسِهِ فَأَشْبَهَ الضَّالَّ عَنْهُ ترجمہ اور رہا اپانچ تو ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ واجب ہے کیونکہ وہ غیر کے ساتھ استطاعت رکھنے والے سے پیس راحلہ کے ساتھ استطاعت رکھنے والے کے مشابہ ہو گیا ہے اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ پانی پر حج واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ بذات خود ادا پر قادر نہیں ہے برخلاف نابینا کے کیونکہ اگر اس کی دستگیری کر دی جائی تو وہ بذات خود ادا کر سکتا ہے تو وہ مقام حج سے بھسکنے والے کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے ظاہر الروایہ کی روایت ہے کہ لئے پانچ مفلوج اور دونوں پاؤں کٹے پر حج واجب نہیں ہے اگر چہ وہ زا دو راحلہ پر قادر ہوں حتی کہ ان پر اپنے مال سے کسی دوسرے کو حج کرانا بھی واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ جب اصل واجب نہیں ہو تو بدل بھی واجب نہ ہوگا اور حسن بن زیاد نے ابو حنیفہ سے روایت کی ہے کہ اپاہج وغیرہ پر حج واجب ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اسی روایت کو ذکر کیا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اپانج دوسرے آدمی کی وجہ سے مستطیع اور صاحب قدرت ہے پس یہ راحلہ کیسا تھ قدرت رکھنے والے کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور راحلہ اس کے ساتھ قدرت رکھنے والے پر حج فرض ہے لہذا اپانچ مستطیع بغیرہ پر بھی حج فرض ہوگا اور امام محمد سے مروی ہی کہ اپانچ پر حج فرض نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ بذات خود اپنے ہاتھ پاؤں سے حج ادا کرنے پر قادر نہیں ہے اس کے برخلاف نابینا کہ اس کی اگر رہبری کر دی جائے تو وہ بذات خود اپنے ہاتھ پاؤں سے ارکان حج ادا کر سکتا ہے پس نابینا آدمی راہ بھٹکے ہوئے کے مانند ہو گیا اور راہ بھٹکے ہوئے کو اگر راہبر، میسر آ جائے تو اس پر حج لازم ہو جاتا ہے پس اسی طرح نابینا کو اگر راہبر مل جائے تو اس پر بھی حج لا زم ہو گا۔
And as for the paralyzed, from Abu Hanifa (it is narrated) that it is obligatory, because he is able through another, so he resembles one able with a mount. And from Muhammad that it is not obligatory, because he is not capable of performing by himself, unlike the blind, because if he is guided, he performs by himself, so he resembles one who has lost the way. Translation: And as for the paralyzed, from Abu Hanifa it is narrated that Hajj is obligatory, because he is able through another, so he resembles one able with a mount. And from Imam Muhammad it is narrated that Hajj is not obligatory upon the paralyzed, because he is not capable of performing by himself, unlike the blind, because if the blind is given guidance, he can perform by himself, so he resembles one who has lost the way. Explanation: The issue: From Imam Abu Hanifa, the Zahir al-Riwayah narration is that Hajj is not obligatory upon the paralyzed, even if they have provision and mount, to the extent that it is not obligatory for them to send someone else to perform Hajj with their wealth, because when the original is not obligatory, the substitute is not obligatory. And Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that Hajj is obligatory upon the paralyzed etc. The author of al-Hidayah mentioned this latter narration. The proof is that the paralyzed is able and powerful through another person, so he resembles one who has power with a mount, and Hajj is fard upon one who has power with a mount; therefore, Hajj will be fard upon the paralyzed who is able through another. And from Imam Muhammad it is narrated that Hajj is not fard upon the paralyzed, because he is not capable of performing the actions of Hajj with his own hands and feet; unlike the blind, because if the blind is guided, he can perform the pillars of Hajj with his own hands and feet. So the blind person is like one who has lost the way, and if one who has lost the way finds a guide, Hajj becomes binding upon him; similarly, if the blind finds a guide, Hajj becomes binding upon him.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Hajj for a paralyzed person (maq'ad). Two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: one (Zahir al-Riwayah) states Hajj is not obligatory upon the paralyzed even if they have means, and they cannot even delegate; the other (from Hasan ibn Ziyad) says it is obligatory because they are mustati' through others, like a person with a mount. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that Hajj is not obligatory because the paralyzed cannot personally perform the actions. The commentary explains the distinction: a blind person can perform if guided, so he is like a lost traveler who must perform Hajj if he finds a guide. The paralyzed cannot perform even with help, so he is not obligated. The text notes that the author of al-Hidayah mentions the narration that makes it obligatory, but the Zahir al-Riwayah is different.

Key Terms
مقعد (maq'ad): A person who is paralyzed, unable to walk or move independently; often used for one who is bedridden or has lost use of limbs.
مستطیع بغیرہ (mustaṭīʿ bi-ghayrihī): One who is able to perform an act through the assistance of another person, rather than by their own independent capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah from Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on Hajj for a paralyzed person who has wealth and can hire someone to perform Hajj for him?
A) Hajj is obligatory, and he must send a proxy
B) Hajj is not obligatory, nor must he send a proxy
C) Hajj is obligatory only if he recovers
D) Hajj is obligatory but he must perform it personally

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on Hajj for the paralyzed hinges on whether personal physical ability is essential or if delegation suffices; the Zahir al-Riwayah adopts the stricter view.

Condition of Istita'ah for Hajj: Provision and Mount
Defines the condition of ability (zad wa rahila) for Hajj obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for Hajj obligation (istita'ah) and apply them to determine when Hajj is obligatory, including the ruling on alternate renting of a mount.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory only when you have enough provision and a mount for the entire journey.

This lesson clarifies the key condition for Hajj obligation: istita'ah (ability). The Hanafi school defines this as having provision (zad) and a mount (rahila) for the entire round trip. We will examine the hadith proof and a critical edge case: what if a person can only afford to share a mount alternately with another?

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Hajj is fard ayn upon every free, adult, sane, healthy Muslim who has istita'ah. The condition for obligation is the ability (istita'ah).
2
Define zad wa rahila
Zad is provision (food, money). Rahila is a mount. For the weak, it means renting one side of a litter (mahmil). For the strong, renting a baggage camel (zamila) plus round-trip expenses.
Ownership is not required; renting suffices.
3
Apply the hadith proof
The Prophet (peace be upon him) defined 'sabil' (means) as provision and mount. This makes them conditions for obligation.
The hadith is ahad, so the ruling is based on zanni evidence.
4
Analyze the alternate sharing scenario
If two persons share one mount alternately (one rides one stage, the other the next), the mount is not available for the entire journey for each. Hence, the condition of istita'ah is not met, and Hajj is not obligatory.
The mount must be continuously available for the whole journey.
5
State the practical ruling
If one cannot afford a mount for the entire journey (even by renting), Hajj is not obligatory. If one can, it is fard ayn.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text

And there is no avoiding power over provision and mount. And that is the amount with which he can rent one side of a litter or a mount for baggage, and the amount of expenses going and coming. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about the means to it, so he said: 'Provision and mount.' And if he can rent alternately, then nothing is upon him, because when they take turns, the mount is not found in the entire journey. Translation: And it is necessary to have power over provision and mount. And that is that he has such wealth that he can rent one side of a litter or a mount for baggage, and he has power over expenses for going and returning. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about the means to it (Hajj), so he said: 'Provision and mount.' And if he has the ability to rent alternately, then nothing is obligatory upon him, because when these two take turns riding, the mount is not found in the entire journey. Explanation: In this passage, the statement about having power over provision and mount is explained. That is, for the obligation of Hajj, power over provision and mount is a condition. Now this power is either by ownership, such that he owns the mount, or by rent, i.e., he has such wealth that he can rent one side of a litter, because a litter has two sides, and one side is sufficient for one rider, or he can rent a mount for baggage (zamila). The detail is that if a person is weak, he should have the ability to rent one side of a litter for himself to ride; if he is strong, he should have the ability to rent a mount for baggage. And he must also have power over expenses for going and returning, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about 'man istata'a ilayhi sabila' and he said: 'That is provision and mount.' And if a person does not have the ability to rent a riding animal for the entire journey, but has the ability to rent on a turn basis, such that two people jointly rent one camel in such a way that one rides one stage and the other rides the next stage, then in this case Hajj will not be obligatory upon him, because when they ride alternately, the mount is not found in the entire journey, whereas for the obligation of Hajj, the arrangement of riding for the entire journey is conditional.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement and expansion on the condition of zad wa rahila (provision and mount) for Hajj. It defines istita'ah as having enough wealth to rent either a place on a litter (for the weak) or a baggage camel (for the strong), plus expenses for the round trip. The primary proof is the hadith: 'The means is provision and mount.' If a person can only afford to share a mount alternately with another (e.g., one rides one stage, the other the next), then Hajj is not obligatory because the mount is not available for the entire journey. This shows the strict Hanafi condition that ability must cover the whole journey, not partially.

Key Terms
زاد و راحلہ (zād wa rāḥilah): Provision (food, money) and a mount (riding animal). The Hanafi definition includes the ability to rent one side of a litter or a baggage camel, plus round-trip expenses.
محمل (maḥmil): A litter or howdah placed on a camel with two sides; one side can be rented for a rider.
زاملہ (zāmilah): A camel used for carrying baggage, ridden by a strong person who can walk alongside or ride atop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) No, because the mount is not available for the entire journey

Hajj is only obligatory when one has provision and a mount for the entire journey; alternate sharing does not fulfill the condition.
