Hajj Obligation for the Paralyzed and Blind
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Hajj obligation for the disabled

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Hajj obligation for a paralyzed person and distinguish it from the ruling for a blind person, citing the Zahir al-Riwayah position and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Personal physical ability is key: a paralyzed person is not obligated even by proxy, but a blind person is obligated if guided.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Hajj obligation for those with severe physical disabilities. The established position distinguishes between one who lacks personal limb movement (paralyzed) and one who merely lacks guidance (blind). Understanding this distinction reveals the Hanafi emphasis on the individual's direct ability to perform the rites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Zahir al-Riwayah position
From Abu Hanifa, the established transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) states that a paralyzed person or one with amputated feet is not obligated to perform Hajj, even if they have financial means and can be carried. They also do not need to send a proxy.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing riwaya
Hasan ibn Ziyad narrates from Abu Hanifa that Hajj is obligatory for the paralyzed person via another person (proxy), analogizing to one who controls a mount.
This riwaya is from the Nawadir, not relied upon.
3
Understand the reasoning for each
Zahir al-Riwayah argues that since the original (personal performance) is impossible, the substitute (proxy) cannot become obligatory. The opposing view says the person is mustati' through another, like a mount owner.
The key difference is whether ability through another suffices.
4
Note Imam Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad holds the same as Zahir al-Riwayah: the paralyzed person lacks personal physical ability, so Hajj is not obligatory.
This strengthens the relied-upon position.
5
Apply the distinction to the blind person
The blind person is different because they can physically perform Hajj with their own limbs if guided. They are analogous to a lost traveler who becomes obligated once a guide is available.
Thus, Hajj is wajib for the blind if they have a guide and means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح مسئلہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے ظاہر الروایہ کی روایت ہے کہ لئے پانچ مفلوج اور دونوں پاؤں کٹے پر حج واجب نہیں ہے اگر چہ وہ زا دو راحلہ پر قادر ہوں حتی کہ ان پر اپنے مال سے کسی دوسرے کو حج کرانا بھی واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ جب اصل واجب نہیں ہو تو بدل بھی واجب نہ ہوگا اور حسن بن زیاد نے ابو حنیفہ سے روایت کی ہے کہ اپاہج وغیرہ پر حج واجب ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اسی روایت کو ذکر کیا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اپانج دوسرے آدمی کی وجہ سے مستطیع اور صاحب قدرت ہے پس یہ راحلہ کیسا تھ قدرت رکھنے والے کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور راحلہ اس کے ساتھ قدرت رکھنے والے پر حج فرض ہے لہذا اپانچ مستطیع بغیرہ پر بھی حج فرض ہوگا اور امام محمد سے مروی ہی کہ اپانچ پر حج فرض نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ بذات خود اپنے ہاتھ پاؤں سے حج ادا کرنے پر قادر نہیں ہے اس کے برخلاف نابینا کہ اس کی اگر رہبری کر دی جائے تو وہ بذات خود اپنے ہاتھ پاؤں سے ارکان حج ادا کر سکتا ہے پس نابینا آدمی راہ بھٹکے ہوئے کے مانند ہو گیا اور راہ بھٹکے ہوئے کو اگر راہبر، میسر آ جائے تو اس پر حج لازم ہو جاتا ہے پس اسی طرح نابینا کو اگر راہبر مل جائے تو اس پر بھی حج لا زم ہو گا۔ زاد و راحلہ پر قدرت شرط ہے
Explanation of the issue: From Imam Abu Hanifa, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, it is narrated that for a paralyzed person and one whose both feet are cut off, Hajj is not obligatory even if they have ability regarding mount and provisions; rather, it is not even obligatory for them to send someone else for Hajj with their wealth, because when the original is not obligatory, the substitute will also not be obligatory. And Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that Hajj is obligatory for a paralyzed person etc. The author of Hidayah mentioned this narration. Evidence: The paralyzed person becomes capable (mustati') and powerful through another person, so he resembles the one who has power over the mount, and Hajj is obligatory on the one who has power over the mount; therefore Hajj becomes obligatory on the paralyzed person through another's capability. And it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that Hajj is not obligatory on the paralyzed person because he himself is not able to perform Hajj with his own hands and feet. Contrary to a blind person: if he is guided, he can perform the rites of Hajj with his own hands and feet. So a blind person is like one who has lost the way, and for one who has lost the way, if a guide becomes available, Hajj becomes incumbent on him. Similarly, for a blind person if a guide is found, Hajj becomes incumbent on him. Ability over provisions and mount is a condition.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage explains an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding who is obligated to perform Hajj. The establishment (Zahir al-Riwayah) from Imam Abu Hanifa states that a person who is completely paralyzed or whose feet are amputated is not obligated to perform Hajj even if they have the financial means and can be carried on a mount. They also do not have to hire someone else to perform Hajj on their behalf. However, a different transmission (riwaya) from Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad (considered Nawadir) says Hajj is obligatory for such a person because they are capable (mustati') through another person, analogous to someone who controls a mount. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds that the paralyzed person is not obligated because they lack personal physical ability. The blind person, on the other hand, is obligated if they can find a guide because they can physically perform the actions of Hajj with their own limbs, similar to a lost traveler who becomes obligated when a guide is available. This shows the principle that personal physical ability to perform the rites is a key factor.

Key Terms
مفلوج (maflūj): A person who is paralyzed, unable to move limbs.
مستطیع (mustaṭīʿ): One who has the legal ability (istita'ah) to perform Hajj, which includes physical and financial capability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah) regarding a paralyzed person who has financial means, what is the ruling on Hajj?
A) Hajj is obligatory on them personally.
B) They must hire someone else to perform Hajj on their behalf.
C) Hajj is not obligatory on them at all.
D) Hajj is obligatory only if they can walk.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, in its relied-upon position, holds that a paralyzed person is not obligated to perform Hajj or send a proxy, while a blind person is obligated if a guide is available.

Condition of Power over Provisions and Mount
Defining istita'ah: provisions, mount, and the case of sharing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of istita'ah for Hajj, cite the hadith proof, and determine when sharing a mount does not satisfy the condition.

Core Idea
Hajj is wajib only if you have full provisions and mount for the entire journey; sharing does not suffice.

The obligation of Hajj is not based on mere physical ability but on financial capacity to obtain provisions and transportation. This lesson examines the Hanafi definition of this capacity, anchored in a prophetic hadith that interprets the Quranic term 'sabil'. We also explore a critical nuance: sharing a mount does not trigger obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
State the two essential components of istita'ah for Hajj according to the Hanafi school: provisions (zad) and a mount (rahila).
2
Define the required quantity
Understand that the required amount is sufficient to hire one side of a mahmil (sedan) or a zamilah (pack camel), plus expenses for the round trip.
This is the minimum threshold for ability.
3
Examine the proof
Recognize the hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) defined 'sabil' (means) as 'az-zad wa ar-rahila' (provisions and mount). This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati' ad-dalala).
4
Analyze the sharing exception
If a person can only afford a share ('uqbah) of a mount by taking turns, this does not constitute full possession because the mount is not available for the entire journey.
The consequence: Hajj is not wajib in this case.
5
Conclude the ruling
When full ability (provisions + mount for the whole trip) is present, Hajj becomes wajib. Otherwise, it is not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ الْقُدْرَةِ عَلَى الزَّادِ وَالرَّاحِلَةِ وَ هُوَ قَدْرُ مَا يَكْتَرى به شقَّ مَحْمَل وأو أس زَامِلَةٍ وقَدْرُ النَّفَقَةِ ذَاهِبًا وَجَانِيًا لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ سُئِلَ عَنِ السَّبِيْلِ إِلَيْهِ فَقَالَ الزَّادُ وَالرَّاحِلَةُ وَإن أمكنه أن يَكْتَرى عَقِبَةً فَلا شَىءَ عَلَيْهِ لَانَّهُمَا إِذَا كَانَا يَتَعَاقَبَان لَمْ تُوجَدِ الرَّاحِلَةُ فِى جَمِيعِ السَّفَرِ
And power over provisions and mount is necessary. And it is an amount sufficient to hire one side of a sedan (mahmil) or the back of a zamilah (pack camel), and the amount of expenses for going and returning, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about the 'means' to it, so he said: 'Provisions and the mount.' And if he is able to hire a turn ('uqbah), then nothing is upon him, because when they take turns, the mount is not found in the entire journey.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage establishes the second major condition for the obligation of Hajj: financial ability to obtain provisions (zad) and a mount (rahila). The definition of ability includes having enough money to hire one side of a mahmil (a camel-borne litter) or to rent a pack camel (zamilah) for luggage, plus the expenses for the round trip. The proof is a hadith in which the Prophet (PBUH) explained the Quranic phrase 'ability to the journey' (istita'ah) as meaning provisions and a mount. An important exception: if a person can only afford to share a mount with another person by taking turns (trading off riding), this does not constitute sufficient ability because the mount is not continuously available throughout the journey. The ruling is that Hajj is not obligatory in such a case.

Key Terms
زاد (zād): Provisions for the journey, including food and other necessities.
راحلة (rāḥilah): A mount suitable for riding, typically a camel.
عقبة (ʿuqbah): A turn or share in the use of a mount when two people share one animal alternately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, what did the Prophet (PBUH) explain as the 'means' (sabil) to Hajj?
A) A healthy body and free time.
B) Provisions and a mount.
C) A companion and a guide.
D) Safety and good weather.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory only when one possesses full provisions and a mount for the entire round trip, as defined by the Prophet's hadith.

Wealth Must Be Surplus to Essentials
Condition for Hajj wealth surplus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which wealth is considered surplus for Hajj and identify which items count as essential needs.

Core Idea
Hajj is only obligatory when your wealth exceeds your primary needs and dependents' expenses.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies a crucial condition for the obligation of Hajj: the wealth used must be surplus to essential needs. It lists dwellings, servants, household goods, and clothing as primary needs, and also requires surplus for dependents' maintenance during the journey. Understanding this principle prevents the common error of assuming any wealth triggers the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses the condition for Hajj to be wajib. Specifically, the wealth must be surplus to essential needs.
Hajj is wajib only when these conditions are met.
2
List the essential needs excluded from wealth calculation
The passage mentions dwelling, servant, household goods, and clothes as primary needs (haja asliyya). These are treated as non-existent for the purpose of Hajj obligation.
These are items one cannot do without.
3
Explain the rationale of primary needs
These items are engaged with the primary need, meaning they are essential for daily life. Therefore, they are not considered part of one's disposable wealth.
The Hanafi school applies this principle broadly.
4
Note the additional condition for dependents
Wealth must also be surplus to the expenditure of dependents (wife, children, etc.) from the time of departure until return.
This ensures that the family is cared for during the Hajj journey.
5
Understand the priority of rights
The passage states that the right of the servant (dependent) takes precedence over the right of Shari'ah (Hajj). This is based on the principle that human obligations precede religious ones when there is a conflict.
This is a key principle in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُشترط أن يَكُونَ فَاضِلا عن المسكن وعَمَّا لَا بُدَّ مِنهُ كَالْخَادِم وَأثَاتِ الْبَيْتِ وَثِيَابِهِ لأَنَّ هَذِهِ الأَشْيَاء مَشْعُولَةُ بالحَاجَةِ الأصْلِيَّةِ وَيُشترط أن يَكُونَ فَاضِلا عَنْ نَفْقَةِ عَيَالِه إِلى حِيْنَ عَوْدِهِ لانَّ النَّفَقَةَ حَقٌّ مُسْتَحَقِّ للمرأة وحق العبدِ مُقَدَّمُ عَلَى حَقَ الشَّرْعِ بِأَمْرِهِ
And it is a condition that (the wealth) be surplus to the dwelling and those things which are indispensable, like the servant, household goods, and his clothes, because these things are engaged with the primary need. And it is a condition that it be surplus to the expenditure of his dependents until his return, because maintenance is an established right for the woman (wife), and the right of Allah's servant takes precedence over the right of Shari'ah by His command.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage specifies that the wealth used for Hajj must be in excess of the essential needs of the person. Essentials include: a dwelling place, a servant (if needed), household goods (like bedding, utensils), and clothing. These are considered primary needs (haja asliyya) and are treated as non-existent for the purpose of Hajj obligation. Additionally, one must have enough surplus to cover the living expenses of their dependents (wife, children, etc.) from the time of departure until return. The reasoning is that the right of human beings (the dependent's nafaqa) is given precedence over the right of Allah (Hajj), based on the Quranic principle that in cases of necessity, Allah permits what is normally forbidden. Thus, ensuring the well-being of family is prioritized.

Key Terms
حاجة أصلية (ḥājah aṣliyyah): Primary need; essential items like dwelling, clothing, etc.
عيال (ʿiyāl): Dependents, including wife, children, and others whom one is obligated to support.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Dwelling house.
B) Servant.
C) Luxury car.
D) Household goods.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is only required when your wealth exceeds your essential living needs and the expenses of your dependents.

People of Makkah: Mount Not Required; Safety Condition Dispute
Special ruling for Makkans and dispute on road safety

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi views on road safety as a condition for Hajj and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
For Makkans, Hajj is wajib without a mount; road safety is a condition, but its role (obligation vs performance) is disputed.

This passage addresses two specific rulings for the people of Makkah regarding the obligation of Hajj. First, the condition of owning a mount (rahila) is waived because they face no extraordinary hardship in reaching the sacred sites. Second, the passage introduces an important intra-Hanafi dispute over whether safety of the road (amn al-ṭarīq) is a condition for the obligation itself or merely for its performance. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for correctly applying the rules of Hajj when travel is dangerous.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
Read the Arabic text and identify that it discusses two distinct points: the mount exemption for Makkans and the necessity of road safety. Note that the second point contains a dispute (ḥīl) and (qīla).
The passage is structured as two legal statements connected by 'wa lā budda'.
2
Understand the mount exemption for Makkans
The passage states that a mount is not a condition of wujūb for residents of Makkah and its surroundings because they face no extra hardship in performing Hajj. Compare this to the obligation of Friday prayer, which also requires no travel.
This ruling is specific to Makkans; non-Makkans require a mount unless they can walk without undue hardship.
3
Analyze the dispute on road safety
The passage presents two views: (1) safety is a condition of wujūb (obligation), so if the road is unsafe, Hajj is not obligatory and no will (waṣiyyah) is required; (2) safety is a condition of adāʾ (performance), so Hajj is obligatory but deferred until it becomes safe. Note the evidence cited for each view.
The first view is narrated from Abu Hanifa; the second relies on the Prophet's definition of istiṭāʿah as only provisions and mount.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical consequence: under the first view, if the road is unsafe, there is no obligation at all, so no will for Hajj is needed. Under the second view, the obligation remains, so one must still make a will for Hajj to be performed after death or when safe.
The difference affects estate planning and whether a person dies with an unfulfilled wajib.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah states that the view making safety a condition of wujūb is narrated from Abu Hanifa and is relied upon (mufta bihi). Thus, in fatwa, this is the operative position.
The authority weight is ẓāhir al-riwāyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ مِنْ شَرْطِ الْوُجُوبِ عَلى أهْلِ مَكَّةَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُمُ الرَّاحِلَةُ لأنَّهُ لا تَلْحَقُهُمُ مُشَقَّةٌ زَائِدَةً فِي الْآدَاءِ فَاشْبَهَ السَّعَى إِلَى الْجُمُعَةِ وَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اَمَنِ الطَّرِيقِ لأنَّ الاِسْتِطَاعَةَ لَا يَثْبُتُ دُونَهُ ثُمَّ قِيلَ هُوَ شَرْطُ الْوُجُوبِ حَتَّى لا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الْإِيْصَاءُ وَهُوَ مَرْوِيٌّ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ قِيْلَ هُوَ شَرُطُ الأدَاءِ دُونَ الْوُجُوبِ لأنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَسَّرَ الْإِسْتِطَاعَةَ بِالزَّادِ وَالرَّاحِلَةِ لَا غَيْرَ
And a mount is not among the conditions of obligation for the people of Makkah and those around them, because no extra hardship in performance affects them, so it resembles going to Friday prayer. And safety of the road is necessary because ability (istita'ah) is not established without it. Then it is said: It is a condition of obligation, such that making a will (for Hajj) is not obligatory on him, and this is narrated from Abu Hanifa. And it is said: It is a condition of performance, not of obligation, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) explained ability as provisions and mount only.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage discusses two special points regarding the obligation of Hajj. First, for residents of Makkah and its surroundings, the condition of owning or hiring a mount (rahila) is waived because the distance to the sacred sites is short and no significant extra hardship is involved. It is compared to the obligation of Friday prayer, which requires no travel. Second, safety of the road (amn al-tariq) is a necessary condition for istita'ah. There is a dispute within the Hanafi school: one position (attributed to Abu Hanifa) holds that safety is a condition for the obligation itself, meaning if the road is unsafe, Hajj is not even required to be performed later or via will. The other position says safety is a condition for the actual performance (ada'), not the obligation; thus if one is unable due to danger, the obligation remains but is deferred. The latter view is based on the fact that the Prophet only mentioned provisions and mount in defining istita'ah, not safety.

Key Terms
امن الطريق (amn al-ṭarīq): Safety of the road from dangers like bandits, wild animals, etc.
الوصية (al-waṣiyyah): Will or testament regarding Hajj to be performed after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is the ruling on a Makkan who cannot perform Hajj because the road is unsafe?
A) Hajj is obligatory but deferred; a will is required.
B) Hajj is not obligatory at all; no will is required.
C) Hajj is obligatory and must be performed regardless.
D) The mount condition is waived, but the road condition is not considered.

Key Takeaway
For a Makkan, the mount is not a condition; but the safety of the road is a condition of obligation per the mufta bihi view, so if it is absent, Hajj is not obligatory and no will is needed.

Surplus Over Residence and Family Nafaqah for Hajj Obligation
Ruling on wealth surplus condition for Hajj obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two surplus conditions for Hajj obligation and explain the legal reasoning (dalil) behind the precedence of family nafaqah.

Core Idea
Hajj is not obligatory unless wealth remains after basic needs and family maintenance are secured.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that for Hajj to be obligatory, one's wealth must be surplus over essential items (hajah asliyyah) like residence, clothing, and servant, and also surplus over the nafaqah (maintenance) of dependents until return. The text from Al-Hidayah establishes this condition and provides a Quranic proof for prioritizing the right of the servant over the right of Shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon. Here, it is the obligation (fard) of Hajj. The ruling: Hajj becomes fard only when certain conditions are met.
The primary ruling is from the Quran and Sunnah; this passage specifies additional financial conditions.
2
Extract the two surplus conditions
Locate the two conditions: (1) wealth must be surplus over residence and necessities (hajah asliyyah), and (2) surplus over the nafaqah of dependents until return from Hajj.
Necessities include servant, household goods, clothing, riding animal, weapons, etc.
3
Understand 'hajah asliyyah'
Grasp the concept of primary need: items essential for basic living are considered non-existent for financial calculations. They are exempt from being counted toward Hajj affordability.
This is a Hanafi legal presumption: what is occupied by necessity is like non-existent.
4
Analyze the proof for nafaqah precedence
The text cites Quran 6:119 to show that under compulsion, Allah permits what is normally forbidden, indicating that the right of the servant (necessity) overrides the right of Shari'ah. Here, the wife's nafaqah is a necessary right, so it takes precedence over the obligation of Hajj.
The dalil is used by qiyas: just as compulsion allows forbidden things, necessity (nafaqah) overrides Hajj obligation.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a person with wealth that covers Hajj expenses but not enough to also leave nafaqah for his family, Hajj is not obligatory because the right of the family takes precedence.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text

وَيُشترط أن يَكُونَ فَاضِلا عن المسكن وعَمَّا لَا بُدَّ مِنهُ كَالْخَادِم وَأثَاتِ الْبَيْتِ وَثِيَابِهِ لأَنَّ هَذِهِ الأَشْيَاء مَشْعُولَةُ بالحَاجَةِ الأصْلِيَّةِ وَيُشترط أن يَكُونَ فَاضِلا عَنْ نَفْقَةٍ عَيَالِه إِلى حِيْنَ عَوْدِهِ لانَّ النَّفَقَةَ حَقٌّ مُسْتَحَقِّ للمرأة وحق العبدِ مُقَدَّمُ عَلَى حَقَ الشَّرْعِ بِأَمْرِهِ
ترجمہ اور شرط ہے کہ یہ مال اس کے مسکن اور ضروریات زندگی سے فاضل ہو جیسے خادم ، اثاث البیت اور کپڑے کیونکہ یہ چیزیں حاجت اصلیہ کے ساتھ مشغول ہیں اور شرط ہے کہ اس کی واپسی تک اسی کی عیال کے نفقہ سے فاضل ہو۔ اس لئے کہ نفقہ عورت کے لئے واجی حق ہے اور بحکم شرع حق عبد حق شرع پر مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح سابق میں گزار ہے کہ وجوب حج کے لئے زاد و راحلہ پر قدرت شرط ہے لیکن اس میں بھی شرط ہے کہ وہ مال جس سے زاد و راحلہ حاصل کرے گا اس کے رہنے کے مکان اور ضروری سامان سے فاضل ہو ضروری سامان جیسے خادم گھر یلو سامان مثلاً بستر فرش کھانے پکانے کا سامان اور اس کے استعمال کے کپڑے سواری کا گھوڑا اور ہتھیار وغیرہ کیونکہ یہ سب چیزیں حاجت اصلیہ کے ساتھ مشغول ہیں اور جو چیز حاجت اصلیہ کے ساتھ مشغول ہو وہ معدوم کے مانند ہوتی ہے، اور یہ مال تا واپسی عیال کے نفقہ سے فاضل ہو کیونکہ بیوی کا نفقہ واجب ہے اور حق العبد شرع پر مقدم ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ قرآن کا ارشاد ہے قَدْ فَصَّلَ لَكُمُ مَا حَرَّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِلَّا مَا اضْطُرِرْتُمْ إِلَيْهِ (الانعام: 19 ) یعنی تمہارے سامنے وہ تمام چیزیں تفصیل سے بیان کر دیں جن کو تم پر حرام کیا ہے مگر یہ کہ تم ان کی طرف مجبور ہو جاؤ دیکھئے اس آیت میں اللہ رب العزت نے بندے کی مجبوری کے پیش نظر حرام چیز کو اس کے لئے مباح کر کے اس کے حق کو اپنے حق پر مقدم کر دیا ہے۔
And it is conditioned that [the wealth] be surplus over the residence and over that which is indispensable, like the servant, household goods, and clothing, because these things are occupied with the primary need. And it is conditioned that it be surplus over the nafaqah of his dependents until his return, because nafaqah is a right entitled to the woman, and the right of the servant takes precedence over the right of the Shari'ah by His command. Translation: And it is a condition that this wealth be surplus over his residence and life necessities, like servant, household goods, and clothing, because these things are occupied with the primary need. And it is a condition that it be surplus over the nafaqah of his dependents until his return, because nafaqah is an obligatory right for the woman, and by the command of Shari'ah, the right of the servant takes precedence over the right of Shari'ah. Explanation: It has passed earlier that for the obligation of Hajj, power over zad and rahila is a condition, but within this there is also a condition that the wealth from which he will obtain zad and rahila be surplus over his residence and necessary goods. Necessary goods like servant, household items such as bed, carpet, cooking utensils, and his clothing, riding horse, and weapons, etc., because all these things are occupied with the primary need, and whatever is occupied with the primary need is like non-existent. And this wealth must be surplus over the nafaqah of his dependents until return, because the wife's nafaqah is obligatory, and the right of the servant takes precedence over Shari'ah, as the Quran says: 'He has detailed for you what He has forbidden to you, except what you are compelled to' (Al-An'am 6:119). That is, He has explained in detail all things that are forbidden to you, except that you are forced to them. See, in this verse, Allah, Lord of Might, due to the servant's compulsion, has made the forbidden thing permissible for him, preferring his right over His own right.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the commentary on Al-Hidayah, establishing the conditions for the obligation of Hajj regarding surplus wealth. The matn states that for Hajj to be obligatory, one must have wealth that is surplus over one's residence, essential items like a servant, household goods, and clothing, because these are occupied by the primary need (hajah asliyyah). The condition also requires surplus over the nafaqah (maintenance) of one's dependents until returning from Hajj, because the wife's nafaqah is a right of Allah's servant that takes precedence over the right of Shari'ah (Hajj). The commentary elaborates that necessary goods include servant, household items, clothing, riding horse, weapons, etc., all considered non-existent for Hajj obligation. The commentary further justifies the precedence of dependents' rights by citing Quran 6:119, where Allah permits forbidden things under compulsion, showing the priority of the servant's need over the divine command. This ruling is a standard Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
حاجت اصلیہ (hajah asliyyah): Primary need: necessary items for basic living such as residence, clothing, servant, etc.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance/sustenance due to dependents (wife, children) that must be provided for during Hajj absence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a person who has enough wealth for Hajj but does not have surplus over the nafaqah of his wife until his return?
A) Hajj is still obligatory because wealth is available.
B) Hajj is not obligatory because the right of the wife takes precedence.
C) Hajj is obligatory but he must also provide nafaqah.
D) Hajj becomes wajib and he must send a proxy.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is only obligatory when wealth is surplus over residence, essential goods, and the nafaqah of dependents until return.

Safety of Route: Condition of Obligation or Performance?
Dispute on whether road safety is for Hajj obligation or performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on whether road safety is a condition for Hajj obligation or performance, and identify the practical consequence concerning bequest.

Core Idea
Road safety's status (obligation vs. performance) determines whether a bequest is needed when danger prevents Hajj.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school and across madhahib: is safety of the road a condition for Hajj to become obligatory, or is it merely a condition for valid performance? The answer affects what a person must do if they cannot travel safely. We will trace the two positions and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Some scholars say road safety is a condition of obligation (shart al-wujub); others say it is a condition of performance (shart al-ada). Name the scholars associated with each.
The first position is narrated from Abu Hanifa (Nawadir), Abu Yusuf, and Imam Shafi'i. The second from Imam Ahmad and is the relied-upon view in Hidayah.
2
Define the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? If a person has means but cannot go due to danger, the first view says no bequest needed; the second says bequest is obligatory.
The passage states the point of dispute clearly: whether bequest is necessary.
3
Examine the proof for the second position
The author of Hidayah presents the Prophet's interpretation of 'sabil' as only zad and rahila. Why does this prove road safety is not a condition of obligation?
The argument: if road safety were a condition, the Prophet would have mentioned it alongside zad and rahila.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi tarjih
Although Abu Hanifa's nawadir view is a condition of obligation, the later relied-upon view in Hidayah is condition of performance. Which one is mufta bihi?
The mufta bihi is the second view (condition of performance), as indicated by the phrase 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' in other contexts.

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ وجوب حج کے لئے راستہ کا پر امن ہونا بھی شرط ہے یعنی اس راستہ ہیں غالب سلامتی اور امن ہو ۔ کیونکہ بغیر امن راہ کے قدرت ثابت نہیں ہو سکتی پھر اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ راستہ کا پر امن ہونا وجوب حج کی شرط ہے یا ادائے حج کی شرط ہے تو بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ راستہ کا مامون ہونا وجوب حج کی شرط ہے۔ یہی حضرت امام صاحب سے نوادر کی روایت ہے اور یہی قواب امام گرفتی اور امام شافعی کا ہے اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ ادائے حج کی شرط ہے یہی امام احمد کا قول ہے شہر اختلاف یہ ہوگا کہ اگر کوئی شخص زاد و راحلہ پر قادر ہو۔ اور تمام شرائط موجود ہوں مگر راستہ پر امن نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ حج نہیں کر سکا یہاں تک کہ قریب المرگ ہو گیا تو ۔ قول اول کے قائلین کے نزدیک اس پر حج کی وصیت کرنا واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ امن راہ کی شرط نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے جب اس پر حج واجب ہی نہیں ہوا تو حج کی وصیت کرنے کا کیا سوال پیدا ہوتا ہے اور قول ثانی کے قائلین کے نزدیک اس پر حج کی وصیت کرنا واجب ہے کیونکہ نفس حج تو اس پر واجب ہو گیا مگر امین راہ نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کو ادا نہ کر سکا اس لئے فریضہ حج کو اپنے ذمہ سے ساقط کرنے کے لئے اپنے مال سے حج کرنے کے لئے کسی کو وصیت کرنا ضروری اور لازم ہے۔ قول ثانی کی دلیل بیان فرماتے ہوئے صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا که رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَیلا کی تغییر فقط زاد و راحلہ کے ساتھ کی ہے اگر امن راہ شرط وجوب ہوتا تو جناب رسول اللہ سے زاد و راحلہ کے ساتھ امن طریق کو بھی ذکر فرماتے ہیں آپ کا زاد و راحلہ کے ساتھ امن طریق کو ذکر نہ کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ امن طریق زاد و راحلہ کی طرح وجوب حج کی شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ ادائے حج کی شرط ہے۔
The author of Al-Hidayah says that for the obligation of Hajj, safety of the road is also a condition, i.e., the road should be predominantly safe and secure. Because without road safety, power (istita'ah) cannot be established. Then there is a difference of opinion: is road safety a condition of obligation or a condition of performance? Some mashayikh said that road being safe is a condition of obligation. This is the narration from Imam Abu Hanifa from nawadir, and this is also the opinion of Imam [Abu] Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i. And some mashayikh said it is a condition of performance; this is the saying of Imam Ahmad. The point of difference will be: if a person has power over zad and rahila and all conditions exist, but due to road not being safe he could not perform Hajj until near death, then according to the first group, making a bequest for Hajj is not obligatory upon him, because since road safety condition was not met, Hajj was not obligatory on him at all. According to the second group, making a bequest for Hajj is obligatory upon him, because the Hajj itself became obligatory on him, but due to lack of road safety he could not perform it, so to remove the obligation from his liability, it is necessary to bequeath from his wealth for someone else to perform Hajj. Presenting the proof of the second group, the author of Al-Hidayah said that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) interpreted the word 'istita'ah' in the verse 'man istata'a ilayhi sabila' only with zad and rahila. If road safety were a condition of obligation, then the Prophet would have mentioned road safety along with zad and rahila. The fact that he did not mention road safety along with zad and rahila is proof that road safety is not a condition of obligation like zad and rahila, but rather a condition of performance.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether safety of the road (amni al-tariq) is a condition for the obligation (wujub) of Hajj or only for its performance (ada'). The author of Al-Hidayah states that road safety is a condition because without it, istita'ah is not established. Then the dispute: one view (narrated from Abu Hanifa in Nawadir, and also from Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i) holds that it is a condition of obligation, so if the road is unsafe, Hajj is not obligatory and no bequest is required. The other view (Imam Ahmad) holds it is a condition of performance, so Hajj is still obligatory, but if one cannot perform due to danger, one must bequeath that someone else perform it from one's wealth. The author of Al-Hidayah leans towards the second view by presenting the proof that the Prophet (ﷺ) interpreted 'sabil' only as zad and rahila, not road safety, implying road safety is not a condition of obligation. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether a bequest is obligatory if one dies without performing Hajj due to road danger. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that road safety is a condition of performance, not obligation, based on the stronger dalil (the Prophet's interpretation).

Key Terms
امن الطریق (amni al-tariq): Safety of the road; predominantly secure and safe from danger.
شرط الوجوب (shart al-wujub): Condition for the obligation; if absent, the act is not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in Al-Hidayah, what must a person do if he has sufficient wealth for Hajj but the road is unsafe and he dies before performing it?
A) Nothing, because Hajj was not obligatory.
B) He must have bequeathed that someone else perform Hajj from his wealth.
C) His heirs must perform Hajj for him.
D) He is excused and no compensation needed.

Key Takeaway
Road safety's classification (condition of obligation vs. performance) determines whether a bequest is obligatory; the Hanafi mufta bihi holds it is a condition of performance.

Woman Requires Mahram or Husband for Hajj
Dispute on necessity of mahram for woman's Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement for a woman's Hajj and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
A woman's Hajj requires a mahram or husband; a group of women does not suffice.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key dispute: can a woman perform Hajj without a mahram when travelling a distance of three days or more? The Hanafi school requires a mahram or husband, while the Shafi'i school permits travel with trustworthy women. We will examine each side's proof and the practical consequence of the difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act (woman performing Hajj) and the condition: she must have a mahram or husband if the journey to Mecca is three days or more.
This is from the matn of Al-Quduri.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a woman may perform Hajj if she travels with a reliable group of women, because security is achieved through the company.
The opponent's reasoning is based on safety in numbers.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argument: a group of trustworthy women provides sufficient security from fitna, so the condition of mahram is not necessary.
This is a qiyas on the permissibility of women travelling together for short distances.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school cites the explicit hadith 'No woman should perform Hajj except with a mahram' (muttafaq alayh). Additionally, the presence of other women does not eliminate fitna; it may even increase it because strangers might join. The prohibition of khalwah (seclusion) with a non-mahram applies even if others are present.
The hadith is the primary dalil; the rational argument about fitna reinforces it.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi says Hajj without mahram is invalid (if distance is travel distance); Shafi'i says it is valid if with trustworthy women. This affects whether the woman must repeat the Hajj.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the requirement of a mahram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيُعْتَبِرُ فِي الْمَرَاةِ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهَا مَحرَمُ تَحْجُ بِهِ أو زَوْجٌ وَلَا يَجُوزُ لَهَا أَنْ تَحُجَّ بِغَيْرِهِمَا إِذَا كَانَ بَيْنَهَا وَ بَيْنَ مكة تلثَةَ أَيَّاهِ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَجُوزُلَهَا الْحَقِّ إِذَا خَرَجَتْ فِي رُفَقَةٍ وَمَعَهَا نِسَاء ثِقَاةً لِحُصُول الأ من بِالمُرَا فَقَةِ وَلَنَا قَولِه عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامِ لَا تَحْجِنَّ إمْرَاةَ إِلَّا وَمَعَهَا مَحْرَمُ وَلِأَنَّهَا بِدُونِ المَحرم يُخَافُ عَلَيْهَا الْفِتْنَةُ وَتَزَدَادُ بِإِبْضِمَادِ غَيْرِهَا إِلَيْهَا وَلِهَذَا تَحْرُمُ الْخَلْوَةُ بِالْأَجْنِيَّةِ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَهَا غَيْرُهَا بِخِلَافٍ مَا إِذَا كَانَ بَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ مَكَة مِن تَلْتَةِ أَيَّامٍ لِأَنَّهُ يُنَاحُ لَهَا الْحُرُوجُ إِلَى مَادُونَ السَّفَرِ بِغَيْرِ مَحْرَ
ترجمہ صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ عورت کے حق میں اس کا انتہا ہو گا کہ عورت کے لئے محرم ہو جس کے ساتھ وہ حج کرے یا اس کا شدہ ساتھ ہو اور عورت کے لئے ان دونوں کے علاوہ کے ساتھ حج کو جانا جائز نہیں سے جبکہ عورت اور مکہ کے درمیان تین دن کی مسافت ہوں۔ اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ عورت کو حج کرنا جائز ہے جبکہ وہ ساتھیوں کے ساتھ نکلے اور ساتھ انتہ عورتیں ہوں کیونکہ رفاقت کی وجہت ان
He said: And for a woman, it is required that she have a mahram with whom she performs Hajj, or a husband. And it is not permissible for her to perform Hajj without them when there is a distance of three days between her and Mecca. And al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible for her to perform Hajj if she goes out in a caravan and with her are trustworthy women, because security is achieved through companionship. And our proof is his saying (peace be upon him): 'No woman should perform Hajj except with a mahram.' And because without a mahram, fitna is feared for her, and it increases by others joining her. For this reason, being alone with a non-mahram is prohibited, even if others are with her. Unlike when there is less than three days between her and Mecca, because it is permitted for her to go out for less than travel distance without a mahram. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said that for a woman, the requirement is that she has a mahram with whom she performs Hajj or her husband. And it is not permissible for her to go for Hajj with anyone else when the distance between her and Mecca is three days. And Imam al-Shafi'i said that Hajj is permissible for her if she goes out with a group and with her are trustworthy women, because security is achieved through companionship.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the necessity of a mahram or husband for a woman performing Hajj. The matn (from Al-Quduri) states that a woman must have a mahram or husband if the distance to Mecca is three days or more. Imam al-Shafi'i permits her to travel with a reliable group of women, citing security through companionship. The Hanafi proof (dalil) is the hadith: 'No woman should perform Hajj except with a mahram' (narrated by Bukhari and Muslim). Additionally, the Hanafi argument is that without a mahram, there is fear of fitna (temptation/chaos), and being alone with a non-mahram is prohibited even if others are present. An exception is made for distances less than three days (i.e., non-travel distance), where she may go without a mahram because the ruling of travel does not apply. This is the Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A male relative whom a woman cannot marry, e.g., father, brother, son, uncle.
رفقة (rufqah): Caravan or group of travelers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for a woman to perform Hajj when the distance to Mecca is three days or more?
A) She can go with a group of trustworthy women.
B) She must have a mahram or husband with her.
C) She can go alone if she is safe.
D) She must send a proxy.

Key Takeaway
A woman's Hajj over travel distance (3 days) requires a mahram or husband; this is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school based on clear hadith.

Safety on the Road: Condition for Hajj Obligation or Performance?
Discussing whether amn al-tariq is a condition for wujub or ada' of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the two Hanafi positions on amn al-tariq as a condition for wujub or ada' of Hajj and apply the mufta bihi to determine the requirement of a will.

Core Idea
Road safety is a condition for Hajj performance, not obligation, according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

This lesson examines a subtle yet consequential difference within the Hanafi school and across madhahib: does the safety of the travel route (amn al-tariq) affect whether Hajj becomes binding (wujub) or only its actual performance (ada')? The answer determines a critical practical ruling: whether a person who cannot perform Hajj due to unsafe roads must make a will for someone else to perform it on his behalf if he dies. We will analyze the two positions, their evidence, and the resolution preferred by the author of al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the specific point of disagreement: Is safety on the road a condition for the obligation (wujub) of Hajj or for its performance (ada')?
2
Identify the two views
First view: condition for wujub (Imam Abu Hanifa in nawadir, Abu Yusuf, Imam al-Shafi'i). Second view: condition for ada' (other Hanafi mashayikh, Imam Ahmad).
The first view is attributed to Abu Hanifa through a rare transmission.
3
Examine the evidence for the second view
The author of Hidayah presents the dalil: the Prophet (SAW) explained 'ability' in the Quranic verse only with provisions and mount, omitting road safety. This silence indicates that road safety is not a condition for obligation.
This is a dalil naqli from the Sunnah, specifically the Prophet's interpretation.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a person has means but the road is unsafe and he dies, the first view says no will is needed (Hajj was never obligatory), while the second view says a will is obligatory (Hajj was obligatory but unperformed).
This shows the real-world impact of the theoretical distinction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author of Hidayah presents the proof for the second view, indicating that it is the relied-upon position in the school: road safety is a condition for performance, not obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ وجوب حج کے لئے راستہ کا پر امن ہونا بھی شرط ہے یعنی اس راستہ ہیں غالب سلامتی اور امن ہو ۔ کیونکہ بغیر امن راہ کے قدرت ثابت نہیں ہو سکتی پھر اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ راستہ کا پر امن ہونا وجوب حج کی شرط ہے یا ادائے حج کی شرط ہے تو بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ راستہ کا مامون ہونا وجوب حج کی شرط ہے۔ یہی حضرت امام صاحب سے نوادر کی روایت ہے اور یہی قواب امام گرفتی اور امام شافعی کا ہے اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ ادائے حج کی شرط ہے یہی امام احمد کا قول ہے شہر اختلاف یہ ہوگا که اگر کوئی شخص زاد و راحلہ پر قادر ہو۔ اور تمام شرائط موجود ہوں مگر راستہ پر امن نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ حج نہیں کر سکا یہاں تک کہ قریب المرگ ہو گیا تو ۔ قول اول کے قائلین کے نزدیک اس پر حج کی وصیت کرنا واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ امن راہ کی شرط نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے جب اس پر حج واجب ہی نہیں ہوا تو حج کی وصیت کرنے کا کیا سوال پیدا ہوتا ہے اور قول ثانی کے قائلین کے نزدیک اس پر حج کی وصیت کرنا واجب ہے کیونکہ نفس حج تو اس پر واجب ہو گیا مگر امین راہ نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کو ادا نہ کر سکا اس لئے فریضہ حج کو اپنے ذمہ سے ساقط کرنے کے لئے اپنے مال سے حج کرنے کے لئے کسی کو وصیت کرنا ضروری اور لازم ہے۔ قول ثانی کی دلیل بیان فرماتے ہوئے صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا كه رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَیلا کی تغییر فقط زاد و راحلہ کے ساتھ کی ہے اگر امن راہ شرط وجوب ہوتا تو جناب رسول اللہ سے زاد و راحلہ کے ساتھ امن طریق کو بھی ذکر فرماتے ہیں آپ کا زاد و راحلہ کے ساتھ امن طریق کو ذکر نہ کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ امن طریق زاد و راحلہ کی طرح وجوب حج کی شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ ادائے حج کی شرط ہے۔
The author of Hidayah says: For the obligation of Hajj, the road being safe is also a condition, meaning that on that road safety and security prevail. Because without road safety, ability cannot be established. Then there is a difference of opinion: is road safety a condition for the obligation of Hajj or for the performance of Hajj? Some scholars said that the road being safe is a condition for the obligation of Hajj. This is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa as a rare transmission (nawadir), and this is also the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i. And some scholars said that it is a condition for the performance of Hajj; this is the saying of Imam Ahmad. The place of difference is this: if a person is capable of provisions and mount, and all conditions are present, but due to the road not being safe he cannot perform Hajj until he nears death, then according to the proponents of the first view, making a will for Hajj is not obligatory upon him because since the condition of road safety was not found, Hajj was not obligatory upon him at all, so no question arises of making a will for Hajj. And according to the proponents of the second view, making a will for Hajj is obligatory upon him because the essence of Hajj became obligatory upon him, but due to lack of road safety he could not perform it, so to discharge the obligation of Hajj from his liability, it is necessary and incumbent to make a will for someone to perform Hajj from his wealth. Presenting the proof for the second view, the author of Hidayah said: The Prophet (SAW) interpreted 'man istata'a ilayhi sabila' only with provisions and mount. If road safety were a condition for obligation, the Prophet would have mentioned road safety along with provisions and mount. His not mentioning road safety along with provisions and mount is evidence that road safety is not like provisions and mount a condition for the obligation of Hajj, but rather a condition for the performance of Hajj.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion probe discussing the condition of safety on the road (amn al-tariq) for Hajj. The author first states that according to the Hidayah, safety on the road is a condition. He then clarifies the difference of opinion: is it a condition for wujub (obligation) or for ada' (performance)? The first view (from some mashayikh, transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa as nawadir, and also held by Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i) holds that it is a condition for obligation. The second view (from other mashayikh and Imam Ahmad) holds that it is a condition for performance. The practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf) is illustrated with a case: a person has means but the road is unsafe, and he nears death. According to the first view, Hajj was never obligatory, so no will is required. According to the second view, Hajj was obligatory but unperformed, so he must make a will for it. The author of Hidayah then presents the proof for the second view: the Prophet (SAW) explained 'ability' in the Quranic verse only as provisions and mount, not mentioning road safety, implying it is not a condition for obligation but for performance. This shows that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the second view, i.e., road safety is a condition for performance, not obligation.

Key Terms
امن راہ (amn al-tariq): Safety and security on the travel route, such that there is no fear of harm.
وجوب حج (wujub al-hajj): The obligation of Hajj becoming binding upon a person.
ادائے حج (ada' al-hajj): The actual performance or fulfillment of the Hajj obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hidayah, if a person has provisions and a mount but the road is unsafe, and he dies before performing Hajj, what must he do?
A) He must make a will for someone to perform Hajj on his behalf.
B) No will is needed because Hajj was never obligatory.
C) He must perform Hajj himself after the road becomes safe.
D) He must pay a penalty.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that amn al-tariq is a condition for the performance (ada') of Hajj, not its obligation (wujub), leading to a will being obligatory if one dies before performing.

Mahram Requirement for Women's Hajj: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Stating the Hanafi ruling on mahram requirement for women's Hajj over three days, with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the requirement of a mahram for women performing Hajj over three days, explain the Shafi'i counterargument, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the prophetic hadith.

Core Idea
A woman must have a mahram or husband for Hajj over three days; safety in numbers does not override the explicit hadith.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a clear legal dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding a woman's obligation to have a mahram when traveling for Hajj. You will examine the respective proofs and understand the practical consequences of each position. The Hanafi school relies on strong textual evidence and the principle of preventing fitna, while the Shafi'i school emphasizes safety in companionship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: a woman must have a mahram or husband to perform Hajj when the distance to Makkah is three days or more.
This is a condition (shart) for the validity of Hajj in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a woman can perform Hajj without a mahram if she travels with a trustworthy group of women, because security is achieved through companionship.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i evidence: the presence of reliable companions (rafaqa) provides safety, making a mahram unnecessary.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Study the Hanafi rebuttal: the Prophet ﷺ explicitly forbade women from traveling three days or more without a mahram. Additionally, fitna increases when women gather, as they are deficient in intellect and religion, and khalwa with a non-mahram is prohibited even if another woman is present.
The hadith from Muslim and Abu Dawud specifically lists permissible escorts (father, son, husband, brother, mahram).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Conclude the practical difference: Hanafi women cannot travel three days or more for Hajj without a mahram; Shafi'i women can if they are in a trustworthy group.
This difference applies to long-distance Hajj travel only.

Source Text

قَالَ وَيُعْتَبِرُ فِي الْمَرَاةِ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهَا مَحرَمُ تَحْجُ بِهِ أو زَوْجٌ وَلَا يَجُوزُ لَهَا أَنْ تَحُجَّ بِغَيْرِهِمَا إِذَا كَانَ بَيْنَهَا وَ بَيْنَ مكة تلثَةَ أَيَّاهِ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَجُوزُلَهَا الْحَقِّ إِذَا خَرَجَتْ فِي رُفَقَةٍ وَمَعَهَا نِسَاء ثِقَاةً لِحُصُول الأ من بِالمُرَا فَقَةِ وَلَنَا قَولِه عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامِ لَا تَحْجِنَّ إمْرَاةَ إِلَّا وَمَعَهَا مَحْرَمُ وَلِأَنَّهَا بِدُونِ المَحرم يُخَافُ عَلَيْهَا الْفِتْنَةُ وَتَزَدَادُ بِإِبْضِمَادِ غَيْرِهَا إِلَيْهَا وَلِهَذَا تَحْرُمُ الْخَلْوَةُ بِالْأَجْنِيَّةِ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَهَا غَيْرُهَا بِخِلَافٍ مَا إِذَا كَانَ بَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ مَكَة مِن تَلْتَةِ أَيَّامٍ لِأَنَّهُ يُنَاحُ لَهَا الْحُرُوجُ إِلَى مَادُونَ السَّفَرِ بِغَيْرِ مَحْرَ ترجمہ صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ عورت کے حق میں اس کا انتہا ہو گا کہ عورت کے لئے محرم ہو جس کے ساتھ وہ حج کرے یا اس کا شدہ ساتھ ہو اور عورت کے لئے ان دونوں کے علاوہ کے ساتھ حج کو جانا جائز نہیں سے جبکہ عورت اور مکہ کے درمیان تین دن کی مسافت ہوں۔ اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ عورت کو حج کرنا جائز ہے جبکہ وہ ساتھیوں کے ساتھ نکلے اور ساتھ انتہ عورتیں ہوں کیونکہ رفاقت کی وجہت ان حاصل ہوا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے ہرگز کوئی عورت حج کو نہ جائے مگر یہ کہ اس کے ساتھ محرم ہو۔ اور اس وجہ سے کہ بغیر محرم کے فتنہ کا خوف ہے اور اس کے علاوہ کو اس کے ساتھ ملنے کی وجہ سے فتنہ میں اضافہ ہوگا اس وجہ سے اجنبیہ عورت کیساتھ خلوت حرام ہے اگر چہ اس کے ساتھ اس کے علاوہ بھی ہو ۔ برخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ اس کے اور مکہ کے درمیان تین دن سے کم مسافت ہو کیونکہ مادون السفر کی طرف بغیر محرم کے لکھنا عورت کے لئے مباح ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عورت کے شہر اور مکتہ المکرمہ کے درمیان اگر تین دن کی مسافت یا اس سے زائد کی دوری ہو تو عورت کو حج کے لئے جانا اس وقت جائز ہوگا جبکہ اس کے ساتھ محرم ہو یا اس کا شوہر اس کے ساتھ ہو ۔ محرم اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کے ساتھ ابدی طور سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہو خواہ قرابت کی وجہ سے خواہ رضاعت کی وجہ سے خواہ مصاہرت ( داماد بیت ) کی وجہ سے لیکن محرم کے لئے شرط ہے کہ وہ عاقل بالغ ہو آزاد ہو یا غلام ہو یا مسلمان ہو اور اگر محرم فاسق ہو یا مجوسی یا بچہ یا مجنون ہو تو اس کا عورت کے ساتھ سفر حج میں ساتھ ہونا معتبر نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ان لوگوں سے مقصد سفر یعنی امن اور حفاظت حاصل نہ ہو سکے گی۔ فاسق سے تو اس لئے کہ اس کے فسق کی وجہ سے وہ عورت خود ہی محفوظ نہ رہ سکے گی اور مجوسی کے مذہب میں چونکہ نکاح محارم حلال سے اس لئے مجوسی کی طرف سے بھی حفاظت ممکن نہیں سے ان دونوں کو محافظ مقرر کرنا تو دودھ کی رکھوالی بلی " کے مانند ہے اور رہا بچہ اور مجنون تو یہ دونوں خود دوسرے کی حفاظت کے محتاج ہیں اس لئے یہ کسی کی کیا حفاظت کر سکتے ہیں حضرت امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ عورت اگر ساتھیوں کے ساتھ نکلی اور اس کی ساتھ ہفتہ اور قابل اعتماد عورتیں ہوں تو اس کے واسطے حج کو جانا جائز ہے اگر چہ اس کے ساتھ محرم اور شوہر نہ ہو ۔ کیونکہ رفاقت کی وجہ سے امن حاصل ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ بغیر محرم کے کوئی عورت حج نہ کرے۔ اور مسلم اور ابو داؤد کی روایت ہے لَا يَحل الأمرا وَتُؤْمِنُ بِاللهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ أَن تُسَافِرَ سَفَراً يَكُونَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ فَصَاعِدَا إِلَّا وَ مَعَهَا أَبُوهَا أَوْ أَبْنَهَا أَوَ زَوَجُهَا أو أخُوهَا أَوْ مَحْرَمُ مِنْهَا یعنی اللہ اور یوم آخرت پر ایمان رکھنے والی عورت کے لئے تین دن یا زیادہ کا سفر کرنا حلال نہیں مگر یہ کہ اس کے ساتھ اس کا باپ ہو یا اس کا بیٹا ہو یا اس کا شوہر ہو یا اس کا بھائی ہو یا اس کا محرم ہو اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ بغیر محرم کے عورت کے لئے سفر کرنا جائز نہیں اگر چہ وہ سفر حج ہو دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بغیر محرم کے عورت پر فتنہ کا اندیشہ ہے اور جب یہ چند ہو جائیں تو چونکہ یہ ناقصات عقل بھی ہیں اور ناقصات دین بھی۔ اس لئے فتنہ میں اضافہ ہوگا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مرد کو اجنبیہ عورت کے ساتھ تنہائی میں جمع ہونا حرام ہے اگر چہ اس عورت کے ساتھ دوسری عورت بھی ہے کیونکہ پہلے ایک ہی فتنہ تھی اور اب دوفتنہ ہو گئیں پس حاصل یہ ہوا کہ بغیر محرم کے تین دن کا سفر عورت کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہاں اگر عورت اور مکہ کے درمیان تین دن سے کم مسافت ہو تو عورت کو بغیر محرم اور بغیر شوہر کے حج کو جانا جائز ہے کیونکہ شریعت اسلام نے بغیر محرم کے مادون السفر کا سفر کرنے کی اجازت دی ہے اور اتنے قلیل عرصہ میں کسی فتنہ کا بھی خوف نہیں ہے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: For a woman, it is required that she have a mahram with whom she performs Hajj, or a husband. And it is not permissible for her to perform Hajj without them when between her and Makkah there is a distance of three days. And al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible for her to perform Hajj when she goes out with a group and with her are trustworthy women, because security is attained through companionship. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (SAW): 'A woman must not perform Hajj except with a mahram.' And because without a mahram, fitna is feared for her, and it increases by the joining of others to her, and for this reason seclusion with a non-mahram woman is prohibited even if others are with her. Unlike when between her and Makkah is less than three days, because she is permitted to go out to a distance less than travel (madoon al-safar) without a mahram. Translation: Sahib Quduri said: For a woman, the condition is that she has a mahram with whom she performs Hajj or her husband, and it is not permissible for her to go for Hajj without them when between her and Makkah is a distance of three days. And Imam Shafi'i said that it is permissible for a woman to perform Hajj when she goes out with companions and with her are trustworthy women, because security is obtained through companionship. And our proof is that the Prophet (SAW) said: 'Never should a woman go for Hajj except that she has a mahram with her.' And because without a mahram there is fear of fitna, and if others join her, fitna increases. For this reason, seclusion with a non-mahram woman is prohibited even if someone else is with her. Contrary to the case when between her and Makkah is less than three days, because going to a distance less than travel without a mahram is permissible for a woman. Explanation of the issue: If between the woman's city and Makkah there is a distance of three days or more, then it is permissible for her to go for Hajj only if she has a mahram or her husband with her. A mahram is one with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, whether due to lineage, breastfeeding, or in-law relationship. But for the mahram, it is a condition that he be sane, adult, free or slave, Muslim. If the mahram is a sinner (fasiq), or a Magian (Majusi), or a child, or insane, then his accompanying the woman on the Hajj journey is not considered valid because from such people, the purpose of the journey—security and protection—cannot be obtained. The fasiq, because due to his transgression, the woman herself will not remain safe. The Magian, because in his religion marriage with close relatives is permissible, so protection from him is also not possible. Appointing these two as protectors is like appointing a cat to guard milk. As for the child and the insane, they themselves need protection from others, so how can they protect anyone? Imam Shafi'i says: If a woman goes out with companions and with her are trustworthy women, then it is permissible for her to go for Hajj even if she does not have a mahram or husband, because security is obtained through companionship. Our proof is that the Prophet (SAW) said that no woman should perform Hajj without a mahram. And narrated by Muslim and Abu Dawud: 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel a journey of three days or more except with her father, her son, her husband, her brother, or her mahram.' That is, a woman believing in Allah and the Last Day is not allowed to travel for three days or more except that with her is her father, her son, her husband, her brother, or her mahram. From this hadith, it is also known that without a mahram, it is not permissible for a woman to travel even if the journey is for Hajj. The second proof is that without a mahram, there is fear of fitna for a woman, and when these women gather, since they are deficient in intellect and religion, fitna will increase. This is why it is prohibited for a man to be alone with a non-mahram woman even if another woman is with her, because previously there was one fitna and now there are two. So the conclusion is that without a mahram, a journey of three days is not permissible for a woman. Yes, if between the woman and Makkah is a distance of less than three days, then it is permissible for her to go for Hajj without a mahram and without a husband, because Islamic law has permitted travel of less than a journey (madoon al-safar) without a mahram, and in such a short time, there is no fear of fitna.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion probe on the requirement of a mahram or husband for a woman performing Hajj. The author begins by quoting al-Quduri's matn that a woman must have a mahram or husband for Hajj when the distance is three days or more. He then presents Imam al-Shafi'i's opposing view, which permits Hajj without a mahram if she is in a trustworthy group of women. The Hanafi response is threefold: (1) the Prophet's hadith 'no woman should perform Hajj except with a mahram', (2) the fear of fitna, which increases when other women join, and (3) the analogy with the prohibition of khalwa (seclusion) with a non-mahram woman even when another woman is present. However, if the distance is less than three days (madoon al-safar), the Hanafi school allows travel without a mahram. The commentary then defines mahram in detail: one to whom marriage is permanently forbidden due to lineage, breastfeeding, or marriage affinity. It also stipulates conditions for a valid mahram: by default, he must be sane, adult, and Muslim, and must be reliable for protection. A fasiq, Magian, child, or insane person cannot serve as a mahram because they cannot provide the intended security. The passage reiterates the Hanafi position and rebuts Shafi'i by citing the hadith from Muslim and Abu Dawud explicitly listing acceptable escorts, and the rational argument that women are deficient in intellect and religion, increasing fitna when they gather. The conclusion is that without a mahram, a woman cannot travel three days or more for Hajj, but she may do so for shorter distances.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A person whom a woman is permanently prohibited from marrying due to blood, breastfeeding, or marriage affinity.
خلوت (khalwa): Seclusion between a man and a non-mahram woman, which is prohibited in the Hanafi school even if another woman is present.
مادون السفر (madoon al-safar): A distance less than that of a legal journey (typically less than three days or approximately 48 miles).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when may a woman perform Hajj without a mahram or husband?
A) When the distance is less than three days.
B) When she is in a trustworthy group of women.
C) When she is over 50 years old.
D) She may never perform Hajj without a mahram.

Key Takeaway
A woman must have a mahram or husband for Hajj when the distance is three days or more; the Shafi'i view allowing trustworthy groups is rejected in the Hanafi school due to explicit hadith and the principle of preventing fitna.

Husband's Right to Prevent Wife from Obligatory Hajj: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on husband's right to prevent wife from obligatory Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether a husband can prevent his wife from obligatory Hajj, explain the Shafi'i counterargument, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Husband cannot prevent obligatory Hajj with a mahram, but can prevent voluntary Hajj.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: does a husband's marital right allow him to prevent his wife from performing obligatory Hajj when she has a mahram? The Hanafi school distinguishes between obligatory and voluntary acts, while Imam al-Shafi'i prioritizes the husband's right. Understanding this dispute clarifies the boundaries between spousal authority and religious obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine what exactly is being disputed: the husband's right to prevent his wife from obligatory Hajj when she has a mahram.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to the text, the husband cannot prevent her because his right does not override obligations. Identify the analogy used (salah and fasting).
3
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues the husband can prevent her because his right (haqq al-'abd) takes precedence over divine rights (haqq Allah).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes voluntary acts from obligatory ones, noting that a vowed Hajj is not initially obligatory. The analogy with salah and fasting is used.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Hanafi, the wife can go if she has a mahram; under Shafi'i, the husband can prevent even obligatory Hajj.

وَإِذَا وَجَدَتْ مَحْرَمًا لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلزَّوْجِ مَنْعَهَا وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِى لَهُ أَنْ يَمْنَعَهَا لأَنَّ فِي الْخُرُوجِ تَفْوِيتُ حَقِّهِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ حَقَّ الزَّوْجِ لَا يَظْهَرُ فِي حَقِّ الْفَرَائِضِ وَالْحَجُّ مِنْهَا حَتَّى لَوْ كَانَ الْحَجُّ نَفَلاً لَهُ أَنْ يَمْنَعَهَا وَلَوْ كَانَ الْمَحْرَمُ فَاسِقاً قَالُوا لَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهَا لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ لَا يَحْصُلُ بِهِ ترجمہ اور جب عورت نے کوئی محرم پایا تو شوہر کو یہ اختیار نہ ہوگا کہ اس کے منع کرے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ شوہر کے لئے اس کو منع کرنا جائز ہے کیونکہ عورت کے حج کو جانے میں اس کے حق کا فوت کرنا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کا حق فرائض کے حق میں ظاہر نہیں ہوتا اور حج بھی انہیں فرائض میں سے ہے حتی کہ اگر حج نفل ہو تو شوہر کو اختیار ہے کہ عورت کو جانے سے روکے اور اگر عورت کا محرم بدکار ہو تو فقہاء نے کہا ہے کہ اس پر حج واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ ایسے محرم کے ہونے سے مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حج کا ارادہ کرنے والی عورت کو اگر محرم میسر ہو تو شوہر کو اختیا نہ ہو گا کہ اس کو فریضہ حج ادا کرنے سے منع کرے اسی کے قائل امام احمد ہیں اور حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ شوہر کو یہ اختیار حاصل ہے امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کے محرم کے ساتھ سفر یہ جانے سے شوہر کا حق فوت ہو جاتا ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ حق العبد حق اللہ پر مقدم ہوتا ہے اس لئے شوہر اپنے حق کی حفاظت کے پیش نظر اس کو حج کا ارادہ کرنے سے منع کر سکتا ہے پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ کسی عورت نے حج کی نذر کی تو شوہر کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ اس کو نذر پوری کرنے سے منع کر دے یہ ہماری دلیل یہ ہی کہ شوہر کا حق فرائض کے حق میں ظاہر نہیں ہوگا چنانچہ شوہر کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ اپنی بیوی کو نماز پڑھنے اور رمضان کے روزے رکھنے سے منع کر دے پس چونکہ حج بھی فرائض دین میں سے ہے اس لئے اس کو ادا کرنے سے منع کرنے کا اختیار بھی شوہر کو حاصل نہ ہو گا ہاں اگر عورت نے نفلی حج کا ارادہ کیا ہے تو شوہر اس کو منع کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ فرائض میں سے نہیں ہے اور اگر عورت کا محرم فاسق ہو یعنی بدکاری میں بیباک ہو تو مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ عورت پر حج فرض نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ایسے محرم کے ہونے سے مقصود حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔
And when she finds a mahram, the husband does not have the right to prevent her. And al-Shafi'i said: He has the right to prevent her because in her going out is elimination of his right. And for us (Hanafi) is that the husband's right does not appear in the rights of obligations, and Hajj is among them. So much so that if Hajj were voluntary, he would have the right to prevent her. And if the mahram is a fasiq (sinful), they said: Hajj is not obligatory upon her because the purpose is not achieved with him. Translation: When a woman finds a mahram, the husband does not have the authority to prevent her. Imam Shafi'i said that the husband is permitted to prevent her because in the woman's going for Hajj, his right is lost. Our proof is that the husband's right does not take precedence over obligatory acts, and Hajj is among them. Even if Hajj were voluntary, he has the right to prevent her. If the mahram is sinful, the jurists said Hajj is not obligatory upon her because the purpose is not achieved. Explanation of the issue: If a woman intending Hajj has a mahram available, the husband does not have the authority to prevent her from performing the obligatory Hajj. Imam Ahmad also holds this. Imam Shafi'i holds that the husband has this authority. Shafi'i's proof is that the husband's right is lost when she travels with a mahram, and it has been stated that the right of the servant (husband) takes precedence over the right of Allah, so the husband can prevent her for the sake of protecting his right. This is similar to a woman who vows to perform Hajj: the husband has the right to prevent her from fulfilling the vow. Our proof is that the husband's right does not appear in the rights of obligations, just as the husband cannot prevent his wife from praying Salah or fasting Ramadan. Since Hajj is also among the obligations of the religion, he also does not have authority to prevent her. However, if the woman intends voluntary Hajj, the husband can prevent her because it is not an obligation. And if the mahram is a fasiq (unrestrained in sin), the mashayikh have said that Hajj is not obligatory upon her because the purpose is not achieved with such a mahram.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on women's Hajj, specifically addressing the husband's right to prevent his wife from going. It presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi position is that when a woman has a valid mahram, her husband cannot prevent her from performing obligatory Hajj, because the husband's rights do not override obligatory acts of worship. The analogy is drawn to salah and fasting: the husband cannot prevent these either. However, for voluntary Hajj, the husband may prevent her. The text also notes that if the mahram is a fasiq (sinful person), according to Hanafi scholars, Hajj is not obligatory on the woman because the purpose of protection is not achieved. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the husband's right (which is a right of a human) takes precedence over the right of Allah, so he can prevent even obligatory Hajj. The Hanafi response distinguishes between obligations and voluntary acts, and emphasizes that the mahram provides necessary protection. The passage also mentions Imam Ahmad's agreement with the Hanafi view on this point.

Key Terms
حق الزوج (haqq al-zawj): The husband's right to prevent his wife from certain acts due to marital rights; does not extend to obligatory acts of worship.
فاسق (fasiq): A sinful person who is not trustworthy; such a mahram does not make Hajj obligatory because he cannot provide safety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, under what condition can a husband prevent his wife from performing Hajj?
A) When the Hajj is obligatory and she has a mahram.
B) When the Hajj is voluntary (nafl).
C) When the distance is less than three days.
D) When she has trustworthy female companions.

Key Takeaway
The husband cannot prevent his wife from obligatory Hajj when she has a trustworthy mahram, but he can prevent voluntary Hajj.

Valid Mahram Conditions and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Conditions and dispute concerning mahram for Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid mahram in Hanafi law and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the mahram is a condition of obligation or performance.

Core Idea
The mahram must be capable of protection; Magians, children, and the insane are invalid, and his expenses are on the woman.

This passage from Al-Hidayah details the qualifications for a mahram accompanying a woman on Hajj. It specifies who cannot serve as a mahram and who bears the expenses. It also introduces an intra-Hanafi difference of opinion on the nature of the mahram condition: is it a condition for the obligation itself (shart al-wujub) or for performance (shart al-ada')?

Guided Path
1
Identify Invalid Mahrams
List the three categories of people who cannot serve as a valid mahram: Magians (due to their permissive beliefs regarding marriage with relatives), children (cannot provide protection), and the insane (also incapable).
The text explicitly states these exceptions.
2
Understand the Expense Rule
Note that the expenses of the mahram (food, transport, etc.) are borne by the woman because she is employing him to help fulfill her obligation.
This is a fixed ruling, not disputed.
3
Relate to Road Safety Dispute
The text compares this dispute to another Hanafi dispute regarding safety of the road (amn al-tariq) – whether it is a condition of obligation or performance.
This parallel helps contextualize the nature of the ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the Dispute
The difference is whether the mahram is a condition of obligation (shart al-wujub) – in which case a woman without a mahram is not obligated to perform Hajj; or a condition of performance (shart al-ada') – in which case she is obligated but must postpone until she can secure a mahram.
The mufta bihi view is that the mahram is a condition of obligation.
5
Apply the Ruling
Given the mufta bihi view, a woman who has no mahram is not required to perform Hajj; if she does have a valid mahram, she must pay his expenses.
This determines whether the obligation exists at all.

لَهَا أَن تَخْرُجَ مَعَ كُلِّ مَحْرِمِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَجُوسِيَا لِأَنَّهُ يَعْتَقِدُ إِبَاحَةَ مِنَاكَحَتِهَا وَلَا عِبْرَةَ بِالصَّبِيِّ وَالْمَجْنُونِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا تَتَأَتَّى مِنْهُمَا الصِّيَانَةُ وَالصَّبِيَّةُ الَّتِي بَلَغَتْ حَدَّ الشَّهَوَةِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْبَالِغَةِ حَتَّى لَا يُسَافِرُ بِهَا مِنْ غَيْرِ مَحْرَمٍ وَ نَفَقَةُ الْمَحْرَمِ عَلَيْهَا لِأَنَّهَا تَتَوَكَّلُ بِهِ إِلَى أَدَاءِ الْحَقِّ وَاخْتَلَفُوا فِى أَنَّ الْمَحْرَمَ شَرَطُ الْوُجُوبِ أَوْ شَرَطُ الْإِدَاءِ عَلَى حَسَبِ اخْتِلَافِهِمْ فِي أُمْنِ الطَّرِيقِ تشریح اور عورت کو ہر محرم کے ساتھ سفر حج کو جانے کی اجازت ہے مگر یہ کہ وہ مجوسی ہو کیونکہ مجوسی اس عورت سے نکاح کو مباح سمجھتا ہے اور بچہ اور مجنون کا اعتبار نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں سے حفاظت حاصل نہیں ہو سکتی اور وہ بچی جو حد شہوت کو پہنچ گئی بالغہ کے مرتبہ میں ہے حتی کہ اس کے ساتھ بغیر محرم کے سفر نہ کرے اور محرم کا نفقہ عورت پر ہے کیونکہ عورت اس کو ادائے حج کا ذریعہ بناتی ہے اور اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ محرم شرط وجوب ہے یا شرط ادا ہے امن طریق میں ان کے اختلاف کے مانند ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ سفر میں عورت کو ہر محرم کے ساتھ نکلنا جائز ہے خواہ وہ آزاد ہو یا غلام ہو۔ مسلمان ہو یا کافر ہو ہاں اگر وہ مجوسی ہو تو اس کے ساتھ نکلنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے کیونکہ مجوس کا یہ عقیدہ ہے کہ ماں بیٹی کے ساتھ بغیر نکاح کے جماع جائز ہے اور دوسرے محارم کے ساتھ نکاح کر کے جماع کرنا جائز ہے پس اس فاسد عقیدہ کی صورت میں عورت خوف فتنہ سے کس طرح محفوظ رہ سکتی ہے اور جب فتنہ
She may go out with every mahram except if he is a Magian, because he believes that marrying her is permissible. And no consideration is given to a child or an insane person because protection cannot be achieved from them. And a girl who has reached the age of desire is like an adult, so she should not travel without a mahram. And the expenses of the mahram are upon her because she is employing him to perform the right. And they differed regarding whether the mahram is a condition of obligation or a condition of performance, according to their difference regarding road safety. Explanation: A woman is permitted to travel for Hajj with every mahram, except if he is a Magian, because the Magian considers marriage with her permissible. A child and an insane person are not considered, because protection cannot be obtained from them. And a girl who has reached the age of desire (i.e., puberty) is like an adult, so she should not travel without a mahram. The expenses of the mahram are upon the woman because she makes him a means to perform the obligation. And there is disagreement among Hanafi scholars as to whether the mahram is a condition of obligation (shart al-wujub) or a condition of performance (shart al-ada'), similar to their disagreement regarding safety of the road. Explanation: In travel, a woman may go out with any mahram whether free or slave, Muslim or disbeliever, except if he is a Magian. This is because the Magian believes it is permissible to have intercourse with his mother and daughter without marriage, and to marry other mahrams. So with such a corrupt belief, how can the woman be safe from fitna?
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage details the conditions for a valid mahram and a dispute within the Hanafi school. It states that a woman may travel with any mahram except a Magian, because Magians consider marriage with close relatives permissible, thus they cannot be trusted for protection. Children and insane persons are also invalid because they cannot provide protection. A girl who has reached puberty is like an adult and requires a mahram. The expenses of the mahram (food, transportation, etc.) are on the woman because she is using him as a means to fulfill her obligation. The passage then mentions an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: whether the mahram is a condition for the obligation itself (shart al-wujub) or for the performance (shart al-ada'). This difference affects whether the Hajj is obligatory on a woman who has no mahram. If it is a condition of obligation, the Hajj is not obligatory on such a woman; if it is a condition of performance, she is still obligated but must postpone until she can secure a mahram. The text notes that this difference parallels the difference regarding safety of the road (amn al-tariq). The passage concludes by reiterating the exception of Magians and the rationale.

Key Terms
شرط الوجوب (shart al-wujub): A condition that must be present for the obligation to exist; if absent, no obligation.
شرط الأداء (shart al-ada'): A condition that must be present for valid performance; if absent, the obligation exists but cannot be performed until condition is met.
مجوسي (majusi): A Magian/Zoroastrian; their belief in allowing marriage with mahrams makes them unsuitable as protectors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is responsible for the expenses of the mahram during the woman's Hajj journey?
A) The mahram himself.
B) The woman.
C) The woman's husband if she is married.
D) The state treasury (Bayt al-Mal).

Key Takeaway
The mahram must be a capable adult Muslim (or at least not Magian), and his expenses are on the woman; the mahram condition is a shart al-wujub in the preferred Hanafi view, meaning no obligation without a mahram.
