Conditions for a Woman's Mahram in Hajj Travel
Rulings on valid mahram: not Magian, child, insane; girl at puberty; expenses; condition of wujub vs ada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid mahram in a woman's Hajj travel and distinguish between the two positions on whether mahram is a condition of obligation or performance.

Core Idea
A woman's mahram must be capable of protection: Magian, child, and insane are invalid; a girl at the age of desire requires one.

This passage from Al-Hidayah outlines essential qualifications for a woman's mahram when traveling for Hajj. It clarifies who can serve as a mahram, how a pre-pubescent girl is treated, and who bears the mahram's expenses. It also addresses a key intra-Hanafi difference: whether the mahram is a prerequisite for the obligation of Hajj itself or only for its performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its exceptions
Read the opening statement: a woman may travel with any mahram except a Magian. Note the general rule and the exception.
The ruling is permissive with a specific prohibition.
2
Analyze the case of the Magian mahram
Understand why a Magian is invalid: because he believes in the permissibility of incest, negating the protective purpose of mahram.
The reasoning is based on belief, not just action.
3
Examine the child and insane mahram
Note that a child or insane person cannot provide protection, so they are not valid mahrams regardless of relation.
Protection (sayanah) is the operative cause.
4
Understand the girl at the age of desire
A girl who has not reached puberty but has reached the age of desire is treated as an adult for the purpose of needing a mahram.
Even if Hajj is not obligatory on her, travel requires a mahram.
5
Distinguish between shart al-wujub and shart al-ada
The passage presents an ikhtilaf: some mashayikh consider mahram a condition of obligation, others a condition of performance. Compare the practical consequences.
The thamarah (practical result) concerns the woman's duty to make a will for badal Hajj.

ہو ہاں اگر وہ مجوسی ہو تو اس کے ساتھ نکلنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے کیونکہ مجوس کا یہ عقیدہ ہے کہ ماں بیٹی کے ساتھ بغیر نکاح کے جماع جائز ہے اور دوسرے محارم کے ساتھ نکاح کر کے جماع کرنا جائز ہے پس اس فاسد عقید : ن صورت میں عورت خوف فتنہ سے کس طرح محفوظ رہ سکتی ہے اور جب فتنہ سے محفوظ نہیں رہ سکتی تو مجوس محرم کی معیت میں بھی سفر کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا اور محرم ہونے میں نابالغ بچہ اور مجنون کا بھی اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں سے عورت کو حفاظت حاصل نہیں ہو سکتی اور جب حفاظت حاصل نہیں ہو سکتی تو ان کی معیت سے کیا فائدہ ہوگا۔ اور جو بچی بالغ نہ ہومگر حد شہوت کو پہنچ گئی ہوتو وہ بالغہ کے مرتبہ میں ہے حتی کہ اس کو بغیر محرم کے سفر کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا اگر چہ اس بچی پر حج فرض نہیں ہے رہا یہ کہ رفیق سفر محرم کا نفقہ کس پر واجب ہے تو صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ محرم کا نفقہ اس عورت پر ہے جس نے اس کو اپنا رفیق سفر بنایا باید ہے کیونکہ عورت ہی نے اس کو ادائے حج کا ذریعہ بنایا ہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کے حق میں زاد وراحلہ کی قدرت میں یہ بھی شامل سے کہ محترم کے نفقہ کی قدرت بھی ہو۔ مشائخ کا اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ محرم کا ہونا وجوب حج کی شرط ہے یا ادائے حج کی شرط ہے اس میں وہی اختلاف ہے جو امن راہ کے سلسلہ میں گذر چکا ہے ثمرہ اختلاف یہ ہے کہ جن حضرات کے نزدیک محرم کا ہونا وجوب حج کی شرط ہے ان کے نزدیک مالدار عورت اگر محرم نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے حج نہ کر سکی تو مرتے وقت اپنے مال سے حج کرانے کی وصیت کرنا واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس پر حج فرض ہی نہیں ہوا تو پھر وصیت کیسی اور جو حضرات ادائے حج کی شرط کہتے ہیں ان کے نزدیک اس عورت پر وصیت کرنا واجب ہوا کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک اس پر حج تو فرض ہو گیا ہے مگر محرم نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ادا نہیں کر سکی تو اس فریضہ حج کو اپنے ذمہ سے ساقط کرنے کے لئے یہ وصیت کرنا واجب ہوگا کہ میرے مال سے کسی دوسرے کو حج بدل کرا دیا جائے اگر اس نے یہ وصیت نہ کی تو گنہ گار ہوگی۔
Ruling on going for Hajj with a Magian child or a mad mahram. She may go out with every mahram except if he is a Magian, because he considers his marriage to her permissible. And no consideration is given to a child or a madman because protection cannot be obtained from them. And a girl who has reached the age of desire is like an adult such that she may not travel without a mahram. And the expenses of the mahram are upon her because she appoints him for the performance of the duty. And they differed as to whether the mahram is a condition of obligation or a condition of performance, according to their difference regarding safety of the road. Elaboration: A woman is permitted to travel for Hajj with every mahram except a Magian, because a Magian considers marriage with her permissible. A child and a madman are not taken into account because protection cannot be obtained from them. A girl who has not reached puberty but has reached the age of desire is like an adult; she may not travel without a mahram even if Hajj is not obligatory upon her. As for the expenses of the mahram, the author of Al-Hidayah said that the mahram's expenses are upon the woman who takes him as a travel companion, because she makes him a means to perform Hajj. This shows that the woman's ability (power) regarding provisions and mount includes ability to provide for the mahram's expenses. The mashayikh differ whether the presence of a mahram is a condition for the obligation of Hajj or a condition for its performance. This is the same difference as that regarding safety of the road. The consequence of the difference is that according to those who say it is a condition of obligation, a wealthy woman who cannot perform Hajj due to lack of a mahram is not obliged to make a will (wasiyyah) to have Hajj performed on her behalf from her wealth, because Hajj was never obligatory upon her. According to those who say it is a condition of performance, she is obliged to make a will, because Hajj became obligatory but she could not perform it due to lack of mahram; to discharge her obligation, she must will that someone else perform Hajj on her behalf with her wealth; if she does not, she is sinful.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage provides detailed conditions for a woman's mahram when traveling for Hajj. The Arabic matn establishes that a woman may travel with any mahram except a Magian, because Magians consider marriage to close relatives permissible, negating the protective purpose of mahram. A child or insane person is invalid as protection cannot be expected. A girl who has reached the age of desire (shahwah) is treated as an adult regarding the need for a mahram, even if Hajj is not obligatory for her. The mahram's expenses are the woman's responsibility since she appoints him. The passage then discusses an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf: is the mahram a condition of wujub (obligation) or ada (performance)? This mirrors the ikhtilaf regarding security of the road. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that if a mahram is a condition of wujub, a woman not having a mahram need not make a will for badal Hajj; if a condition of ada, she must. The text aligns with the Hanafi position that mahram is a condition of ada.

Key Terms
مجوسی (majusi): A Magian (Zoroastrian) who does not observe Islamic prohibitions on marriage to mahrams.
حد الشهوة (hadd al-shahwah): The age at which a girl becomes sexually desirable, typically around puberty.
شرط الوجوب (shart al-wujub): A condition that must exist for the act to be obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a wealthy woman has no mahram to perform Hajj, what is her obligation?
A) Hajj is not obligatory at all, and no will is needed.
B) She must make a will to have Hajj performed on her behalf.
C) She must go alone.
D) She must find a mahram, even if it delays Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that mahram is a condition of performance, so a woman without a mahram must make a will for badal Hajj.

Child's or Slave's Hajj After Capacity: Nafl, Not Fard
Ruling with proof: Child's or slave's Hajj after capacity remains nafl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a child's or slave's Hajj after attaining capacity fulfills the obligatory Hajj and explain the distinction between ihram and wudu.

Core Idea
A Hajj begun before capacity is nafl and cannot become fard because ihram fixes the nature at its start.

You might think that once a child becomes baligh during Hajj, the ongoing Hajj should count as obligatory. But the Hanafi school rules otherwise. Let's explore why the intention at ihram is decisive and how this case differs from wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine that the act is the Hajj performed by a child/slave after attaining capacity during the rituals. The ruling is that it does not suffice for the obligatory Hajj.
The Hajj counts as nafl even if the pilgrim intended fard.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is the principle that the intention at ihram determines the type of Hajj. Since at the time of ihram the person was not obligated, the ihram was contracted for nafl.
The text states: 'li-anna ihramahuma in'aqada li-ada' al-nafl' – because their ihram was contracted for nafl.
3
Analyze the objection via qiyas
The text raises an analogy with wudu: why can't ihram be like wudu, which if made before puberty can be used for prayer after puberty?
Wudu is a separate prerequisite; ihram is the first act of Hajj.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes: ihram includes niyyah that fixes the nature of the Hajj at the start, and no new niyyah is needed later. In contrast, wudu is independent of the prayer's intention.
Thus the analogy fails because the illa (effective cause) differs.
5
Conclude the thamarah (practical consequence)
The child/slave must perform a separate Hajj after attaining capacity if they have the means. The first Hajj remains nafl and earns reward but does not fulfill the obligation.
This ruling is consensus (muttafaq alayh) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بچه احرام باندھنے کے بعد بالغ ہو جائے اور غلام آزاد ہو جائے کیا فرض حج ادا ہو جائے گا وَإِذَا بَلَعَ الصَّبِيُّ بَعْدَ مَا أَحْرَمَ أَوْ أَعْتِقَ الْعَبْدُ فَمَضَيَا لَمْ يَجُرُهُمَا عَنْ حَجَّةِ الْإِسْلَامِ لِأَنَّ احْرَامَهُمَا انْعَقَدَ لِأَدَاءِ النَّقْلِ فَلَا يُنْقَلِبُ لأدَاءِ الفَرضِ
ترجمہ اور اگر احرام باندھنے کے بعد بچہ بالغ ہو گیا یا غلام آزاد ہو گیا پس دونوں نے حج پورا کر لیا تو ان دونوں کو فریضہ حج سے کافی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ان دونوں کا احترام اوائل کے لئے منعقد ہوا ہے تو وہ بدل کر وائے فرض کے لئے نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح مسئلہ بیدی کہ اگر نا بالغ بچہ احرام باندھنے کے بعد بالغ ہوا یا غلام احرام باندھنے کے بعد آزاد ہوا پھر ان دونوں نے ارکان حج پورے کر لئے تو فریضہ حج ادا نہیں ہو گا بلکہ ان کو اگر زاد و راحلہ کی قدرت ہو تو ہر ایک پر فریضہ حج ادا کرنا لازم ہوگا کیونکہ ان دونوں نے احرام حج نفل کے واسطے باندھا تھا تو یہ بدل کر ادائے فرض کے لئے نہیں ہوگا پس اس احرام سے حج نفل ہی ادا ہو گا فرض ادا کرنے کے لئے آئندہ سفر کرنا پڑیگا یہاں ایک سوال ہو سکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ حج میں احترام شرط ہے جیسے نماز کے لئے وضو شرط ہے اور بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس وضو سے نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے جو بالغ ہونے سے پہلے کیا تھا لیکن یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ وہ عمر کے ساتھہ بالغ ہوا ہو کیونکہ اگر احتلام سے بالغ ہونا معلوم ہوا ہے تو اس کا وضو ہی ٹوٹ گیا بہر حال جس طرح اس وضو سے فرض نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے جو بالغ ہونے سے پہلے کیا تھا اسی طرح اس احترام سے فریضہ حج ادا کرنا جائز ہونا چاہئے جو احرام بالغ ہونے سے پہلے باندھا گیا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہمارے سے فریضہ ہونا نزد یک احرام نیت سے متحقق ہوتا ہے اور احرام باندھتے ہی افعال حج شروع ہو گئے افعال حج شروع کرنے کے لئے کسی نئی نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس کے برخلاف وضو کہ وہ نماز شروع کرنے سے پہلے تقف بجاتا ہے حاصل یہ کہ احرام اور افعال حج شروع کرنے کے درمیان کوئی پہلے
If a child becomes baligh after he has entered ihram, or a slave is freed, and then they complete (the Hajj), it will not suffice them for the Hajj of Islam because their ihram was contracted for the performance of nafl (supererogatory), so it cannot be converted to the performance of fard (obligatory). Translation: And if after entering ihram, a child becomes baligh or a slave is freed, and then both complete the Hajj, it will not suffice for the obligatory Hajj, because their ihram was contracted for nafl, so it will not convert to fard. Elaboration: The scenario is that if a minor child enters ihram and then becomes baligh, or a slave enters ihram and then is freed, and then both complete the pillars of Hajj, the obligatory Hajj is not fulfilled. Rather, if they have the ability (provisions and mount), each must perform the obligatory Hajj, because they entered ihram for nafl Hajj. So it will not convert to fard. Only a nafl Hajj will be performed; for the fard they must travel again. Here a question may arise: In Hajj, ihram is a condition, just as wudu is a condition for prayer. And after becoming baligh, it is permissible to pray with the wudu made before baligh, provided he attained puberty by age (since if by wet dream, his wudu is nullified). Similarly, one might think that the ihram made before baligh should suffice for fard Hajj. The answer is: In our view, the intention (niyyah) at the time of ihram determines whether it is fard or nafl. At the moment of ihram, the actions of Hajj begin; no new intention is needed after that. In contrast, wudu is separate from the prayer; it is performed before prayer. The summary is that there is a gap between ihram and the start of Hajj actions? [cut off]
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on whether Hajj performed by a child who attains puberty during the pilgrimage, or a slave who is freed, fulfills the obligatory Hajj. The matn states it does not, because their ihram was contracted for nafl (since they were not obligated at that time). The ruling is based on the fact that ihram is the beginning of Hajj acts, and the niyyah at ihram determines the nature. Once ihram is made for nafl, it cannot be changed to fard mid-course. The commentary addresses an objection: why can't it be like wudu, which, if made before puberty, can be used for prayer after puberty? The distinction is that wudu is a separate prerequisite done before prayer, whereas ihram is itself the first act of Hajj, and the intention (niyyah) is fixed at that point. Therefore, the Hajj performed remains nafl, and they must perform another Hajj for fard if they are capable.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration entered by a pilgrim with the intention of Hajj, involving specific prohibitions.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory (voluntary) act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A 12-year-old boy enters ihram for Hajj. During the journey, he turns 13 and becomes baligh. He completes all rituals. According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of this Hajj?
A) It fulfills his obligatory Hajj.
B) It counts as a nafl Hajj; he must perform obligatory Hajj later.
C) It is invalid and he must repeat it.
D) It counts only if he made intention for fard at ihram.

Key Takeaway
The intention at ihram determines whether Hajj is fard or nafl; capacity attained later does not convert it.

Mahram as Condition for Woman's Hajj: Wujub vs Ada
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahram condition for Hajj obligation vs performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a mahram is a condition for the obligation (wujub) or performance (ada) of Hajj for a woman, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah) of each view.

Core Idea
The presence of a mahram determines whether Hajj is obligatory at all or merely deferred — the ikhtilaf changes the need for a wasiyyah.

A woman's obligation to perform Hajj is contingent on her ability to secure a mahram companion. But Hanafi scholars differ on whether the mahram is needed for the very obligation of Hajj or for its performance. This seemingly technical distinction has a direct practical consequence: does a woman who cannot find a mahram need to make a will for a substitute Hajj? This lesson unpacks the dispute and its thamarah.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed ruling
Start with the basic rule: a woman must travel with a mahram for Hajj; without it, travel is impermissible.
2
Identify the point of ikhtilaf
The mashayikh differ: is the mahram a condition for the obligation (wujub) of Hajj or for its performance (ada)?
3
Trace the basis of the ikhtilaf
The dispute is analogous to the earlier discussion on safety of the road. Both sides use the same analogy but emphasize different aspects.
4
Describe the thamarah al-khilaf
If mahram is for wujub, Hajj is not obligatory, so no wasiyyah needed. If for ada, Hajj is obligatory but deferred, so wasiyyah is wajib.
5
Note the absence of tarjih
The text presents both views without preponderance; the student must recognize that this ikhtilaf is unresolved here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کتاب الحج سے محفوظ نہیں رہ سکتی تو مجوس محرم کی معیت میں بھی سفر کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا اور محرم ہونے میں نابالغ بچہ اور مجنون کا بھی اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں سے عورت کو حفاظت حاصل نہیں ہو سکتی اور جب حفاظت حاصل نہیں ہو سکتی تو ان کی معیت سے کیا فائدہ ہوگا۔ اور جو بچی بالغ نہ ہومگر حد شہوت کو پہنچ گئی ہوتو وہ بالغہ کے مرتبہ میں ہے حتی کہ اس کو بغیر محرم کے سفر کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا اگر چہ اس بچی پر حج فرض نہیں ہے رہا یہ کہ رفیق سفر محرم کا نفقہ کس پر واجب ہے تو صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ محرم کا نفقہ اس عورت پر ہے جس نے اس کو اپنا رفیق سفر بنایا ہے باید ہے کیونکہ عورت ہی نے اس کو ادائے حج کا ذریعہ بنایا ہے اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کے حق میں زاد وراحلہ کی قدرت میں یہ بھی شامل سے کہ محرم کے نفقہ کی قدرت بھی ہو۔ مشائخ کا اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ محرم کا ہونا وجوب حج کی شرط ہے یا ادائے حج کی شرط ہے اس میں وہی اختلاف ہے جو امن راہ کے سلسلہ میں گذر چکا ہے ثمرہ اختلاف یہ ہے کہ جن حضرات کے نزدیک محرم کا ہونا وجوب حج کی شرط ہے ان کے نزدیک مالدار عورت اگر محرم نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے حج نہ کر سکی تو مرتے وقت اپنے مال سے حج کرانے کی وصیت کرنا واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس پر حج فرض ہی نہیں ہوا تو پھر وصیت کیسی اور جو حضرات ادائے حج کی شرط کہتے ہیں ان کے نزدیک اس عورت پر وصیت کرنا واجب ہوا کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک اس پر حج تو فرض ہو گیا ہے مگر محرم نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ادا نہیں کر سکی تو اس فریضہ حج کو اپنے ذمہ سے ساقط کرنے کے لئے یہ وصیت کرنا واجب ہوگا کہ میرے مال سے کسی دوسرے کو حج بدل کرا دیا جائے اگر اس نے یہ وصیت نہ کی تو گنہ گار ہوگی۔
Travel cannot be safe without a mahram; therefore travel with a Magian mahram is also not permissible. In being a mahram, a minor child and an insane person are not considered because protection for the woman cannot be obtained from them, and when protection cannot be obtained, what benefit is there in their company? A girl who is not adult but has reached the age of desire is in the rank of an adult, so much so that traveling without a mahram is not permissible for her, even though Hajj is not obligatory upon her. As for upon whom the expenses of the mahram travel companion are obligatory, the author of Hidayah said: The mahram's expenses are upon the woman who made him her travel companion, because the woman made him a means for performing Hajj. From this it is understood that in the woman's ability to afford provisions and mount, it also includes the ability to afford the mahram's expenses. The mashayikh have an ikhtilaf about whether the existence of a mahram is a condition for the obligation of Hajj or for the performance of Hajj. This ikhtilaf is the same as that which passed regarding safety of the road. The consequence of the ikhtilaf is: according to those who hold that mahram is a condition for wujub, a wealthy woman who could not perform Hajj due to lack of a mahram would not be obliged to make a will (wasiyyah) to have Hajj performed from her wealth after her death, because Hajj was not obligatory upon her. And according to those who say it is a condition for ada, she is obliged to make a will, because according to them Hajj was obligatory upon her but she could not perform it due to lack of a mahram, so to discharge this obligation from her liability, it is wajib to make a will that someone else be sent as a badal to perform Hajj from her wealth. If she does not make this will, she will be sinful.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Hidayah addresses the conditions for a woman's travel for Hajj. It first states that a mahram is required for the safety of the woman, and that a non-Muslim (Magian) does not qualify as a mahram. A minor or insane person also does not qualify because they cannot provide protection. A girl who has reached the age of desire (bulugh al-shahwah) is treated as an adult in this ruling even if not physically adult. The passage then discusses the nafaqa of the mahram: the woman must bear his expenses as she benefits from his companionship. Finally, it presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf among the mashayikh (later scholars) regarding whether the mahram is a condition for the obligation (wujub) of Hajj or for its performance (ada). The practical difference (thamarah) is in the ruling on wasiyyah: if mahram is a condition for wujub, no wasiyyah is needed; if for ada, she must make a will to have Hajj performed on her behalf. This ikhtilaf parallels the earlier discussion on safety of the road. The text does not give a definitive tarjih.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A male relative whom a woman is permanently prohibited from marrying (e.g., father, brother, son), and with whom she may travel.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance expenses, here referring to the expenses of the mahram during travel.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation, the point at which Hajj becomes binding upon a person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mashayikh who hold that mahram is a condition for wujub, what is the ruling on a wealthy woman who cannot find a mahram?
A) She must make a wasiyyah to have Hajj performed on her behalf.
B) She is not required to make any wasiyyah because Hajj was not obligatory on her.
C) She must perform Hajj even without a mahram.
D) She must send a deputy with a mahram.

Key Takeaway
The existence of a mahram is required for a woman's Hajj travel, but Hanafi scholars differ on whether it affects the obligation (wujub) or only the performance (ada), with practical consequences for making a will.

Hajj Before Obligation Does Not Fulfill Hajjat al-Islam
Ruling on whether pre-obligation Hajj suffices for fard after status change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Hajj performed by a child or slave before obligation and explain why the analogy with wudu is invalid.

Core Idea
A nafl act cannot become fard retroactively because intention binds the act from its start.

This lesson examines a key principle in Hanafi fiqh: the intent at the inception of an act determines its legal nature. A child or slave who performs Hajj before becoming legally obligated does so as a nafl act; even if they become obligated during the journey, that Hajj does not become fard. We will explore the ruling, its proof, and a common objection based on analogy with wudu.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and the case
Identify the two scenarios: a child attaining puberty after ihram, and a slave being freed after ihram. The ruling is that their completed Hajj does not suffice for Hajjat al-Islam (the obligatory Hajj).
The Hajj is valid as nafl but does not fulfill the fard obligation.
2
Identify the proof: the nature of ihram intention
The Hanafi position is based on the fact that the intention at the time of ihram determines the nature of the Hajj. Since the child and slave were not obligated at that moment, their ihram was for nafl, and it cannot change to fard later.
The acts of Hajj begin immediately upon ihram; no new intention can alter the character of an already commenced act.
3
Examine the qiyas objection with wudu
Consider the objection: just as wudu performed before adulthood can be used for fard salah after adulthood, why can't ihram performed before obligation serve for fard Hajj?
This analogy seems plausible on the surface.
4
Analyze the distinction (time gap)
The key difference is the presence of a time gap. Between wudu and salah, there is a clear time gap allowing a new intention for the fard act. But in Hajj, the acts begin immediately with ihram—there is no gap. Therefore, the qiyas is invalid.
The contrast with the child who starts salah immediately after wudu and becomes adult during it: even then, the salah remains nafl.

Source Text

نماز کے لئے وضو شرط ہے اور بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس وضو سے نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے جو بالغ ہونے سے پہلے کیا تھا لیکن یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ وہ عمر کے ساتھہ بالغ ہوا ہو کیونکہ اگر احتلام سے بالغ ہونا معلوم ہوا ہے تو اس کا وضو ہی ٹوٹ گیا بہر حال جس طرح اس وضو سے فرض نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے جو بالغ ہونے سے پہلے کیا تھا اسی طرح اس احرام سے فریضہ حج ادا کرنا جائز ہونا چاہئے جو احرام بالغ ہونے سے پہلے باندھا گیا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک حج کا فریضہ ہونا احرام کی نیت سے متحقق ہوتا ہے اور احرام باندھتے ہی افعال حج شروع ہو گئے، افعال حج شروع کرنے کے لئے کسی نئی نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف وضو کہ وہ نماز فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے ایک کو دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگر بچہ نے وضو کرتے ہی نماز شروع کر دی اور پھر وہ عمر کے ذریعہ بالغ ہو گیا اور اس نے نماز کے فرض ہونے کی نیت کر لی تو یہ نماز بدل کر فرض نہ ہو گی۔ پس اسی طرح جب بچہ نے احرام باندھ کر حج نفل شروع کر دیا پھر بالغ ہوا اور اس نے اس حج کے فرض ہونے کی نیت کی تو یہ بدل کر فرض نہ ہوگا۔
The child becomes adult after putting on ihram, and the slave becomes free: will the obligatory Hajj be performed? And if the child attains puberty after putting on ihram, or the slave is freed, and they complete (the Hajj), it will not suffice them for the Hajj of Islam, because their ihram was concluded for performing nafl, so it does not change to performing fard. Translation: And if after putting on ihram the child becomes adult or the slave becomes free, and both complete the Hajj, then it will not be sufficient for them for the obligatory Hajj, because their ihram was concluded for the initial (nafl), so it will not change to performing fard. Explanation: The issue is that if a minor child becomes adult after putting on ihram, or a slave becomes free after putting on ihram, and then both complete the pillars of Hajj, then the obligatory Hajj will not be performed. Rather, if they have the ability to afford provisions and mount, then each one must perform the obligatory Hajj, because both had put on ihram for nafl Hajj, so it will not change to performing fard. Therefore, from this ihram, nafl Hajj will be performed; to perform the fard, they will have to travel in the future. Here a question can arise: that in Hajj, ihram is a condition, just as wudu is a condition for salah. And after becoming adult, it is permissible to pray with that wudu which was made before adulthood—but this is when he attained adulthood by age, because if adulthood is known by wet dream, his wudu is broken. In any case, just as it is permissible to pray fard salah with that wudu which was made before adulthood, similarly it should be permissible to perform the obligatory Hajj with this ihram which was put on before adulthood. The answer to this is: according to us, the becoming of Hajj as fard is realized by the intention of ihram, and as soon as ihram is put on, the acts of Hajj begin; there is no need for a new intention to begin the acts of Hajj. In contrast, wudu ends before starting salah. The conclusion is that there is no time gap between ihram and beginning the acts of Hajj; rather, as soon as ihram is put on, the acts of Hajj begin. And between wudu and salah there is a time gap. So with this difference, how can one be analogized to the other? Thus, if a child starts salah immediately after wudu and then becomes adult by age and he intends the salah as fard, this salah will not become fard (it remains nafl). Similarly, when a child put on ihram and started nafl Hajj, then became adult and intended this Hajj as fard, it will not become fard.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn and its commentary. The core ruling: if a child or slave performs Hajj before becoming legally responsible (adult or free), that Hajj does not fulfill the obligatory Hajj (Hajjat al-Islam). It remains a nafl Hajj. The proof lies in the nature of ihram: the intention at the time of ihram determines the act. Since the child and slave were not obligated at the time, their ihram was for nafl. The commentary addresses a potential objection based on qiyas with wudu: just as wudu performed before adulthood can be used for fard salah after adulthood, why can't ihram performed before adulthood serve for fard Hajj? The answer distinguishes that there is a time gap between wudu and salah, allowing a new intention, whereas in Hajj, the acts begin immediately with ihram, and no new intention can change the nature of an already commenced act. Thus the qiyas is invalid. This shows the Hanafi principle that the intention at the start binds the entire act.

Key Terms
حَجَّةُ الْإِسْلَامِ (Hajjat al-Islam): The obligatory Hajj that every Muslim must perform once in a lifetime if conditions are met.
نَقْل (naql): A supererogatory act (nafl) as opposed to fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the child is not yet obligated.
C) Because the child's ihram was for nafl and cannot change.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
The intention at the moment of ihram determines the nature of Hajj; it cannot be changed later even if the person becomes obligated.

Child vs Slave: Renewing Ihram and Binding Nature
Distinguishes child's renewal from slave's renewal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a child can renew ihram before wuquf but a slave cannot, using the concepts of lazima and ahliyyah.

Core Idea
A child's ihram is non-binding due to lack of capacity; a slave's ihram binds him completely.

This lesson explores a subtle distinction in Hajj: the ability to renew ihram for the obligatory Hajj before standing at Arafah. The Hanafi school rules differently for a child who attains majority versus a slave who becomes free. The key lies in the binding nature (luzum) of ihram, which depends on legal capacity (ahliyyah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for child and slave
State the explicit ruling: the child can renew ihram (ja'iz), the slave cannot (ghayr ja'iz).
2
Extract the 'illa (effective cause)
Identify why the child's ihram is non-binding: lack of legal capacity (ahliyyah) means the child is not fully obligated by Shariah.
3
Understand the consequence of binding nature
A non-binding ihram can be broken; a binding one cannot. The slave is fully obligated, so his ihram is lazim.
4
Apply the principle to related scenarios
Consider penalties: a child incurs no penalty for ihram violations, while a slave does (though he cannot pay monetary fines).
This reinforces the distinction in binding nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ جَدَدَ الصَّبِيُّ الْإِحْرَامَ قَبْلَ الْوُقُوفِ وَ نَوَى حَجَّةَ الْإِسْلَامِ جَازَ وَالْعَبْدُ لَوْ فَعَلَ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَجُزْ لِأَنَّ إِحْرَامَ الصَّبِيِّ غَيْرُ لَازِمٍ لِعَدَمِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ أَمَّا إِحْرَامُ الْعَبْدِ لَازِمٌ فَلَا يُمْكِنُهُ الْحُرُوجُ مِنْهُ بِالشُّرُوعِ فِي غَيْرِهِ وَاللهُ أَعْلَمُ ترجمہ اگر بچہ نے وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے تجدید احرام کر لیا اور فرض حج کی نیت کر لی تو جائز ہے اور اگر یہ کام غلام نے کیا تو جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ بچہ کا احرام عدم اہلیت کی وجہ سے غیر لازم ہے اور غلام کا احرام لازم ہے پس اس کے غیر میں شروع کر کے اس سے نکلنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر نا بالغ نے احرام باندھا پھر بالغ ہو گیا اور پھر اس نے وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے اس احرام کو توڑ کر دوسرا احرام فرض حج ادا کرنے کے لئے باندھا تو جائز ہو گیا لیکن اگر غلام نے احرام باندھا اور پھر آزاد ہو گیا اور پھر وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے اس نے تجدید احرام کر کے فرض حج کی نیت کر لی تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے ۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ نابالغ کا احرام اس کی عدم اہلیت اور شریعت کے احکام کا مکلف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے غیر لازم تھا یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر اس نے کسی فعل ممنوع کا ارتکاب کر لیا تو اس پر کوئی تاوان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جب اس کا احرام غیر لازم ہے تو اس کو توڑنا بھی جائز ہے اور رہا غلام تو اس کا احرام لازم ہے کیونکہ غلام احکام شرع کا مکلف ہوتا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر اس نے حالت احرام میں شکار کر لیا تو اس پر روزے واجب ہوں گے کیونکہ اس نے شکار کو مارنے کی وجہ سے اپنے احرام پر جنایت کی ہے ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ یہ کفارہ بالمال ادا نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ غلام مال کا مالک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے کفارہ بالمال کا اہل نہیں ہوتا بہر حال اس کا احرام جب لازم ہے تو اس احرام کو توڑ کر دوسرا احرام باندھنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
And if the child renews the ihram before wuquf and intends the Hajj of Islam, it is permissible. But if the slave does that, it is not permissible, because the child's ihram is not binding due to lack of legal capacity. As for the slave's ihram, it is binding, so it is not possible for him to exit from it by starting something else. And Allah knows best. Translation: If a child renews ihram before wuquf and intends the obligatory Hajj, it is permissible. But if a slave does this, it is not permissible, because a child's ihram is not binding due to lack of capacity, and a slave's ihram is binding, so it is not possible for him to exit from it by starting something else. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The scenario is that if a minor put on ihram, then became adult, and then before wuquf he broke that ihram and put on another ihram with the intention of performing the obligatory Hajj, then it is permissible. But if a slave put on ihram, then became free, and then before wuquf he renewed ihram and intended the obligatory Hajj, then this is not permissible. The reason for the difference is that the minor's ihram was non-binding due to his lack of capacity and not being obligated by the rulings of Shariah. For this reason, if he committed a prohibited act, no penalty is obligatory upon him. So when his ihram is non-binding, it is permissible to break it. As for the slave, his ihram is binding because the slave is obligated by the rulings of Shariah. For this reason, if he hunts while in ihram, fasting becomes obligatory upon him, because he has perpetrated a crime against his ihram by killing the game. However, it must be noted that he cannot pay monetary expiation because the slave, not being an owner of property, is not eligible for monetary expiation. In any case, when his ihram is binding, it is not possible to break that ihram and put on another. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage addresses a further nuance: the ability to renew ihram for the obligatory Hajj before wuquf. The matn rules that a child can do so, but a slave cannot. The commentary explains the underlying 'illa (effective cause): the child's ihram is non-binding (ghayr lazim) because the child lacks full legal capacity (ahliyyah) and is not obligated by Shariah. Therefore, the child can break it and start anew. The slave, however, has full capacity for obligations (though property rights are limited), so his ihram is binding (lazim). Once binding, he cannot simply exit it to start another. The commentary reinforces this by noting that a slave incurs penalties for ihram violations (e.g., hunting) even though he cannot pay monetary fines due to lack of ownership. This distinction highlights the Hanafi principle that the binding nature of ihram depends on the legal capacity of the person.

Key Terms
لازم (lazim): Binding; an ihram that cannot be broken without penalty.
اہلیت (ahliyyah): Legal capacity; the ability to assume obligations and incur liabilities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a child renew his ihram before wuquf but a slave cannot?
A) Because the child is not obligated to perform Hajj.
B) Because the child's ihram is non-binding due to lack of legal capacity.
C) Because the slave's ihram is binding and he cannot exit it.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
The binding nature of ihram depends on legal capacity; a child's acts are non-binding, while a slave's are binding.

The Five Mawaqit: Places for Ihram
Lists the five miqat places and states the ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five mawaqit locations and explain the obligation to assume ihram before passing them.

Core Idea
Passing the miqat without ihram is prohibited; ihram may be taken earlier but not later.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) designated five fixed places (mawaqit) for entering the state of ihram. These are not mere markers but legal boundaries — crossing them without ihram violates the Hajj/Umrah obligation. This lesson establishes the locations and the core ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Five Mawaqit
Name each miqat and the region it serves as listed in the Hadith.
Memorize the five: Dhu al-Hulayfah (Madinah), Dhat 'Iraq (Iraq), Juhfah (Sham), Qarn (Najd), Yalamlam (Yemen).
2
Understand the Ruling
The text states it is not permissible (la yajuz) to pass them without ihram. In Hanafi fiqh, this implies prohibition – the act is haram and requires a dam (sacrifice) if violated.
3
Distinguish Timing
Note that you may assume ihram before reaching the miqat (taqdim) but you may not delay it beyond. This is agreed upon (bil-ittifaq).
Early ihram is valid; delayed ihram (crossing without it) incurs penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل مواقيت کے بیان میں ہے مواقیت کی تعریف اور مواضع میقات وَالْمَوَاقِيتُ الَّتِي لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يُجَاوِزَهَا الْإِنْسَانُ إِلَّا مُحْرِمًا خَمْسَةٌ لِأَهْلِ الْمَدِينَةِ ذُو الْحُلَيْفَةِ وَلِأَهْلِ الْعِرَاقِ ذَاتُ عِرْقٍ وَلِأَهْلِ الشَّامِ جُحْفَةُ وَلِأَهْلِ نَجْدٍ قَرْنٌ وَلِأَهْلِ الْيَمَنِ يَلَمْلَمْ هَكَذَا وَقَّتَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ هَذِهِ الْمَوَاقِيتُ لِهَؤُلَاءِ وَفَائِدَةُ التَّوْقِيتِ الْمَنْعُ عَنْ تَأخِيرِ الْإِحْرَامِ عَنْهَا لِأَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ التَّقْدِيمُ عَلَيْهَا بِالِاتِّفَاقِ ترجمہ اور وہ مواقیت جن سے انسان کو بغیر احرام کے تجاوز کرنا جائز نہیں ہے پانچ میں اہل مدینہ کے لئے ذوالحلیفہ ہے اور اہل عراق
The chapter on mawaqit. The mawaqit that it is not permissible for a person to pass them except being in ihram are five: for the people of Madinah, Dhu al-Hulayfah; for the people of Iraq, Dhat 'Iraq; for the people of Sham, Juhfah; for the people of Najd, Qarn; for the people of Yemen, Yalamlam. Thus the Messenger of Allah designated these mawaqit for these people. And the benefit of specifying them is to prevent delaying ihram beyond them, because it is permissible to assume ihram before them by consensus. Translation: And those mawaqit that it is not permissible for a person to pass without ihram are five: for the people of Madinah, Dhu al-Hulayfah; for the people of Iraq, Dhat 'Iraq; for the people of Sham, Juhfah; for the people of Najd, Qarn; and for the people of Yemen, Yalamlam. The Messenger of Allah specified these mawaqit for these people. The benefit of specifying them is to prevent delaying ihram beyond them, because it is permissible to assume ihram before them by consensus.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter (fasl) on mawaqit (the fixed places for entering the state of ihram). The matn states the well-known five miqat locations appointed by the Prophet (peace be upon him) for the people of different regions: Dhu al-Hulayfah (for Madinah), Dhat 'Iraq (for Iraq), Juhfah (for Syria/Sham), Qarn (for Najd), and Yalamlam (for Yemen). The ruling is that one must not pass beyond these points without assuming ihram, though one may enter ihram before reaching them. The 'benefit of designation' (faidat al-tawqit) is to make it impermissible to delay ihram beyond these points. This is a foundational ruling for Hajj and Umrah.

Key Terms
میقات (miqat): A fixed place or time for entering the state of ihram; here, the five spatial mawaqit.
ذو الحلیفہ (Dhu al-Hulayfah): A place near Madinah, the miqat for those coming from Madinah direction.
ذات عرق (Dhat 'Iraq): A miqat for those coming from Iraq.
جحفہ (Juhfah): A miqat for those coming from Syria (Sham).
قرن (Qarn): A miqat for those coming from Najd.
یلملم (Yalamlam): A miqat for those coming from Yemen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the miqat for a person coming from Iraq?
A) Dhu al-Hulayfah
B) Juhfah
C) Dhat 'Iraq
D) Yalamlam

Key Takeaway
The five mawaqit are fixed boundaries for entering ihram; passing them without ihram is prohibited, though early ihram is permissible.

Child's Ihram Renewal vs Slave's Ihram for Hajj
Explaining why a child can renew Ihram but a slave cannot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on renewal of Ihram for a child who reaches puberty and a slave who is freed, and explain the legal basis using the concept of lizum (bindingness) and legal capacity (ahliyyah).

Core Idea
A child's Ihram is non-binding so renewal is valid; a slave's Ihram is binding so renewal is invalid.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from al-Hidayah: why a minor who enters Ihram for supererogatory Hajj can later renew it for obligatory Hajj after reaching puberty, while a slave who does the same cannot. The key lies in legal capacity—the child lacks it, the slave has it. The author uses a qiyas with wudu and prayer to illustrate the principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage compares a child who renews Ihram after puberty with a slave who renews after being freed. Understand the factual difference.
2
Analyze the qiyas with wudu-prayer
The author first rejects an analogy between wudu/prayer and Ihram/Hajj because of surplus time. Grasp why the analogy fails.
The key difference: between wudu and prayer there is time to decide, but Ihram starts the Hajj acts immediately.
3
Determine the binding nature of Ihram
The child's Ihram is ghayr lazim (non-binding) due to lack of ahliyyah; the slave's Ihram is lazim (binding) because he is mukallaf. This is the decisive difference.
A child's Ihram does not obligate expiations; a slave's does.
4
Apply the ruling
The child may break his Ihram and renew; the slave cannot. Know the consequence.

وقت فاضل نہیں ہے بلکہ احرام باندھتے ہی افعال حج شروع ہو گئے اور وضو اور نماز کے درمیان وقت فاضل ہوتا ہے پس اس فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے ایک کو دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہوگا چنانچہ اگر بچہ نے وضو کرتے ہی نماز شروع کر دی اور پھر وہ عمر کے ذریعہ بالغ ہو گیا اور اس نے نماز کے فرض ہونے کی نیت کر لی تو یہ نماز بدل کر فرض نہ ہو گی پس اسی طرح جب بچہ نے احرام باندھ کر حج نفل شروع کر دیا پھر بالغ ہوا اور اس نے اس حج کے فرض ہونے کی نیت کی تو یہ بدل کر فرض نہ ہوگا۔
بچے نے وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے احترام کی تجدید کر لی اور فرض حج کی نیت کر لی تو حج درست ہو جائے گا وَلَوْ جَدَدَ الصَّى الْإِحْرَامَ قَبْلَ الْوُقُوفِ وَ نَوَى حَجَّةَ الإِسلَامِ جَازَ وَالْعَبْدُ لَوَفَعَلَ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَجُر لأنَّ إحرام الصَّبي غَيْرُ لازم لِعَدَمِ الأهْلِيَّةِ أَمَّا إحْرَامُ الْعَبدِ لَازِمُ فَلَا يُمْكِنُهُ الْحُرُوجُ مِنْهُ بِالشَّرُوع فِى غَيْرِهِ وَالله اعلم ترجمہ اگر بچہ نے وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے تجدید احرام کر لیا اور فرض حج کی نیت کر لی تو جائز ہے اور اگر یہ کام غلام نے کیا تو جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ بچہ کا احرام عدم اہلیت کی وجہ سے غیر لازم ہے اور غلام کا احترام لازم ہے پس اس کے غیر میں شروع کر کے اس سے نکلنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر نا بالغ نے احرام باندھا پھر بالغ ہو گیا اور پھر اس نے وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے اس احرام کو توڑ کر دوسرا احرام فرض حج ادا کرنے کے لئے باندھا تو جائز ہو گیا لیکن اگر تمام نے احرام باندھا اور پھر آزاد ہو گیا اور پھر وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے اس نے تجدید احترامہ کر کے فرض حج کی نیت کر لی تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے ۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ نابالغ کا احترام اس کی عدم اہلیت اور شریعت کے احکام کا مکلف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے غیر لازم تھا یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر اس نے کسی فعل ممنوع کا ارتکاب کر لیا تو اس پر کوئی تاوان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جب اس کا احترام غیر لازم ہے تو اس کو صبح کرنا بھی جائز ہے اور ربا غلام تو اس کا احترام لازم ہے کیونکہ غلام احکام شرع کا مکلف ہوتا ہے ہیں وجہ ہے کہ اگر اس نے حالت احرام میں شکار کر لیا تو اس پر روزے واجب ہوں گے کیونکہ اس نے شکار کو مارنے کی وجہ سے اپنے احرام پر جنایت کی ہے ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ یہ کفارہ بالمال ادا نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ غلام مال کا مالک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے کفارہ بالمال کا اہل نہیں ہوتا بہر حال نام کا احترام جب لازم ہے تو اس احترام کو تو ڑ کر دوسرا احرام باندھنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
There is no surplus time; rather with tying Ihram, the actions of Hajj begin, whereas between wudu and prayer there is surplus time. So with this difference, how can one analogize one to the other? If a child started prayer right after wudu and then reached puberty through age and intended that prayer as obligatory, that prayer would not become obligatory. Similarly, when a child starts a supererogatory Hajj by tying Ihram, then reaches puberty and intends that Hajj as obligatory, it will not become obligatory. If the child renews Ihram before the standing at Arafah and intends the Hajj of Islam (obligatory Hajj), it is permissible. If a slave does that, it is not permissible. Because the child's Ihram is non-binding due to lack of legal capacity. As for the slave's Ihram, it is binding, so he cannot exit it by beginning something else. And Allah knows best. Translation: If a child renews Ihram before the standing at Arafah and intends obligatory Hajj, it is permissible. If a slave does that, it is not permissible because the child's Ihram is non-binding due to lack of capacity, and the slave's Ihram is binding, so it is not possible for him to exit it by beginning something else. And Allah knows best. Commentary: The scenario is that if a minor ties Ihram, then reaches puberty, and then before the standing at Arafah breaks that Ihram and ties another Ihram to perform obligatory Hajj, it becomes permissible. But if a slave ties Ihram, then becomes free, and then before the standing at Arafah renews Ihram and intends obligatory Hajj, it is not permissible. The reason for the difference is that the minor's Ihram was non-binding due to his lack of capacity and not being obligated by Shariah rulings. This is why if he commits a prohibited act, no compensation is due upon him. So when his Ihram is non-binding, breaking it is also permissible. As for the slave, his Ihram is binding because the slave is obligated by Shariah rulings. This is why if he hunts while in Ihram, fasting becomes obligatory upon him because he has violated his Ihram by killing the game. However, this expiation cannot be paid with wealth because the slave does not own property and is not eligible for expiation with wealth. In any case, when the slave's Ihram is binding, it is not possible to break it and tie another Ihram. And Allah knows best. Jameel Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Hidayah concerning the renewal of Ihram for a child (sabi) and a slave ('abd) before the standing at Arafah. The author first draws a comparison between wudu/prayer and Ihram/Hajj to show that an analogy is invalid due to a key difference: in wudu there is surplus time between the act and the prayer, whereas in Hajj the acts begin immediately with Ihram. The core ruling is that if a child ties Ihram for a supererogatory Hajj, then reaches puberty, and before Arafah renews his Ihram intending obligatory Hajj, it is valid. However, if a slave does the same (ties Ihram as a slave, then becomes free, then renews Ihram intending obligatory Hajj), it is not valid. The reason is that the child's Ihram is non-binding (ghayr lazim) because he lacked legal capacity (ahliyyah) at the time of the first Ihram. Thus he can exit it and make a new Ihram. In contrast, the slave's Ihram is binding (lazim) because he is a fully obligated person (mukallaf) when he ties it. Even if he later becomes free, the original Ihram remains binding and cannot be replaced. The passage also notes that while a slave may commit violations in Ihram (like hunting) and owe expiation (kaffarah), that expiation is by fasting, not by wealth, since a slave does not own property. This illustrates the slave's capacity for obligation. The Hanafi position is clear: the child's Ihram is not binding; the slave's is.

Key Terms
احرام (Ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, entered by reciting the talbiyah and wearing specific garments, which prohibits certain acts.
لازم (Lazim): Binding, irrevocable; the Ihram of a legally capable person cannot be exited without completing the rites or offering a sacrifice (dam).
صبی (Sabi): A minor child who has not reached puberty; his actions are valid but not binding (ghayr lazim).
عبد (Abd): A slave; a legally capable person (mukallaf) but with limited ownership rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a child renew his Ihram for obligatory Hajj after reaching puberty, but a slave cannot after being freed?
A) Because the child's Ihram was not binding due to lack of legal capacity, while the slave's Ihram was binding.
B) Because the child is younger and thus has more excuses.
C) Because the slave's Ihram is void due to his servitude.
D) Because the child can afford to repeat Hajj, but the slave cannot.

Key Takeaway
The decisive factor is legal capacity: a child's Ihram is non-binding, so renewal is permitted; a slave's Ihram is binding, so it cannot be replaced.

The Five Mawaqit: Fixed Boundaries for Ihram
Defining the five fixed miqat boundaries for Ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five miqat locations, state the ruling for passing them without Ihram, and apply the rule to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Passing the miqat without Ihram is prohibited; the miqat is a condition, but you may enter Ihram earlier.

The miqat is the prescribed boundary from which a pilgrim must enter Ihram. The Prophet (peace be upon him) designated five specific locations for different regions. Understanding these boundaries is essential for performing Hajj and Umrah correctly. This passage clarifies the locations, the legal implications of passing them without Ihram, and the consensus that one may tie Ihram before reaching the miqat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five mawaqit
List the five locations and the regions they serve: Dhul Hulaifah (Madinah), Dhat Irq (Iraq), Juhfah (Sham/Egypt), Qarn (Najd), Yalamlam (Yemen). Note that Dhat Irq was fixed by Umar (RA) based on prophetic knowledge.
Memorize the names and regions for application.
2
Understand the ruling on the miqat
It is wajib to enter Ihram before or at the miqat. Passing the miqat without Ihram is prohibited (haram) and requires a dam (sacrifice) as compensation. The miqat is a condition for beginning Hajj/Umrah in a valid state.
The ruling is derived from the hadith and the consensus of the Companions.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith of Ibn Abbas (RA) in Sahihayn names four miqat locations and states they apply to residents and those passing through. Dhat Irq is proven by other narrations. The Prophet fixed these boundaries by divine guidance.
The hadith uses the verb 'waqata' (fixed), indicating a binding designation.
4
Clarify the permissibility of early Ihram
The text explicitly states that tying Ihram before the miqat is permissible by consensus (bil-ittifaq). The prohibition is only on delaying Ihram beyond the miqat, not on doing it earlier.
Many mistakenly think Ihram must be tied exactly at the miqat. Early Ihram is valid and often recommended for convenience.
5
Apply to different travelers
Identify which miqat applies based on a traveller's route. For example, someone from Egypt uses Juhfah; someone from India via sea may use Yalamlam. The miqat applies even if they do not reside in that region.
If one lives between the miqat and Makkah, they tie Ihram from their home. Makkans tie from Makkah.

المَوَاقِيْتَ کہنا کس طرح درست ہوگا جبکہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں عراق فتح بھی نہیں ہوا تھا اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آنحضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کو بذریعہ وحی معلوم ہو گیا تھا۔ کہ عراق اور شام فتح ہو جائیں گے اور عراق، شام کی طرح دار الا سلام ہوگا اسلئے آپ سے نے اہل شام اور اہل عراق کے لئے میقات مقرر فرما دیا تھا۔ (۳) اہل شام کا میقات جحفہ ہے یہی اہل مصر کا میقات ہے یہاں سے مکہ ۸۲ میل ہے اور مدینہ منورہ تین منزل ہے اور بحر قلزم چھ میل ہے۔ ۴) اہل نجد کا میقات قرآن ہے۔ (۵) اہل یمن کا میقات یا علم ہے یہ ملکہ سے جنوب میں تمیں میل ہے صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مواقیت احادیث سے ثابت ہیں چنانچہ ذات عرق کے علاوہ باقی چار میقات کے تعین کا ثبوت صحیحین میں ہے اور ذات عرق کا ثبوت مسلم اور ابو داؤد میں ہے صحیحین میں حضرت ابن عباس کی حدیث ہے أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَقَتَ لِأَهْلِ الْمَدِينَةِ ذَا الْحُلَيْفَةَ وَلأَهل الشَّامِ الجُحْفَةَ وَلِأَهْلِ نَجَدٍ قَرْنَ الْمَنَازِلَ لِأَهْلِ الْيَمَنِ يَلَملَم هُنَّ لَهُنَّ وَ لِمَن أَتَى عَلَيْهِنَّ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَهْلِهِنَّ مِمَّن أَرَادَ الحَج وَالْعُمْرَةَ وَمَنْ كَانَ دُونَ ذَالِكَ فَمِن حَيْثُ شَاءُ حَتَّى أَهْلَ مَكَّةَ مِنْ مَكَة یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے موقت فرمایا اہل مدینہ کے واسطے ذوالحلیفہ اور اہل شام کے واسطے مجحفہ اور اہل نجد کے لئے قرآن المنازل اور اہل یمن کے واسطے یہ علم یہ مواقیت یہاں کے رہنے والوں کے واسطے ہیں اور ان کے علاوہ جو ان پر آئے ان لوگوں میں سے جو حج یا عمرہ کا ارادہ رکھتے ہوں اور جولوگ ان مواقیت سے اس طرف ہوں تو وہ جہاں سے چاہیں حتی کہ مکہ والے مکہ سے احرام باندھیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرمانے ہیں کہ ان مواقیت کو مقرر کرنے کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ ان مواقیت سے احرام میں تاخیر کرنا ممنوع ہے یہ مطلب نہیں ہے کہ ان مواقیت پر پہنچنے سے پہلے احرام نہیں باندھ سکتا۔ کیونکہ میقات سے پہلے احرام باندھنا بالاتفاق جائز ہے۔
Section on Mawaqit. Explanation of Mawaqit: Definition and locations of Miqat. And the Mawaqit which it is not permissible for a person to pass except in Ihram are five: For the people of Madinah: Dhul Hulaifah; for the people of Iraq: Dhat Irq; for the people of Sham: Juhfah; for the people of Najd: Qarn; for the people of Yemen: Yalamlam. Thus the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) fixed these Mawaqit for these people. The benefit of fixing them is to prevent delaying Ihram beyond them, because it is permissible to do Ihram before them by consensus. Translation: And the Mawaqit from which it is not permissible for a person to pass without Ihram are five: for the people of Madinah, Dhul Hulaifah; for the people of Iraq, Dhat Irq; for the people of Sham, Juhfah; for the people of Najd, Qarn; and for the people of Yemen, Yalamlam. Thus the Messenger of Allah fixed these Mawaqit for these people. And the benefit of fixing the miqat is to prevent delaying Ihram beyond them, because it is permissible to do Ihram before them by consensus. Commentary: So far it has been explained upon whom Hajj is obligatory and upon whom it is not, and what are the conditions for Hajj being obligatory. Now in this section, it will be mentioned where Hajj begins. 'Mawaqit' is the plural of 'miqat', and miqat is used for a fixed time, but here it is used metaphorically for a fixed place. So here miqat refers to the places from which it is not permissible to pass without Ihram. And the Mawaqit are five: (1) The miqat of the people of Madinah is Dhul Hulaifah. Hulaifah is the diminutive of Hulfah. There used to be a tree there, now a mosque has been built. This place is about six miles from Madinah. (2) The miqat of the people of Iraq is Dhat Irq. From this place to Makkah is forty-two miles. Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) fixed this as miqat after conquering Kufa and Basra. But an objection might be raised: How can the author of al-Hidayah say 'Thus the Messenger of Allah fixed these Mawaqit' when Iraq had not been conquered in his time? The answer is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) knew through revelation that Iraq and Sham would be conquered and would become Dar al-Islam, so he fixed the miqat for the people of Sham and Iraq. (3) The miqat of the people of Sham is Juhfah; this is also the miqat for the people of Egypt. From here to Makkah is 82 miles, and it is three stages from Madinah, and six miles from the Red Sea. (4) The miqat of the people of Najd is Qarn. (5) The miqat of the people of Yemen is Yalamlam. It is sixty miles south of Makkah. The author of al-Hidayah says that the Mawaqit are proven by hadiths. For the four miqat besides Dhat Irq, the proof is in Sahihayn (Bukhari and Muslim), and for Dhat Irq, the proof is in Muslim and Abu Dawud. In the Sahihayn, the hadith of Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) is: 'Verily the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) fixed for the people of Madinah Dhul Hulaifah; for the people of Sham, Juhfah; for the people of Najd, Qarn al-Manazil; for the people of Yemen, Yalamlam. These are for them and for those who come upon them from other than their people, from those who intend Hajj and Umrah. And whoever is before these (on the side of Makkah), then from wherever he wishes, even the people of Makkah from Makkah.' The author of al-Hidayah says that the benefit of fixing these Mawaqit is that delaying Ihram beyond them is prohibited. It does not mean that one cannot tie Ihram before reaching them. Because tying Ihram before the miqat is permissible by consensus.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter (fasl) on the mawaqit (plural of miqat). The author defines mawaqit as the boundaries from which a person intending Hajj or Umrah must enter the state of Ihram and cannot pass without it. The Prophet (peace be upon him) designated five specific locations for different regions: (1) Dhul Hulaifah for people of Madinah (now known as Abyar Ali, about 6 miles from Madinah); (2) Dhat Irq for people of Iraq; (3) Juhfah for people of Sham (Syria) and Egypt; (4) Qarn al-Manazil for people of Najd; (5) Yalamlam for people of Yemen. The commentary clarifies that Dhat Irq was fixed by Umar (RA) after the conquest of Iraq, but the text of al-Hidayah attributes the fixing to the Prophet (peace be upon him) because he knew through revelation that Iraq would become part of Dar al-Islam and thus a miqat was needed. The hadith of Ibn Abbas (RA) in Sahihayn confirms the first four and adds that these mawaqit apply not only to residents of those regions but to anyone passing through them towards Makkah for Hajj or Umrah. Those whose homes lie between the miqat and Makkah can tie Ihram from their home; residents of Makkah tie Ihram from Makkah. The key ruling is that one must not pass the miqat without Ihram; it is prohibited (mamnu') to delay Ihram beyond it. However, it is permissible by consensus to tie Ihram before reaching the miqat. The miqat is a condition (shart) for entering Hajj; tying Ihram before it is valid but not obligatory.

Key Terms
مواقیت (Mawaqit): Plural of miqat; the fixed boundaries from which pilgrims must enter Ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
میقات (Miqat): A fixed time or place; here used metaphorically for a place designated for beginning Ihram.
ذوالحلیفہ (Dhul Hulaifah): The miqat for people of Madinah, located about 6 miles outside Madinah, now known as Abyar Ali.
ذات عرق (Dhat Irq): The miqat for people of Iraq, fixed by Umar (RA) after the conquest of Iraq, located about 42 miles from Makkah.
جحفہ (Juhfah): The miqat for people of Sham and Egypt, located about 82 miles from Makkah.
قرن (Qarn): The miqat for people of Najd, also known as Qarn al-Manazil.
یلملم (Yalamlam): The miqat for people of Yemen, located about 60 miles south of Makkah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on passing the miqat without Ihram according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is permissible if one makes up for it later.
B) It is prohibited (haram), and one must offer a dam (sacrifice) as compensation.
C) It is makruh and requires no compensation.
D) It is invalid and Hajj is not accepted.

Key Takeaway
The miqat is a fixed boundary that must not be crossed without Ihram; violate it and pay a dam, but your Hajj/Umrah remains valid.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
The Five Miqats: Boundaries for Ihram
Defines and lists the five Miqats with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five Miqats, explain their hadith evidence, and apply the Hanafi ruling that passing beyond a Miqat without Ihram is prohibited for anyone intending to enter Makkah.

Core Idea
The five Miqats are fixed by revelation; passing them without Ihram is prohibited for anyone entering Makkah, not only pilgrims.

Hajj and Umrah have specific starting points—geographical boundaries called Miqats—where the pilgrim must enter the state of Ihram. This lesson introduces the five Miqats established by the Prophet ﷺ, their hadith proofs, and the Hanafi ruling that the obligation applies to all persons entering Makkah, whether for Hajj, Umrah, or other purposes. Understanding these boundaries is essential for correctly performing the pilgrimage and avoiding sin.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term 'Miqat'
The passage explains that 'Miqat' literally means an appointed time, but here it is used metaphorically for an appointed place. Identify the shift from temporal to spatial meaning.
This metaphorical usage is common in Hanafi fiqh for technical terms.
2
List the five Miqats and their assigned regions
Identify each Miqat alongside its corresponding region: Dhu al-Hulayfah (Madinah), Juhfah (Syria/Egypt), Qarn al-Manazil (Najd), Yalamlam (Yemen), and Dhat Irq (Iraq). Note the additional detail about Dhat Irq being appointed by Umar (RA) but confirmed by revelation.
Memorize these five; they are frequently tested in fiqh exams.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The passage quotes the hadith of Ibn Abbas (RA) from Sahihayn. Note that four Miqats are explicitly mentioned in the hadith; Dhat Irq is also proven via Muslim and Abu Dawud. Understand how the Prophet ﷺ fixed these boundaries.
The hadith's wording specifies 'for those who intend Hajj or Umrah', but Hanafis extend it to all entries into Makkah.
4
Distinguish the ruling for different categories of people
The hadith distinguishes: (a) residents of the Miqat region—their Miqat is that boundary; (b) those coming from beyond—they must enter Ihram at the Miqat they pass; (c) those living within the Miqat boundaries (including Makkans)—they may enter Ihram from their homes.
This is crucial for determining when and where to enter Ihram.
5
Understand the permissibility of early Ihram
The passage clarifies that delaying Ihram beyond the Miqat is prohibited, but entering Ihram before reaching the Miqat is unanimously permissible and even meritorious.
This corrects a common misunderstanding that one must wait until the Miqat.

Book of Hajj. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 3. For the people of Iraq, Dhat Irq is the Miqat; for the people of Syria, Juhfah; for the people of Najd, Qarn; and for the people of Yemen, Yalamlam. Similarly, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed these Miqats for those people. The benefit of fixing the Miqat is to prohibit delay of Ihram, because it is permissible to perform Ihram before these Miqats. Explanation: So far it has been stated upon whom Hajj is obligatory and upon whom it is not, and what are the conditions for Hajj being wajib. Now in this chapter it will be mentioned where the commencement of Hajj will be. Mawaqit is the plural of Miqat, and Miqat is used for an appointed time, but here it is used metaphorically for an appointed place. Here Miqat means those places beyond which it is not permissible to pass without Ihram. The Mawaqit are five: (1) The Miqat of the people of Madinah is Dhu al-Hulayfah. It is the diminutive of Khalifah? Here there used to be a tree, now a mosque has been built. This place is about six miles from Madinah. (2) The Miqat of the people of Iraq is Dhat Irq. This place is 42 miles from Makkah al-Mukarramah. Sayyiduna Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) appointed this place as Miqat after conquering Kufa and Basra. But there is an objection: How can the author of al-Hidayah say, 'Thus the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed these Mawaqit' when Iraq had not been conquered during his time? The answer is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) knew by revelation that Iraq and Syria would be conquered and would become Dar al-Islam, so he appointed Miqats for the people of Syria and Iraq. (3) The Miqat of the people of Syria is Juhfah. This is also the Miqat of the people of Egypt. It is 82 miles from Makkah, three stages from Madinah al-Munawwarah, and six miles from the Red Sea. (4) The Miqat of the people of Najd is Qarn. (5) The Miqat of the people of Yemen is Yalamlam. It is 10? miles south of Makkah. The author of al-Hidayah says that the Mawaqit are established by ahadith. Thus, for the four Miqats other than Dhat Irq, the proof is in the Sahihayn, and for Dhat Irq the proof is in Muslim and Abu Dawud. In the Sahihayn is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed for the people of Madinah Dhu al-Hulayfah, for the people of Syria Juhfah, for the people of Najd Qarn al-Manazil, and for the people of Yemen Yalamlam. These are for them and for those who come upon them from other than their people, from those who intend Hajj or Umrah. And whoever is within these (Miqats), then (his Miqat is) from where he wishes, even the people of Makkah from Makkah.' That is, the Prophet (peace be upon him) appointed Dhu al-Hulayfah for the people of Madinah, Juhfah for the people of Syria, Qarn al-Manazil for the people of Najd, and Yalamlam for the people of Yemen. These Miqats are for the residents of those places and for those from elsewhere who pass through them intending Hajj or Umrah. And those who are on this side of these Miqats (i.e., between them and Makkah) may enter Ihram from wherever they wish, and even the people of Makkah from Makkah. The author of al-Hidayah says that the benefit of fixing these Miqats is that delaying Ihram beyond them is prohibited. This does not mean that one cannot enter Ihram before reaching the Miqat, because entering Ihram before the Miqat is unanimously permissible.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling exposition on the Mawaqit (plural of Miqat) — the appointed boundaries for entering the state of Ihram for Hajj and Umrah. The author first clarifies that 'Miqat' literally means an appointed time, but here it is used metaphorically for a specific place. The ruling is that it is not permissible for any pilgrim to pass beyond these boundaries without entering Ihram. The five Miqats are then listed with their locations and historical background. A key point is that Dhat Irq was appointed by Umar (RA) after the conquest of Iraq, but the author resolves an apparent contradiction — how can the Prophet (SAW) be said to have appointed it? The answer is that the Prophet (SAW) knew by revelation that Iraq would become Muslim territory and thus legislated its Miqat. The hadith of Ibn Abbas (RA) from Sahihayn is quoted as the primary evidence establishing these Miqats for their respective regions and also for those coming from beyond. The author emphasizes that the purpose of the Miqat is to prevent delay in entering Ihram; however, it is perfectly permissible (and even meritorious) to enter Ihram before reaching the Miqat.

Key Terms
میقات (miqāt): A specific geographical boundary appointed for entering Ihram; one may not pass it without Ihram when intending to enter Makkah.
آفاقی (āfāqī): A person who resides outside the boundaries of the Miqats (i.e., beyond the appointed stations).
ذوالحلیلہ (dhū al-ḥulayfah): The Miqat for the people of Madinah, about six miles from Madinah; now known as Abar Ali, with a mosque.
ذات عرق (dhātu 'irq): The Miqat for the people of Iraq, appointed by Umar (RA) after the conquest of Iraq; 42 miles from Makkah.
جحفہ (juḥfah): The Miqat for the people of Syria (Sham) and Egypt; 82 miles from Makkah.
قرن المنازل (qarn al-manāzil): The Miqat for the people of Najd; known as al-Sayl al-Kabir.
یلملم (yalamlam): The Miqat for the people of Yemen; about 10 miles south of Makkah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in al-Hidayah, which of the following is NOT explicitly mentioned as a Miqat appointed by the Prophet ﷺ?
A) Dhu al-Hulayfah
B) Juhfah
C) Dhat Irq
D) Qarn al-Manazil

Key Takeaway
The five Miqats are fixed boundaries for entering Ihram; the Hanafi school obligates Ihram for anyone entering Makkah, and passing without Ihram requires a dam.

Ruling for Aafaqi Passing Miqat: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on ihram obligation for entering Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that an Aafaqi must enter ihram when passing the Miqat intending to enter Makkah for any purpose, explain the Shafi'i objection that ihram is only for Hajj or Umrah, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the principle of ta'zim al-haram.

Core Idea
Ihram is wajib for entering Makkah from beyond the Miqat, regardless of intention, due to the sanctity of the Haram.

This passage presents a key fiqh dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school. The question is whether an Aafaqi (a person living outside the Miqat boundaries) must enter the state of ihram when crossing the Miqat to enter Makkah for purposes other than Hajj or Umrah, such as business or visiting. By studying this dispute, you will learn not only the ruling itself but also how each school derives its position from the sources and how the Hanafi school defends its view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its core rationale
Identify the ruling: it is wajib for an Aafaqi to enter ihram when reaching the Miqat with the intention of entering Makkah, whether for Hajj, Umrah, or any other purpose. The rationale is that ihram is for glorifying the Haram, not solely for pilgrimage.
The term 'wajib' indicates a binding obligation, not merely recommended.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its proofs
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that ihram is required only for Hajj or Umrah. His proofs: (1) Ihram is legislated specifically for pilgrimage (Quran 2:196); (2) The Prophet (SAW) entered Makkah during the Conquest without ihram, indicating it is not required for non-pilgrimage entries.
The Conquest of Makkah is a key counter-example.
3
Follow the Hanafi hadith proof
The Hanafi school relies on the general hadith of Ibn Abbas (RA): 'None shall pass the Miqat except in a state of ihram.' According to Hanafi usul, this general negation (لا يجوز) indicates prohibition of crossing without ihram, and the imperative to enter ihram is derived from the exception.
The hadith is considered authentic (sahih) by both schools, but the point of contention is its interpretation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rational proof
The Hanafi argument is that the obligation of ihram is due to the sanctity of the Haram (ta'zim al-buq'ah al-sharifah), not because it is a condition for Hajj/Umrah. Evidence: the people of Hill (within Miqat) must enter ihram when entering Makkah even if not for pilgrimage.
This rational proof (qiyas) strengthens the hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: an Aafaqi entering Makkah for business is required to enter ihram in the Hanafi school, but not in the Shafi'i school. The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi (relied upon) and is considered stronger because the hadith is explicit and the rational basis is consistent.
The Shafi'i position is respected as a legitimate ikhtilaf.

ثُمَّ الْأَفَاقِي إِذَا انْتَهَى إِلَيْهَا عَلَى قَصْدِ دُخُولِ مَكَّةَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُحْرِمَ فَصَدَ الْحَجَّ أَوِ الْعُمْرَةَ أَو لَمْ يَقْصُدْ عِندَنَا لِقَوْلِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا يُجَاوِزُ أَحَدٌ المَيقَاتَ إِلَّا مُحْرِمًا ولأنَّ وُجُوبَ الإِحْرَامِ لَتَعْظِيمِ هَذِهِ الْبَقْعَةِ الشَّرِيفَةِ فَيَسْتَوِى فِيهِ الحاج والمعتمر وغيرهما
ترجمہ پھر آفاقی آدمی جب مکہ میں داخل ہونے کے ارادہ سے میقات پر پہنچا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس پر احرام باندھنا واجب سے خواہ حج کا ارادہ کرے یا عمرہ کا ارادہ کرے یا کچھ ارادہ نہ کرے کیونکہ حضور ہی نے فرمایا کہ کوئی شخص میقات سے تجاوز نہ کرے مگر احرام باندھ کر کیونکہ احترام واجب ہونا اس بقعہ شریفہ کی تعظیم کے لئے ہے لہذا اسمیں حج یا عمرہ کا ارادہ کرنے والا اور ان دونوں کے علاوہ سب برابر ہیں۔
تشریح آفاقی وہ لوگ کہلاتے ہیں جو مواقیت سے باہر رہنے والے ہیں، اور جو مواقیت کے اندر رہنے والے ہیں ان کو سکی کہا جاتا ہے آفاقی لوگوں کے مواقیت تو وہ ہیں جو ہم نے گذشتہ صفحات میں ذکر کئے ہیں اور کی یعنی ان لوگوں کے میقات جو مواقیت اور حرم کے درمیان میں رہتے ہیں حل ہے یعنی حرم شروع ہونے سے پہلے پہلے احرام باندھ لیں۔ صاحب عنایہ کے بیان کے مطابق ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ جو شخص آفاقی اور مکی دونوں کے میقات سے آگے جانے کا ارادہ رکھتا ہو اس کے لئے بغیر احرام کے جانا جائز نہیں ہے اور جو شخص فقط ایک میقات یعنی آفاقی لوگوں کے میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کا ارادہ رکھتا ہو اور مکی کے میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کا ارادہ نہ ہو تو اس کو بغیر احرام کے جانا جائز ہے مثلا کوئی شخص جدہ یاصل میں کسی جگہ جانا چاہتا ہے تو اس پر احرام باندھنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ اتی ضابطہ کی روشنی میں صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی آفاقی شخص مکتہ المکرمہ جانے کے ارادہ سے میقات پر پہنچا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس پر احرام باندھنا واجب ہے خواہ اس کا ارادہ حج کا ہو یا عمرہ کا یا ان دونوں کے علاوہ تجارت وغیرہ کا یہی امام احمد کا مذہب ہے اور حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر حج یا عمرہ کے ارادہ سے مکہ جانے کا ارادہ ہو تو احرام باندھنا واجب ہے اور اگر ان کے علاوہ کا ارادہ ہو تو احرام واجب نہیں ہے۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ احرام حج یا عمرہ دونوں میں سے ایک کے لئے مشروع ہوا ہے پس جب ان میں سے کسی ایک کی نیت کرے گا تو احرام لازم ہو گا ورنہ نہیں۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم فتح مکہ کے روز بغیر احرام کے داخل ہوئے تھے کیونکہ فتح مکہ کے موقع پر آپ کا ارادہ نہ حج کا تھا اور نہ عمرہ کا بلکہ مکہ کو فتح کرنے کا ارادہ تھا۔
ہماری دلیل ابن عباس کی حدیث ہے قَالَ سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ لَا يُجَاوِرُ الْمِيقَاتَ أَحَدُ الَّا مُحُوماً فرمایا کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو کہتے ہوئے سنا ہے کہ کوئی شخص بغیر احرام کے میقات سے تجاوز نہ کرے اس حدیث کا اطلاق اس پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ میقات سے تجاوز کر کے مکتہ المکرمہ جانے والا خواہ حج یا عمرہ کا ارادہ کرے یا تجارت وغیرہ کسی اور چیز کا ارادہ کرے بہر صورت اس پر احترام واجب ہے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ احرام باندھنا سرزمین حرم کی تعظیم کے پیش نظر واجب ہوا ہے نہ کہ حج اور عمرہ کی شرط ہونے کی وجہ سے یہی وجہ ہے کہ جو لوگ میقات اور حرم کے درمیان میں رہتے ہیں ان پر بھی احرام باندھنا واجب ہے بہر حال احترام کا وجوب حریم کی
Ruling for the Aafaqi passing the Miqat without Ihram. Then the Aafaqi, when he reaches it (the Miqat) with the intention of entering Makkah, it is necessary upon him to enter Ihram, whether he intends Hajj or Umrah or does not intend them, according to us (Hanafis), because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'None shall pass the Miqat except in a state of Ihram.' And because the obligation of Ihram is for the glorification of this noble precinct, so in it the Hajj pilgrim, the Umrah pilgrim, and others are equal. Translation: Then when an Aafaqi person reaches the Miqat with the intention of entering Makkah, according to us it is wajib upon him to enter Ihram, whether he intends Hajj, Umrah, or does not intend anything, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'None shall pass the Miqat except in a state of Ihram.' And because the obligation of Ihram is for the glorification of this noble place, so the one intending Hajj, Umrah, and others are all equal. Explanation: Aafaqis are those who live outside the Mawaqit. Those who live within the Mawaqit are called Suki? Their Miqat is al-Hill, i.e., they should enter Ihram before entering the Haram. According to the statement of the author of al-Inayah, the rule is: A person who intends to pass beyond both the Miqat of the Aafaqi and the Miqat of the Makkan (i.e., the boundary of the Haram) may not go without Ihram. But one who intends to pass only the Miqat of the Aafaqi (i.e., going to a place within the Miqat area but not to the Haram) may go without Ihram. For example, if someone wants to go to Jeddah or some other place, it is not wajib upon him to enter Ihram. According to this rule, the case is: if an Aafaqi person reaches the Miqat intending to go to Makkah al-Mukarramah, then according to us it is wajib upon him to enter Ihram, whether his intention is Hajj, Umrah, or trade, etc. This is also the madhhab of Imam Ahmad. Imam al-Shafi'i said: If he intends to go to Makkah for Hajj or Umrah, then entering Ihram is wajib; but if he intends something else, then Ihram is not wajib. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that Ihram is legislated only for one of the two acts (Hajj or Umrah), so when he intends one of them, Ihram becomes necessary; otherwise not. Another proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) entered Makkah on the day of the Conquest without Ihram because his intention was not Hajj or Umrah but conquest. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: He said, 'I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'None shall pass the Miqat except in a state of Ihram.' He said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saying: 'None shall pass the Miqat without Ihram.' The generality of this hadith indicates that one who passes the Miqat to enter Makkah, whether he intends Hajj, Umrah, or trade, must enter Ihram in any case. Another proof is that entering Ihram is obligatory for the glorification of the land of the Haram, not because it is a condition for Hajj and Umrah. That is why those who live between the Miqat and the Haram must also enter Ihram. In any case, the obligation of Ihram is for the sanctity of the Haram.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute (ikhtilaf) between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school regarding the obligation of Ihram for an Aafaqi (a person living outside the Miqat boundaries) who wishes to enter Makkah for a purpose other than Hajj or Umrah. The Hanafi position, supported by Imam Ahmad, is that entering Ihram is wajib upon every Aafaqi who intends to enter Makkah, regardless of the purpose — even if it is for trade or any other worldly need. The Shafi'i position restricts this obligation to those intending Hajj or Umrah specifically. The author presents the Shafi'i proofs: (1) Ihram is legislated only for Hajj and Umrah, so it cannot be required for other actions; (2) The Prophet (SAW) entered Makkah without Ihram during the Conquest of Makkah, which was not for Hajj or Umrah. The Hanafi proofs are: (1) The general hadith of Ibn Abbas (RA): 'None shall pass the Miqat except in a state of Ihram' — this is an imperative (amr) indicating wujub, and it is general for all who intend to enter Makkah; (2) The very purpose of Ihram is to glorify the Sacred Land (Haram), and that glorification is independent of whether one intends Hajj or Umrah. The author also clarifies the rule from al-Inayah: if a person intends to pass only the outer Miqat (the Aafaqi Miqat) but not enter the Haram (e.g., going to Jeddah), then Ihram is not required; but if he intends to pass both boundaries and enter Makkah itself, Ihram is wajib.

Key Terms
آفاقی (āfāqī): A person who lives outside the Mawaqit (the five appointed Miqat boundaries).
میقات (miqāt): Plural: mawaqit. The geographical boundaries fixed by the Prophet (SAW) beyond which one cannot pass without Ihram when intending to enter Makkah.
وجوب (wujūb): Legal obligation (wajib) that is less than fard (pillar) but still sinful to leave.
بقعہ شریفہ (buq'ah sharīfah): The noble place, referring to the Haram of Makkah, whose sanctity necessitates Ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
According to the Hanafi school, the obligation of ihram for an Aafaqi entering Makkah is based on the sanctity of the Haram, not limited to pilgrimage, and is established by the general hadith of Ibn Abbas.
