Obligation of Ihram at the Miqat for the Afaqi: A Comparative Hanafi-Shafi'i Analysis
Hanafi ruling with inter-madhhab proof and rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ihram obligation for an Afaqi entering Makkah regardless of intention, explain the Hanafi proof from hadith, and refute the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concept of general applicability and the Prophet's special dispensation.

Core Idea
Ihram at the miqat is wajib for every entry into Makkah because the sanctity of the Haram demands it, not merely the intention of pilgrimage.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a key point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether an Afaqi entering Makkah for purposes other than Hajj or Umrah must still enter ihram. The Hanafi position, grounded in a general prophetic command, holds that ihram is wajib for anyone crossing the miqat into Makkah, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts the obligation to those intending pilgrimage. In this lesson, we will dissect the reasoning on both sides and understand why the Hanafi view is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the Hanafi ruling
The issue is whether ihram is obligatory for an Afaqi entering Makkah without intention of Hajj or Umrah. The Hanafi ruling is that it is wajib regardless of intention.
The ruling applies to any Afaqi who intends to enter Makkah from beyond the miqat.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'No one passes the miqat except in ihram.' The rationale is that ihram is for honoring the Haram, not merely as a ritual condition for Hajj/Umrah.
The hadith is general ('amm) and includes all purposes.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proofs
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that ihram is wajib only when intending Hajj or Umrah. His proofs: (1) ihram is legislated specifically for these rituals, and (2) the Prophet entered Makkah without ihram during the Conquest.
The Shafi'i view restricts the obligation to those with ritual intent.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proofs
The Hanafi response: the hadith is general and must be followed; the Prophet's entry during the Conquest was a special dispensation (khususiyyah) limited to that day, as per his own sermon.
The Prophet's action does not override the general command.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafi: a trader must enter ihram; Shafi'i: no ihram required. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.
This difference has real implications for Muslims traveling to Makkah for non-pilgrimage purposes.

جو مواقیت کے اندر رہنے والے ہیں ان کو سکی کہا جاتا ہے آفاقی لوگوں کے مواقیت تو وہ ہیں جو ہم نے گذشتہ صفحات میں ذکر کئے ہیں اور کی یعنی ان لوگوں کے میقات جو مواقیت اور حرم کے درمیان میں رہتے ہیں حل ہے یعنی حرم شروع ہونے سے پہلے پہلے احرام باندھ لیں۔ صاحب عنایہ کے بیان کے مطابق ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ جو شخص آفاقی اور مکی دونوں کے میقات سے آگے جانے کا ارادہ رکھتا ہو اس کے لئے بغیر احرام کے جانا جائز نہیں ہے اور جو شخص فقط ایک میقات یعنی آفاقی لوگوں کے میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کا ارادہ رکھتا ہو اور مکی کے میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کا ارادہ نہ ہو تو اس کو بغیر احرام کے جانا جائز ہے مثلا کوئی شخص جدہ یاصل میں کسی جگہ جانا چاہتا ہے تو اس پر احرام باندھنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ اتی ضابطہ کی روشنی میں صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی آفاقی شخص مکتہ المکرمہ جانے کے ارادہ سے میقات پر پہنچا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس پر احرام باندھنا واجب ہے خواہ اس کا ارادہ حج کا ہو یا عمرہ کا یا ان دونوں کے علاوہ تجارت وغیرہ کا یہی امام احمد کا مذہب ہے اور حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر حج یا عمرہ کے ارادہ سے مکہ جانے کا ارادہ ہو تو احرام باندھنا واجب ہے اور اگر ان کے علاوہ کا ارادہ ہو تو احرام واجب نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ احرام حج یا عمرہ دونوں میں سے ایک کے لئے مشروع ہوا ہے پس جب ان میں سے کسی ایک کی نیت کرے گا تو احرام لازم ہو گا ورنہ نہیں۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم فتح مکہ کے روز بغیر احرام کے داخل ہوئے تھے کیونکہ فتح مکہ کے موقع پر آپ کا ارادہ نہ حج کا تھا اور نہ عمرہ کا بلکہ مکہ کو فتح کرنے کا ارادہ تھا۔ ہماری دلیل ابن عباس کی حدیث ہے قَالَ سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ لَا يُجَاوِزُ الْمِيقَاتَ أَحَدُ الَّا مُحْرِماً فرمایا کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو کہتے ہوئے سنا ہے کہ کوئی شخص بغیر احرام کے میقات سے تجاوز نہ کرے اس حدیث کا اطلاق اس پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ میقات سے تجاوز کر کے مکتہ المکرمہ جانے والا خواہ حج یا عمرہ کا ارادہ کرے یا تجارت وغیرہ کسی اور چیز کا ارادہ کرے بہر صورت اس پر احترام واجب ہے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ احرام باندھنا سرزمین حرم کی تعظیم کے پیش نظر واجب ہوا ہے نہ کہ حج اور عمرہ کی شرط ہونے کی وجہ سے یہی وجہ ہے کہ جو لوگ میقات اور حرم کے درمیان میں رہتے ہیں ان پر بھی احرام باندھنا واجب ہے بہر حال احترام کا وجوب حریم کی سرزمین کے معظم اور مکرم ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے اور تعظیم میں سب برابر ہے برابر ہیں یعنی تعظیم حرم سب پر واجب ہے خواہ وہ حج کا ارادہ رکھتا ہو یا عمرہ کا یا ان دونوں کے علاوہ تجارت وغیرہ کا۔ اور امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث فتح مکہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ فتح مکہ کے موقع پر بغیر احرام کے مکتہ المکرمہ میں داخل ہونا آپ کی خصوصیات میں سے ہے اور یہ خصوصیت بھی صرف تھوڑی دیر کے لئے تھی جیسا کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فتح مکہ کے دن اپنے خطبہ میں فرمایا ت إِنَّ مَكَّةَ حَرَامٌ حَرَّمَهَا اللَّهُ تَعَالَى يَوْمَ خَلَقَ السَّمواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَأَنهَا لَم تَحِلُّ لِأَحَدٍ قَبْلِي وَ لَا تَحِلُّ لِأَحَدٍ بَعْدِى وَإِنَّمَا أُحِلَّتْ لِى سَاعَةَ مِنْ نَهَارٍ ثُمَّ عَادَتْ حَرَاماً إلى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ یعنی تک محترم ہے اللہ تعالیٰ نے زمین و آسمان کی تخلیق کے دن ہی محترمہ بنادیا تھا نہ مجھ سے پہلے کسی کے لئے حلال ہے اور نہ مجھ سے بعد حلال ہے میرے لئے دن کی ایک ساعت کے لئے حلال کیا گیا تھا پھر اس کی حرمت قیامت تک کے لئے لوٹ آئی یعنی اب اگر میں بھی مکہ میں داخل ہوں تو میرے لئے بھی احرام باندھنا ضروری ہے۔
Then the Afaqi, when he reaches it (the miqat) intending to enter Makkah, must enter ihram whether he intends Hajj or Umrah or does not intend, according to us, because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'No one may pass the miqat except in ihram.' And because the obligation of ihram is to honor this noble land, so the Hajj pilgrim, the Umrah performer, and others are equal in this. Translation: Then an Afaqi person, when he reaches the miqat with the intention of entering Makkah, according to us it is wajib upon him to tie ihram, whether he intends Hajj or Umrah or does not intend anything, because the Prophet said: 'No one may pass the miqat except by tying ihram,' because the obligation of ihram is for the glorification of this noble place, so in this, the one intending Hajj, Umrah, or others are all equal. Commentary: Afaqi refers to those who live outside the miqat, and those who live inside the miqat are called 'saki'. The miqat for Afaqi are those we mentioned in previous pages, and the miqat for those who live between the miqat and the Haram is 'hill', i.e., they should tie ihram before the Haram begins. According to the author of al-'Inayah, the rule is: one who intends to pass both the miqat of the Afaqi and the miqat of the Makkan (i.e., the boundaries of the Haram) cannot go without ihram; but one who intends only to pass the Afaqi's miqat but not the Makkan's miqat, it is permissible to go without ihram. For example, if someone wishes to go to Jeddah, tying ihram is not wajib upon him. In light of this rule, the case is: if an Afaqi person reaches the miqat intending to go to Makkah, according to us it is wajib upon him to tie ihram, whether his intention is Hajj, Umrah, or trade, etc. This is also the madhhab of Imam Ahmad. Imam al-Shafi'i said: If he intends Hajj or Umrah, then ihram is wajib; if he intends other than these, ihram is not wajib. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that ihram is legislated for either Hajj or Umrah, so when he intends one of them, ihram becomes obligatory, otherwise not. His second proof is that the Messenger entered Makkah without ihram on the day of the Conquest, because his intention was not Hajj or Umrah but to conquer Makkah. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saying: No one passes the miqat except in ihram.' The generality of this hadith indicates that whoever passes the miqat to go to Makkah, whether he intends Hajj, Umrah, trade, or anything else, in any case ihram is wajib upon him. The second proof is that tying ihram is wajib out of respect for the land of the Haram, not because it is a condition for Hajj and Umrah. This is also why those who live between the miqat and the Haram must also tie ihram. In any case, the obligation of ihram is due to the nobility and sanctity of the land of the Haram, and all are equal in this respect: glorification of the Haram is wajib upon all, whether they intend Hajj, Umrah, or trade, etc. The response to the hadith of the Conquest presented by Imam al-Shafi'i is that entering Makkah without ihram on the occasion of the Conquest was one of the special characteristics of the Prophet, and this characteristic was only for a short time, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said in his sermon on the day of the Conquest: 'Indeed, Makkah is sacred; Allah made it sacred the day He created the heavens and the earth. It was not permitted for anyone before me, nor will it be permitted for anyone after me. It was only permitted for me for a part of a day, then its sanctity returned until the Day of Resurrection.' That is, it is sacred; Allah made it sacred on the day of creation of the heavens and earth. It was not permitted for anyone before me nor after me. It was permitted for me for one hour of a day, then its sanctity returned until the Day of Resurrection. Meaning, even if I enter Makkah now, it is necessary for me to tie ihram.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of ihram for an Afaqi upon reaching the miqat, along with a refutation of the Shafi'i position. The author begins by stating the ruling: an Afaqi who reaches the miqat intending to enter Makkah must enter ihram, whether his intention is Hajj, Umrah, or any other purpose. This is the Hanafi position. The proof is given: the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) 'No one may pass the miqat except in ihram,' and the rational reason that ihram is wajib due to the sanctity of the Haram, not merely as a condition for Hajj/Umrah. The commentary explains the definition of Afaqi and those inside the miqat, and clarifies the rule with examples. Then the Shafi'i position is presented: ihram is wajib only if intending Hajj or Umrah, otherwise not. Their proofs are that ihram is legislated specifically for these rituals and the Prophet's entry during the Conquest without ihram. The Hanafi response follows: the hadith is general and includes all intentions; the Prophet's entry was a special dispensation (khususiyyah) limited to that day, as per his own sermon. The Hanafi position is thus relied upon.

Key Terms
آفاقی (afaagi): One who resides outside the miqat boundaries.
میقات (mee’qat): The designated boundary from which pilgrims must enter ihram.
احرام (ihram): The state of intention and restriction for entering the Haram for pilgrimage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is ihram wajib for an Afaqi entering Makkah regardless of intention?
A) Because the Prophet entered Makkah during the Conquest without ihram.
B) Because ihram is a condition for Hajj and Umrah only.
C) Because the obligation of ihram is due to the sanctity of the Haram, not limited to rituals.
D) Because the Afaqi is required to perform Hajj every year.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates ihram upon any Afaqi crossing the miqat into Makkah, based on the generality of the hadith and the principle of honoring the Haram, regardless of the purpose of entry.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Permissibility for Residents Inside the Miqat to Enter Makkah Without Ihram
Ruling with rational proof (istihsan) and analogue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a person inside the miqat may enter Makkah without ihram for a need, explain the basis of istihsan due to hardship (haraj), and distinguish the exceptional case when Hajj or Umrah is intended.

Core Idea
Those inside the miqat may enter Makkah without ihram for frequent needs due to removal of hardship.

This lesson examines a specific relaxation in Hajj/Umrah rulings: a person whose residence or location lies inside the miqat but outside Makkah is permitted to enter Makkah without ihram for daily or frequent needs. The ruling is rooted in the principle of removing hardship (rafʿ al-ḥaraj) and analogizes such a person to the residents of Makkah themselves. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the scope of ihram obligations and the role of necessity in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling
Read the opening phrase: 'Whoever is inside the miqat... may enter Makkah without ihram for his need.' The subject is dākhil al-mīqāt, and the ruling is permissibility (ibāḥa) for entry without ihram for a need.
The ruling applies only when the entry is for a need, not for the express purpose of performing Hajj or Umrah.
2
Understand the proof: istihsan based on hardship
The text gives the ratio: 'because his entry into Makkah is frequent, and requiring ihram every time would be clear hardship (ḥaraj).' This is an istihsān argument that overrides the general principle of requiring ihram.
Ḥaraj is a fundamental concept in Hanafi fiqh; Allah has removed hardship from the religion (Qur'an 22:78).
3
Trace the analogy to the people of Makkah
The passage states 'so he becomes like the people of Makkah' – analogous ruling is already established for Makkans: they may leave and re-enter without ihram for their needs.
This is a qiyās shabah (analogy based on similarity) where the effective cause is the frequency of need and the removal of hardship.
4
Differentiate the exception for intentional ritual
The exception is stated: 'unlike when he intends to perform a ritual' (i.e., Hajj or Umrah). In that case, ihram is wajib because the intention is occasional and does not cause hardship.
The key distinction is the purpose of the journey: need vs. worship.

كَاهْلِ مَكَّةَ حَيْثُ يُبَاحُ لَهُمُ الْحُرُوجُ مِنْهَا ثُمَّ دُخُولُهَا بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامِ لِحَاجَتِهِم بِخَلافِ مَا إذَا قَصَدَ اَدَاءَ النَّسُكِ لِأَنَّهُ يَتَحَقَّقُ أَحْيَانًا فَلَا حَرَج ترجمہ نکلنا اور مکہ میں بغیر احرام کے داخل ہو نا مباح اور جائز ہے پس اسی طرح میقات کے اندر رہنے والوں کے لئے بھی مکہ میں آمد و رفت بغیر احرام کے جائز تے لیکن اگر کوئی میقات کا رہنے والا ادائے حج یا ادائے عمرہ کے ارادہ سے مکہ میں جانا چاہے تو اس کو احرام باندھنا واجب ہے کیونکہ اس ارادہ سے جانا تو کبھی کبھی ہوتا ہے اور کبھی کبھی احرام باندھنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اس لئے اس ارادہ سے داخل مکہ ہونے والے کے لئے احترام باندھنا واجب قرار دیا گیا ہے صاحب عنایہ نے تحریر کیا ہے کہ اصل یہ ہے کہ لکڑی چن کر لانے والوں کے لئے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے
And whoever is inside the miqat, he may enter Makkah without ihram for his need, because his entry into Makkah is frequent, and requiring ihram every time would be clear hardship. So he becomes like the people of Makkah, for whom it is permissible to leave Makkah and then enter without ihram for their needs. Unlike the case when he intends to perform a ritual, because that happens only occasionally, so there is no hardship. Translation: And a person who is inside the miqat, it is permissible for him to enter Makkah without ihram for some need, because his entry into Makkah is frequent, and requiring ihram every time would be clear hardship. So he becomes like the residents of Makkah, for whom it is permissible to leave Makkah and then enter without ihram for their needs. Contrary to the case when he intends to perform Hajj or Umrah, because that intention occurs only occasionally, so there is no hardship. Commentary: The issue is that a person who is inside the miqat, whether he is a resident or present there in any way, if he wishes to go to Makkah for a need, he is permitted to enter without ihram. Because although belief in the sanctity of the Haram is wajib upon him, its expression through ihram is waived due to the frequency of entry. Frequent entry to Makkah for human needs and worldly necessities may necessitate many trips, and if ihram were required each time, it would be a clear hardship, whereas Allah has removed hardship from His servants. So the resident inside the miqat is like the residents of Makkah, for whom it is permissible to leave and enter without ihram for their needs. Similarly, for those inside the miqat, entering Makkah without ihram is permissible. However, if a resident of the miqat intends to perform Hajj or Umrah, then ihram is wajib upon him, because such intention occurs only occasionally, and tying ihram occasionally does not involve hardship. The author of al-'Inayah wrote that the principle is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave an exemption for wood gatherers...
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that a person who is inside the miqat (i.e., residing between the miqat and the Haram) may enter Makkah without ihram for a need. The proof is based on istihsan due to hardship (haraj): if ihram were required every time such a person entered Makkah for frequent needs, it would cause severe difficulty. Therefore, such a person is treated like the residents of Makkah, who are permitted to leave and enter without ihram for their needs. However, if the intention is to perform Hajj or Umrah, ihram becomes wajib, because that is an occasional act and does not create hardship. The commentary expands on this, citing the Quranic principle of removing hardship, and compares to the people of Makkah. The passage ends with a reference to the author of al-'Inayah about wood gatherers, but the text is cut off.

Key Terms
داخل الميقات (dākhil al-mīqāt): One who resides between the miqat and the Haram (i.e., within the miqat boundaries but not in Makkah itself).
حرج (ḥaraj): Hardship or difficulty that the law seeks to avoid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what is the basis for allowing a person inside the miqat to enter Makkah without ihram for a need?
A) Explicit hadith
B) General principle of permissibility
C) Removal of hardship (raf' al-ḥaraj)
D) Consensus of the companions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts those inside the miqat from tying ihram for frequent, need-based entries into Makkah, applying the principle of removing hardship (rafʿ al-ḥaraj) and analogizing them to the people of Makkah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Entering Makkah without Ihram for Miqat Residents: Hanafi Ruling
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on miqat residents entering Makkah without ihram for non-ritual needs, explain the madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school, and apply the principle of hardship removal.

Core Idea
Frequent entry to Makkah without ihram is allowed for miqat residents to avoid hardship.

The Haram of Makkah is sacred and entering it in a state of ihram is generally required for Hajj and Umrah. However, for those who reside within the miqat boundaries, frequent visits for daily needs would cause undue hardship if ihram were required every time. The Hanafi school, based on istihsan and the Qur'anic principle of removing hardship, permits such entry without ihram. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the counterargument from the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the passage to determine what act is being ruled upon and for whom. Note the key phrase: 'man kana dakhila al-miqat lahu an yadkhula Makkata bighayri al-ihram li-hajatihi.'
The ruling applies to anyone physically inside the miqat, not just residents.
2
Understand the basis: hardship (haraj) and istihsan
The passage argues that frequent entry makes ihram burdensome. Identify the Qur'anic principle cited: 'ma ja'ala Allahu alaykum min haraj.' This justifies the dispensation.
This is a classic Hanafi use of istihsan over strict qiyas.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school cites the Prophet's entry without ihram at the Conquest. The Hanafi response clarifies that this was a special dispensation for the Prophet alone, quoting the hadith 'innama uhillat li sa'atan min nihar.'
The Hanafi response does not reject the hadith but limits its application.
4
Note the exception: intention for Hajj/Umrah
The permissibility does not apply when one intends to perform Hajj or Umrah. In that case, ihram is obligatory because it is occasional, not burdensome.
This exception preserves the general rule that Hajj and Umrah require ihram.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Consider a resident of Jeddah (inside the miqat) who needs to go to Makkah for work daily. Under Hanafi fiqh, he may enter without ihram each time, but if he intends Umrah, he must wear ihram.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between schools.

کتاب الحج سرزمین کے معظم اور مکرم ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے اور تعظیم میں سب برابر ہے برابر ہیں یعنی تعظیم حرم سب پر واجب ہے خواہ وہ حج کا ارادہ رکھتا ہو یا عمرہ کا یا ان دونوں کے علاوہ تجارت وغیرہ کا۔ اور امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث فتح مکہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ فتح مکہ کے موقع پر بغیر احرام کے مکہ میں داخل ہونا آپ کی خصوصیات میں سے ہے اور یہ خصوصیت بھی صرف تھوڑی دیر کے لئے تھی جیسا کہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فتح مکہ کے دن اپنے خطبہ میں فرمایا إِنَّ مَكَّةَ حَرَامٌ حَرَّمَهَا اللَّهُ تَعَالَى يَوْمَ خَلَقَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَإِنَّهَا لَمْ تَحِلَّ لِأَحَدٍ قَبْلِي وَلَا تَحِلُّ لِأَحَدٍ بَعْدِي وَإِنَّمَا أُحِلَّتْ لِي سَاعَةً مِنْ نَهَارٍ ثُمَّ عَادَتْ حَرَامًا إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ یعنی تک محترم ہے اللہ تعالیٰ نے زمین و آسمان کی تخلیق کے دن ہی محترمہ بنا دیا تھا نہ مجھ سے پہلے کسی کے لئے حلال ہے اور نہ مجھ سے بعد حلال ہے میرے لئے دن کی ایک ساعت کے لئے حلال کیا گیا تھا پھر اس کی حرمت قیامت تک کے لئے لوٹ آئی یعنی اب اگر میں بھی مکہ میں داخل ہوں تو میرے لئے بھی احرام باندھنا ضروری ہے۔
وَمَنْ كَانَ دَاخِلَ الْمِيقَاتِ لَهُ أَنْ يَدْخُلَ مَكَّةَ بِغَيْرِ الْإِحْرَامِ لِحَاجَتِهِ لِأَنَّهُ يَكْثُرُ دُخُولُهُ مَكَّةَ وَفِي إِيجَابِ الْإِحْرَامِ فِي كُلِّ مَرَّةٍ حَرَجٌ بَيِّنٌ فَصَارَ كَأَهْلِ مَكَّةَ حَيْثُ يُبَاحُ لَهُمُ الْخُرُوجُ مِنْهَا ثُمَّ دُخُولُهَا بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامٍ لِحَاجَتِهِمْ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَصَدَ أَدَاءَ النُّسُكِ لِأَنَّهُ يَتَحَقَّقُ أَحْيَانًا فَلَا حَرَجَ۔
ترجمہ اور جوشخص میقات کے اندر ہو اس کے لئے اپنی کسی ضرورت سے بغیر احرام کے مکہ میں داخل ہونا جائز ہے کیونکہ مکہ میں اس کا دخول بکثرت واقع ہوتا ہے اور ہر مرتبہ احرام واجب کرنے میں کھلا ہوا حرج ہے پس یہ شخص اہل مکہ کے مانند ہو گیا چنانچہ اہل مکہ کے لئے مکہ سے نکلنا پھر مکہ میں اپنی ضرورتوں سے بغیر احرام کے داخل ہونا مباح ہے برخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ حج ادا کرنے کا ارادہ کیا ہو کیونکہ یہ ارادہ تو کبھی کبھی متحقق ہوتا ہے تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جو شخص میقات کے اندر ہو خواہ وہاں کا رہنے والا ہو خواہ کسی طور سے وہاں موجود ہو۔ اگر یہ شخص کسی ضرورت سے مکہ جا چاہے تو اس کو بغیر احرام کے داخل ہونے کی اجازت ہے کیونکہ حرم کی تعظیم اگر چہ اس پر اعتقاد واجب ہے لیکن اس کا اظہار بطریق احرام اٹھا لیا گیا ہے اس لئے کہ حاجات انسانی اور ضروریات دنیاوی کو پورا کرنے کے لئے مکہ میں شخص بکثرت داخل ہوگا اور دن میں کئی کئی بار آمد و رفت ہوسکتی ہے پس اگر اس شخص پر ہر بار مکہ میں داخل ہونے کے لئے احرام باندھنا واجب کر دیا گیا تو یہ کھلے حرج میں مبتلا ہوگا حالانکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے اپنے بندوں سے حرج کو دور کیا ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے مَا جَعَلَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْكُمْ مِنْ حَرَجٍ۔ میقات کے اندر کا رہنے والا باشندگان مکہ کے مانند ہو گیا اور باشندگان مکہ کے لئے اپنی ضروریات کے واسطے مکہ سے نکلنا اور مکہ میں بغیر احرام کے داخل ہونا مباح اور جائز ہے پس اسی طرح میقات کے اندر رہنے والوں کے لئے بھی مکہ میں آمد و رفت بغیر احرام کے جائز ہے لیکن اگر کوئی میقات کا رہنے والا ادائے حج یا ادائے عمرہ کے ارادہ سے مکہ میں جانا چاہے تو اس کو احرام باندھنا واجب ہے کیونکہ اس ارادہ سے جانا تو کبھی کبھی ہوتا ہے اور کبھی کبھی احرام باندھنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اس لئے اس ارادہ سے داخل مکہ ہونے والے کے لئے احرام باندھنا واجب قرار دیا گیا ہے صاحب عنایہ نے تحریر کیا ہے کہ اصل یہ ہے کہ لکڑی چن کر لانے والوں کے لئے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے بغیر احرام کے مکہ میں داخل ہونے کی اجازت دی ہے اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے مکہ اور میقات کے اندر رہنے والوں کے لئے اپنی ضرورتوں کے پیش نظر بغیر احرام کے مکہ میں داخل ہونے کی اجازت ہے۔
The Book of Hajj: [The ruling] is because the land is honored and revered, and in reverence all are equal—meaning reverence of the Haram is obligatory upon all, whether one intends Hajj, Umrah, or besides these, trade, etc. And the answer to the hadith of the Conquest of Makkah presented by Imam al-Shafi'i is that entering Makkah without ihram at the time of the Conquest was among his (the Prophet's) special characteristics, and this characteristic was only for a short time, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said in his sermon on the day of the Conquest: 'Indeed Makkah is sacred, Allah made it sacred the day He created the heavens and the earth; it has not been permissible for anyone before me, nor will it be permissible for anyone after me; it was only made permissible for me for a portion of a day, then it returned to sacredness until the Day of Judgment.' Meaning it is sacred. Allah made it sacred on the day of creating the earth and heavens. It was not lawful for anyone before me, nor will it be lawful after me. It was made lawful for me for one hour of the day, then its sanctity returned until the Day of Judgment. That is, if I now enter Makkah, it is necessary for me to wear ihram. And for one who is inside the miqat, he may enter Makkah without ihram for his need, because his entry into Makkah is frequent, and requiring ihram every time involves clear hardship. So he becomes like the people of Makkah, for whom it is permissible to leave Makkah then enter it without ihram for their needs. Unlike when one intends to perform a ritual (Hajj/Umrah), because that intention occurs only occasionally, so there is no hardship. Translation: And whoever is inside the miqat, it is permissible for him to enter Makkah without ihram for his need, because his entry into Makkah occurs frequently, and in requiring ihram every time there is clear hardship. So this person becomes like the inhabitants of Makkah, for whom it is permitted to leave Makkah and then enter it without ihram for their needs. Contrary to the case when he intends to perform Hajj, because that intention occurs only occasionally, so there is no hardship. Explanation: The matter is that whoever is inside the miqat, whether a resident or present there in any way. If this person wants to go to Makkah for some need, he is permitted to enter without ihram because, although reverence of the Haram is obligatory upon him in belief, its manifestation through ihram is waived because for fulfilling human needs and worldly necessities, a person enters Makkah frequently and may come and go many times a day. So if ihram were required every time he enters Makkah, he would be in clear hardship, whereas Allah has removed hardship from His servants, as He says: 'Allah has not placed upon you any hardship in religion.' The resident inside the miqat becomes like the inhabitants of Makkah, and for the inhabitants of Makkah it is permissible to leave Makkah and enter it without ihram for their needs. Thus, similarly, for those residing inside the miqat, entering Makkah without ihram is permissible. However, if a resident of the miqat intends to perform Hajj or Umrah, then it is obligatory upon him to wear ihram because going with that intention occurs only occasionally, and occasional ihram involves no hardship. Therefore, for one entering Makkah with that intention, ihram is obligatory. The author of al-‘Inayah wrote that the origin is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) permitted wood gatherers to enter Makkah without ihram. This indicates that for residents of Makkah and the miqat area, entering Makkah for their needs without ihram is permitted.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling with proof on the permissibility for residents inside the miqat (the boundary for ihram) to enter Makkah without ihram for their daily needs. The author first addresses the objection of Imam al-Shafi'i who cites the hadith of the Conquest of Makkah where the Prophet (PBUH) entered Makkah without ihram. The Hanafi response clarifies that this was a special dispensation for the Prophet alone, limited to a few hours on that day, as stated in the authentic hadith. Therefore, it does not set a general precedent. After refuting the opposing view, the ruling is presented: Anyone who is inside the miqat—whether a resident or temporarily present—may enter Makkah without ihram for any need (e.g., trade, visiting family) because frequent entry would otherwise cause undue hardship (haraj). The reasoning is based on istihsan: the Qur'anic principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj) and qiyas to the people of Makkah, who are permitted to leave and re-enter without ihram for their needs. However, this dispensation does not apply when one intends to perform Hajj or Umrah, because that is a rare occasion and does not create hardship. The passage further explains that the reverence of the Haram is fulfilled through belief and respect, not necessarily by wearing ihram on every visit. The commentary from al-'Inayah adds that the Prophet himself allowed wood gatherers to enter without ihram, reinforcing the ruling.

Key Terms
الميقات (al-mīqāt): The specific boundary set for entering ihram for Hajj or Umrah, beyond which those coming from outside must wear ihram. Those inside it have different rules.
الإحرام (al-iḥrām): The state of consecration for Hajj/Umrah, marked by wearing specific garments and abstaining from certain prohibitions.
الحرج (al-ḥaraj): Undue hardship or difficulty that is removed by Islamic law (raf' al-haraj).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following best describes the ruling for a person who lives inside the miqat and wants to enter Makkah to buy groceries?
A) He must wear ihram every time he enters Makkah.
B) He may enter without ihram because frequent entry would cause hardship.
C) He may never enter Makkah without ihram regardless of his residence.
D) He must perform a full Hajj first before entering without ihram.

Key Takeaway
Miqat residents may enter Makkah without ihram for daily needs due to hardship, but must wear ihram when intending Hajj or Umrah.
